COMPLETE PROFESSIONAL SOFTWARE ARCHITECTURE PROMPT SYSTEM

WHAT WE'RE BUILDING:

A master prompt system you copy-paste into any AI agent (Lovable, Replit, Bolt)

to scaffold any SaaS web or mobile app — from quick MVPs to production-grade platforms.

HOW TO USE: Run one section prompt per session. Pass each section's output as

context into the next section prompt. Use [TRACK] and [CONDITIONAL] flags to

skip sections that don't apply to your app.

THE SYSTEM STRUCTURE:

TWO TRACKS

FAST TRACK → MVPs, quick builds (\~20 sections, 1-2 hrs)

FULL TRACK → Production, client work (\~45-55 sections, 1 day)

Same prompts. You just skip conditionals on Fast Track.

THREE LAYERS

LAYER 1 → Universal Core (every app uses this)

LAYER 2 → Platform-specific (Web / Mobile)

LAYER 3 → App-type specific (E-commerce / AI / Social etc.)

LAYER 1 --- 32 SECTIONS (UNIVERSAL CORE — every SaaS app uses this):

FOUNDATION

01. Product & Business Foundation

02. Functional Requirements & Scope

03. Non-Functional Requirements

04. Capacity Planning & Cost

SYSTEM ARCHITECTURE

05. High-Level Architecture

06. Authentication & Authorization

07. Database & Data Modeling

08. API Design

09. Real-Time Architecture [conditional]

12. Third-Party Integrations Map

13. Async Processing & Messaging [conditional]

DESIGN & FRONTEND

14. UI/UX & Design System

16. Rate Limiting, Throttling & Resource Governance

17. Data Integrity & Transaction Boundaries

EACH PROMPT FOLLOWS THIS STRUCTURE:

[TRACK] → Fast Track / Full Track / Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Yes/No --- skip condition if No

[PURPOSE] → Why this section exists

[PROMPT] → The actual prompt

[AGENT HINT] → What the AI agent should do with this output

Prompts

GLOBAL AGENT EXECUTION PROTOCOL

READ THIS ONCE — APPLIES TO EVERY SECTION IN THIS DOCUMENT

WHAT THIS IS:

This protocol governs how any AI agent — Cursor, Claude Code,

Lovable, Bolt, Replit, GPT, Gemini, or any future agent —

must behave when executing any section prompt in this document.

You do not need to repeat these rules in each section.

Read this once. Apply it everywhere.

RULE 1 — BEFORE YOU START ANY SECTION

Always check these three things before generating anything:

1. PROJECT_CONTEXT.md

Read it fully. Every decision already made lives here.

Never contradict it. If you do not have it, ask for it.

2. Blank fields (marked ___)

A blank field means the user has not decided yet.

Do NOT assume. Do NOT skip. Ask the user to fill it in first.

One blank in a critical field (auth model, DB engine, multi-tenancy)

can make everything you generate wrong.

3. Conflict check

Before writing a single line of code, scan the section for

any decision that contradicts PROJECT_CONTEXT.md or a

previous section's output.

If you find a conflict — STOP. Flag it. Wait for resolution.

Never generate code on top of a known conflict.

RULE 2 — HOW TO READ A SECTION PROMPT

Every section in this document has the same structure:

[TRACK]       → tells you Fast Track / Full Track / Both

Skip this section if it does not match user's track.

[CONDITIONAL] → tells you when to skip this section entirely.

If the skip condition applies — stop, tell the user

this section is not needed, move to the next.

[PURPOSE]     → explains WHY this section exists.

Read it. It tells you the intent behind every decision.

Do not generate output that violates the purpose.

The body of the section → the questions the user fills in.

These are your INPUTS. Every filled answer is a spec.

Treat them as requirements, not suggestions.

[AGENT HINT]  → your OUTPUT instructions.

This tells you exactly what to generate for this section.

Do not generate things not listed here.

Do not skip things that are listed here.

RULE 3 — HOW TO GENERATE OUTPUT

FORMAT — always follow this structure for every output:

┌─────────────────────────────────────┐

│ SECTION [N] — [NAME] — EXECUTING    │

└─────────────────────────────────────┘

CONFLICT CHECK: [none found / list any found]

GENERATING:

→ [file path or component name]

[code block]

→ [file path or component name]

[code block]

COMMANDS TO RUN:

[install / migration / seed commands if applicable]

SECTION COMPLETE.

Add to PROJECT_CONTEXT.md:

- [key decision 1]

- [key decision 2]

- [key decision 3]

FILE NAMING:

- Show full file path before every code block

- Example: src/middleware/auth.ts — not just auth.ts

- One file per responsibility — do not combine unrelated logic

CODE QUALITY — non-negotiable:

- Use the language and framework in PROJECT_CONTEXT.md

- Follow the naming conventions already established

- No placeholder comments like "// TODO: implement this"

- No hardcoded secrets, URLs, or environment-specific values

- Every file must be complete and runnable — no partial outputs

RULE 4 — THE 10 UNIVERSAL CONSTRAINTS

These apply to every single section, no exceptions:

1. NEVER contradict a decision owned by a previous section.

Check the Ownership Table in the Master Prompt.

If §06 owns the auth model — §15 references it, never redefines it.

2. NEVER generate code for a section marked [FULL ONLY]

if the user is on Fast Track.

Ask before proceeding if you are unsure of their track.

3. NEVER skip a section marked [BOTH TRACKS] without

explicit instruction from the user.

4. NEVER store secrets, API keys, or passwords in code.

Always use environment variables.

Always reference the .env.example pattern from §26.

5. NEVER use a different DB engine, auth method, or API style

than what was decided in §05, §06, §07, §08.

Those are locked decisions. They do not change per section.

6. NEVER generate frontend code that bypasses backend validation.

Every client-side check must have a server-side equivalent.

7. NEVER collapse 401 (unauthenticated) and 403 (unauthorized).

They are different errors. Always keep them distinct.

8. NEVER store PII in logs, analytics events, or error messages.

Check §19 classification table before touching user data.

9. NEVER generate a migration that drops a column or table

in a single deploy step.

Always use expand-contract pattern (§32 schema evolution rules).

10. NEVER end a section with partial output.

If context window is running out — say so.

Ask the user to start a new session and continue.

Never silently cut off.

RULE 5 — CONTEXT WINDOW MANAGEMENT

This is critical. Every agent has a context limit.

These rules prevent silent failures.

At the START of each session:

→ Paste the PROJECT_CONTEXT.md block

→ Paste the filled section prompt

→ Nothing else unless the section specifically references

output from a previous section

If context is getting full (you feel the session slowing down

or outputs getting shorter):

→ STOP before starting a new file

→ Tell the user: "Context window filling. Start new session.

Paste PROJECT_CONTEXT.md + this section + the last file

I generated, then say CONTINUE."

Never let context overflow silently.

A silent overflow = corrupted output = wasted work.

RULE 6 — PROJECT_CONTEXT.md — THE SINGLE SOURCE OF TRUTH

This file is the memory of the entire project across all sessions.

It must be updated after every section.

MINIMUM required fields in PROJECT_CONTEXT.md:

# PROJECT CONTEXT

App name:

App type:

Platform: (web / mobile / both)

Track: (Fast / Full)

## Stack

Language:

Framework:

DB engine:

Cache:

Auth model:

API style:

Hosting:

## Key Decisions

Multi-tenant: (yes / no — model: ___)

Auth tokens: (JWT / session / opaque)

State management: (name)

CSS / styling: (name)

Queue system: (name or none)

Search engine: (name or none)

File storage: (name or none)

## Scale

Target users:

Target RPS:

SLO uptime:

## Compliance

Requirements: (none / GDPR / HIPAA / PCI / SOC2)

## Completed Sections

§01: [date] — [one-line summary of key output]

§02: [date] — [one-line summary]

... (add each section as you complete it)

## Active Constraints

(Any non-standard decisions or overrides the agent must know)

The agent must READ this file at the start of every session.

The agent must TELL the user what to add after every section.

The user must UPDATE it before starting the next section.

RULE 7 — HOW TO HANDLE ERRORS & GAPS

If a required field is blank:

→ List every blank field at the top

→ Do not proceed until the user fills them

→ Example: "Cannot generate auth system — auth model is blank.

Please specify: JWT / session-based / opaque token"

If you find a contradiction between sections:

→ Name both sections and the exact conflict

→ State which section OWNS the decision (Ownership Table)

→ Do not generate code until resolved

→ Example: "Conflict: §06 says JWT stateless, but §07

has a sessions table. §06 owns auth model.

Do you want to remove the sessions table or switch to

stateful sessions?"

If a section is marked [CONDITIONAL] and the condition is not met:

→ Tell the user: "§09 Real-Time is conditional.

Your app does not have real-time features declared in §01.

Skip this section? (yes / no)"

If you are unsure about something:

→ Ask one specific question

→ Do not ask multiple questions at once

→ Do not assume and proceed silently

RULE 8 — AGENT-SPECIFIC NOTES

These are optimizations per agent — same rules, better execution:

CURSOR:

→ Use @PROJECT_CONTEXT.md to reference the context file

→ Use Composer (Cmd+I) for multi-file section outputs

→ Use Chat for single-file or question sections (§01-§04)

→ Tag existing files with @ when a section modifies them

Example: @auth.ts when running §18 Security

CLAUDE CODE:

→ Save PROJECT_CONTEXT.md in repo root before starting

→ Run sections from the project root directory

→ Use: claude "execute §06 using PROJECT_CONTEXT.md: [paste section]"

→ Claude Code can run migrations and installs directly — let it

LOVABLE / BOLT:

→ These are UI-first — run §14 and §15 before §05-§08

to get the visual scaffold first, then add backend logic

→ Paste one section at a time into the chat

→ Download and save code after each section before continuing

REPLIT:

→ Use the AI tab for section execution

→ Keep PROJECT_CONTEXT.md as a pinned file in the workspace

→ Replit handles installs automatically — trust the [AGENT HINT] commands

GPT / GEMINI / OTHER:

→ Paste PROJECT_CONTEXT.md as the first message in every new chat

→ Then paste the filled section prompt

→ These agents do not have file access — you must paste context manually

QUICK REFERENCE — WHAT TO DO EACH SESSION

START:   Paste PROJECT_CONTEXT.md + filled section prompt

CHECK:   Blanks? Conflicts? Track match? Conditional skip?

EXECUTE: Generate output per [AGENT HINT]

END:     Tell user what to add to PROJECT_CONTEXT.md

NEXT:    User updates context, opens new session, repeats

MASTER STITCHING PROMPT

THE COMMAND CENTER FOR THE ENTIRE SYSTEM

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No — always run this FIRST, before any section

[PURPOSE]     → This is the starting prompt for every project.

Run it once at the beginning. It sets your track,

identifies which sections to run, in what order,

what to skip, and how to pass context between sections.

It is the blueprint for using the entire system.

WHAT YOU ARE BUILDING

I am building a [type] SaaS application.

Brief description: ___

Platform: (web only / mobile only / web + mobile)

Target users: ___

Core problem solved: ___

Monetization model: (freemium / subscription / usage-based / one-time / marketplace)

Team size: ___

Timeline: (MVP in ___ weeks / production in ___ months)

Budget type: (bootstrapped / funded / enterprise)

Compliance requirements: (none / GDPR / HIPAA / PCI / SOC2 / other)

STEP 1 — CHOOSE YOUR TRACK

Read the descriptions below and decide which track applies.

You can change tracks at any point.

FAST TRACK   → MVP / Quick Build

Use when:

- Timeline is under 4 weeks

- Team is 1-3 people

- No compliance requirements (HIPAA / PCI / SOC2)

- No external API customers (no public API)

- Goal is to validate an idea, not scale it

- Budget is bootstrapped

Fast Track runs ~20 sections.

You skip [CONDITIONAL] sections unless your app specifically needs them.

You skip all Full Track-only sections.

Estimated time: 1–3 hours total.

FULL TRACK   → Production / Client Work

Use when:

- Timeline is 4+ weeks

- Team is 3+ people

- Any compliance requirement exists

- You have paying customers or external API consumers

- The app needs to scale beyond 10k users

- It's client work or a funded startup

Full Track runs all 32 sections.

Estimated time: 1 full working day.

MY TRACK: (Fast Track / Full Track)

STEP 2 — CHOOSE YOUR LAYER COMBINATION

Every app runs Layer 1 (32 sections).

Then pick which additional layers apply.

LAYER 1 → Always (32 sections — Universal Core)

Run for every app, web or mobile, MVP or production.

LAYER 2A → Web-Specific (8 sections — W1 to W8)

Run when your app has a web frontend.

Covers: SEO, Core Web Vitals, Browser Compatibility, PWA,

Cookie Consent, Social Sharing, Accessibility, URL Structure.

LAYER 2B → Mobile-Specific (12 sections — M1 to M12)

Run when your app has a native or hybrid mobile app.

Covers: App Store, Versioning, Background Tasks, Battery,

Permissions, Biometric, Deep Linking, App Size,

Crash Reporting, OTA Updates, A/B Testing, Tablet Layout.

LAYER 3 → App-Type Module (pick one if applicable)

Run the ONE module that matches your app type.

Only run this if your app clearly fits the category.

3A → E-commerce / Marketplace

3B → Social / Community Platform

3C → AI-Powered Application

3D → Regulated Industry (Healthcare / Fintech / Legal)

3E → Offline-First Application

MY LAYERS: (e.g. Layer 1 + Layer 2A + Layer 3C)

STEP 5 — HOW TO RUN EACH SECTION

RULE 1 — ONE SECTION PER SESSION

Open a new chat session for each section.

Do not try to run multiple sections in one session.

Each section is a full prompt — it needs full context window.

RULE 2 — ALWAYS START WITH CONTEXT BLOCK

At the top of every section session, paste this context block:

(Fill it in after completing §01-04)

╔══════════════════════════════════════════╗

║  PROJECT CONTEXT BLOCK                   ║

║  (paste at top of every section session) ║

╚══════════════════════════════════════════╝

App name: ___

Type: ___

Platform: (web / mobile / both)

Track: (Fast / Full)

Auth model: ___

DB type: ___

Multi-tenant: (yes / no)

Compliance: ___

Scale target: ___ users / ___ RPS

Tech stack: ___

Key constraints: ___

§01 output summary: [paste 3-5 bullet points from your §01 output]

§02 output summary: [paste key entities and user roles]

§03 output summary: [paste key NFR targets]

§04 output summary: [paste scale tier and cost model]

RULE 3 — PASS OUTPUTS FORWARD

After completing each section, copy the key decisions into your

Project Context Block. This keeps every session aligned.

Key outputs to save after each section:

After §05: Architecture style, services list, tech stack

After §06: Auth model, token strategy, session type

After §07: DB engine, schema approach, multi-tenancy model

After §08: API style (REST/GraphQL), versioning, auth method

After §12: All third-party services and their integration type

After §14: Design system name, token names, component library

After §15: State management choice, routing model, SSR/CSR

RULE 4 — FLAG CONFLICTS IMMEDIATELY

If any section output contradicts a previous decision,

stop and resolve it before proceeding.

Do NOT continue with a known contradiction — it compounds.

RULE 5 — AGENT HINTS ARE INSTRUCTIONS

Every section ends with [AGENT HINT].

These are direct instructions to the AI agent for what code to generate.

After filling in the section answers, paste the whole section

(with your answers filled in) into Lovable / Replit / Bolt.

The [AGENT HINT] tells the agent exactly what to build.

STEP 6 — SECTION DEPENDENCY MAP

These are the hard dependencies — sections that MUST be

completed before the section that depends on them.

§01 ──────────────────┬──→ §02

├──→ §03

├──→ §04

└──→ all sections (context)

§02 + §03 + §04 ─────┬──→ §05

└──→ §06, §07, §08 (via §05)

§05 ──────────────────┬──→ §06 (trust boundaries)

├──→ §07 (module boundaries)

├──→ §08 (API style decision)

└──→ §15 (rendering strategy)

§06 ──────────────────┬──→ §07 (identity model)

├──→ §08 (auth headers)

├──→ §15 (auth state)

└──→ §18 (security model)

§07 ──────────────────┬──→ §08 (data shapes)

├──→ §17 (transaction model)

└──→ §29 (retention per entity)

§08 ──────────────────┬──→ §12 (integration contracts)

├──→ §13 (async job triggers)

└──→ §15 (API client)

§12 ──────────────────└──→ §13 (queue triggers from integrations)

§14 ──────────────────└──→ §15 (component library)

§05 + §06 + §07 ──────└──→ §16 (what to rate-limit)

§19 ──────────────────└──→ §20 (compliance per data class)

§27 (Observability) ──┬──→ requires §25 (infra) to be done

└──→ requires §04 (scale) as reference

§30 (Testing) ────────└──→ requires §07, §08, §12 to be complete

STEP 7 — SECTION CONFLICT RULES

These rules prevent the most common contradictions between sections.

The rule states which section OWNS the decision.

All other sections reference it — they do NOT redefine it.

OWNERSHIP MAP:

Decision                          Owned by    Referenced by

Auth model (JWT vs session)       §06         §07, §08, §15, §18

Token refresh strategy            §06         §15 (interceptor)

Multi-tenancy model               §05         §06, §07, §08, §16, §19

DB engine choice                  §07         §17, §21, §22, §24

API versioning scheme             §08         §32 (evolution)

Rate limit tiers & rules          §16         §06 (auth limits), §08

Encryption standard (at rest)     §18         §07, §10, §29

PII field classification          §19         §07, §27, §29

Compliance obligations            §20         §18, §19, §27, §29

Caching layer choice (Redis etc)  §21         §06 (session), §16

DB migration tooling              §07 §21D    §24, §26, §32

SLO / uptime targets              §03         §22, §25, §27

Log retention period              §27         §29 (aligns with §20)

Test types & coverage gates       §30         §26 (CI blocks)

Feature flag lifecycle            §28, §32    never contradict each other

Invariant: If two sections define the same thing differently,

the section listed under "Owned by" wins.

Fix the contradiction in the referencing section.

STEP 8 — RECOMMENDED RUN ORDER BY APP TYPE

Use these optimized sequences for common app types.

They front-load the sections that have the most downstream dependencies.

B2B SaaS (multi-tenant, subscription)

Consumer Web App (freemium, growth-focused)

01→02→03→04→05→06→07→08→09→12→14→15→16

→18→19→21→24→28→11(search)→13(async)→22→27→30→32

Layer 2A: W1→W2→W5→W6→W7→W8

Mobile App (iOS + Android)

STEP 9 — WHAT THE AI AGENT DOES WITH THIS SYSTEM

Each section prompt produces structured output that the

AI agent (Lovable / Replit / Bolt) uses as follows:

§01-04 output  →  Creates project scaffold, folder structure,

README, initial config files

§05 output     →  Generates architecture diagram,

service boundaries, tech stack setup

§06 output     →  Generates auth system (login/signup/JWT/session),

middleware stack, role model

§07 output     →  Generates DB schema, migrations, seed files,

repository interfaces

§08 output     →  Generates API routes, validation schemas,

OpenAPI/Swagger spec

§09 output     →  Generates WebSocket/SSE server setup,

event emitters, reconnect logic

§10 output     →  Generates upload handlers, storage client,

stream pipeline

§11 output     →  Generates search index setup, query builders,

indexing workers

§12 output     →  Generates integration clients, retry workers,

health check endpoints

§13 output     →  Generates queue setup, job handlers,

dead letter processing

§14 output     →  Generates design token file, component interfaces,

Storybook structure

§15 output     →  Generates router config, API client, store setup,

error boundaries

§16 output     →  Generates rate limit middleware,

quota enforcement, abuse detection

§17 output     →  Generates transaction wrappers,

optimistic lock patterns, rollback handlers

§18 output     →  Generates security middleware stack,

CSP headers, SSRF protection

§19 output     →  Generates PII field registry, consent handlers,

data classification tags

§20 output     →  Generates compliance checklist, audit log schema,

data processing records

§21 output     →  Generates cache layer setup, TTL config,

invalidation strategy

§22 output     →  Generates circuit breakers, retry policies,

fallback handlers

§23 output     →  Generates performance budgets, profiling hooks,

load test baseline

§24 output     →  Generates CI/CD pipeline YAML, deploy scripts,

environment configs

§25 output     →  Generates security scan configs, threat model doc,

pen test scope

§26 output     →  Generates docker-compose, linting config,

pre-commit hooks, PR template

§27 output     →  Generates logger setup, metrics registry,

alerting rules, dashboard JSON

§28 output     →  Generates analytics event tracker, feature flags,

funnel definitions

§29 output     →  Generates retention jobs, GDPR erasure workflow,

DSAR export endpoint

§30 output     →  Generates test factories, integration test boilerplate,

E2E test structure, k6 load scripts

§31 output     →  Generates i18n config, translation key structure,

timezone formatters

§32 output     →  Generates API versioning middleware, deprecation headers,

ADR template, flag lifecycle rules

§01 — PRODUCT STRATEGY + UX BLUEPRINT + COMMERCIAL MODEL

You are a senior product architect preparing a Product & Business

Foundation

document that will be handed directly to an AI development agent (e.g.,

Replit,

Lovable, Bolt) to scaffold a web and/or mobile application.

Your output must be precise, specific, and actionable --- not generic.

Avoid vague phrases like "scalable", "user-friendly", or "seamless

experience."

If critical information is missing, make a clearly labeled assumption.

Do NOT begin technical architecture. Do NOT write code.

Flag any assumptions that must be validated before development starts.

1\. PRODUCT DEFINITION

One-liner:

"This product helps [specific user] solve [specific problem] by

[clear mechanism]."

• Core value proposition (1--2 sentences, no fluff)

• Key differentiator (pick ONE primary: cost / UX / automation / AI /

network effect / speed)

• Why now? (market timing, tech enabler, regulation, behavior shift)

• What this product is NOT (scope boundary)

2\. PROBLEM & MARKET

• The broken workflow (step-by-step, what users do today without this

product)

• Direct alternatives (name them specifically)

• Indirect alternatives (workarounds, spreadsheets, manual processes)

• Why existing solutions fail (be specific, not "they're too

expensive")

• Switching cost for the user

• Target segment: [role] + [company size or context] +

[geography]

• Market size estimate (rough TAM/SAM is fine, state your assumption)

3\. USER PERSONAS

For each user type (primary, secondary, admin):

• Role & context

• Primary goal

• Pain points (top 3, ranked)

• Trigger event (what causes them to open the app right now)

• Usage frequency & estimated session length

• Criticality (if this user churns, does the product fail?)

• Device preference (web / iOS / Android / all)

• Technical literacy level (low / medium / high)

4\. CRITICAL USER JOURNEYS

List the 3--5 most critical flows that must work perfectly at launch.

For each:

• Journey name

• Start state → end state

• Numbered steps (specific, not vague)

• Platform (web / mobile / both)

• What failure here means for the user

5\. ONBOARDING FLOW

• Signup method (email / social / SSO / phone / invite-only)

• Steps from signup → first value moment (numbered, specific)

• "Aha moment" --- the exact point a new user gets value for the

first time

• What the empty state looks like (no data, no team, fresh account)

• Guided setup requirements (tooltips / checklist / walkthrough / none)

• What triggers the first re-engagement if user drops off after signup

6\. SCREEN INVENTORY

List every screen the MVP requires. For each screen:

• Screen name

• Primary purpose (one sentence)

• Platform (web / mobile / both)

• User type who sees it

Group by:

Auth screens (login, signup, forgot password, etc.)

Onboarding screens

Core app screens

Settings & account screens

Admin screens (if any)

Target: 10--20 screens for MVP. If more, flag for scope review.

7\. WEB vs MOBILE STRATEGY

• What is exclusively done on web (and why)

• What is exclusively done on mobile (and why)

• What is shared across both

• Mobile-specific requirements:

• Push notifications: yes/no --- if yes, what triggers them?

• Offline capability: yes/no --- if yes, which features work offline?

• Camera / GPS / biometrics: yes/no --- if yes, exact purpose

• App store distribution: iOS / Android / both / PWA only

• Deep linking required: yes/no

• Decision: Responsive web vs native app --- state the choice and

rationale

8\. NOTIFICATION STRATEGY

For each notification type needed:

• Trigger event (what causes this notification)

• Channel (push / email / SMS / in-app)

• Recipient

• Timing (immediate / scheduled / digest)

• Re-engagement logic (what sequence fires if user goes inactive)

• User control (can they opt out? which ones are mandatory?)

9\. MULTI-TENANCY & COLLABORATION MODEL

• Single-user or multi-user accounts?

• If multi-user:

• Who creates the account (owner)?

• How are others invited?

• Role hierarchy (owner / admin / member / viewer)

• What happens when the owner leaves or deletes the account?

• Can users belong to multiple workspaces?

• Data ownership model (who owns the data --- user or organization?)

10\. ERROR & EDGE CASE HANDLING

Define product-level decisions for:

• Payment failure → what does the user see and what happens to their

account?

• Session expiry mid-flow → where do they land after re-login?

• Internet loss mid-action → is data saved? is the user warned?

• Third-party service downtime → is there a fallback or graceful

degradation?

• Invalid / incomplete data submission → inline errors or page-level?

• Account deletion → what is deleted, what is retained, is it

reversible?

11\. MONETIZATION

• Revenue model (subscription / usage-based / one-time / marketplace /

freemium)

• Value metric (what scales with usage --- seats, actions, volume,

etc.)

• Pricing tiers (2--3 tiers, name specific feature differences per

tier)

• Upgrade trigger (exact moment user hits a paywall --- which action,

which screen)

• Expansion path (how does revenue grow per account over time)

• Billing lifecycle: trial → paid → renewal → cancellation →

reactivation

• Payment processor + region (Stripe / Razorpay / other)

12\. RETENTION & GROWTH

• Primary retention driver (habit / data lock-in / workflow dependency

/ network)

• Lock-in mechanism (what makes leaving painful or costly)

• Viral or growth loop (referral / collaboration / sharing --- or none)

• Distribution model (self-serve / sales-led / product-led /

partnership)

• Key activation moment (when does a new user get undeniable value?)

13\. SCOPE

MVP --- ship this, nothing else:

• [Feature] --- [one line on why it's in MVP]

Phase 2 --- after first 100 active users:

• [Feature list]

Explicitly out of scope for MVP:

• [Anything that might be assumed but should NOT be built yet]

14\. SUCCESS METRICS

Define success at 30 / 90 / 180 days:

• Activation metric (% of signups who complete onboarding)

• Retention metric (D7 and D30 return rate)

• Revenue metric (MRR / ARR target)

• Engagement metric (sessions per user per week, key actions per

session)

• One North Star metric (the single number that proves this product is

working)

15\. ACCESSIBILITY & LOCALIZATION

State your decision clearly --- skipping is a valid choice, but it must

be explicit:

• Languages at launch

• RTL support: yes / no

• Accessibility standard: WCAG 2.1 AA / basic / none (state why)

• Currency, date, and number format requirements

16\. CONSTRAINTS & RISKS

Constraints:

• Team size & skillset

• Budget range

• Target launch date

• Regulatory requirements (GDPR / data residency / industry-specific)

Risks (top 3, ranked by severity):

• Risk → likelihood → mitigation

17\. ASSUMPTIONS TO VALIDATE

List every assumption made in this document that must be confirmed

before a development agent begins scaffolding.

Mark each as:

[CRITICAL] --- blocks the build if wrong

[IMPORTANT] --- changes scope if wrong

[MINOR] --- can be adjusted post-launch

18. APPLICATION-LEVEL CONTRACTS

[Auth Middleware, Token Refresh & Session Store]

18A. MIDDLEWARE STACK ORDER

Declare the exact middleware execution order for every inbound request:

1. Transport security (TLS termination / HTTPS enforcement)

2. Request ID injection (correlation ID for tracing)

3. Rate-limit check (pre-auth — IP / global)

4. Auth token extraction (header / cookie / query param — pick ONE)

5. Token verification (local JWT validation OR remote introspection)

6. Session hydration (load session state from store if stateful)

7. Identity attachment (set req.user / ctx.identity)

8. Tenant resolution (extract tenantId from token / subdomain / header)

9. Permission evaluation (RBAC / ABAC check against req.user + route)

10. Rate-limit check (post-auth — per-user / per-tenant)

11. Request body parsing

12. Route handler

Invariant: Auth middleware MUST run before any business logic handler.

Invariant: Tenant resolution MUST run before permission evaluation.

Invariant: A missing or malformed auth token MUST return 401 — never 500.

Define:

- Middleware framework/layer: (express/koa/fastify/custom/other)

- Auth token extraction strategy: (Authorization header Bearer / HttpOnly cookie / both)

- Short-circuit on auth failure: (yes — stop pipeline / no — continue with null identity)

- Logging at which middleware steps: (all / auth only / failures only)

18B. TOKEN REFRESH INTERCEPTOR

Define the client-side (and server-side) token refresh contract:

CLIENT INTERCEPTOR CONTRACT:

- Trigger condition: (401 response / token expiry within N seconds / explicit check)

- Refresh endpoint: POST /auth/refresh (or equivalent)

- Refresh request payload: { refreshToken: string }

- Refresh response shape: { accessToken: string, expiresIn: number, refreshToken?: string }

- Retry behavior after refresh: (replay original request once / notify caller / redirect to login)

- Concurrent refresh handling: (queue pending requests / one refresh at a time — use mutex/lock)

- Refresh failure behavior: (clear session + redirect to login / emit auth:logout event)

- Max refresh retry attempts: ___

SERVER INTERCEPTOR CONTRACT:

- Refresh token rotation: (yes — issue new refresh token on each use / no — static)

- Refresh token storage: (DB / Redis / signed cookie — must match session store)

- Refresh token family tracking: (yes — detect reuse attack / no)

- Revoke all refresh tokens on logout: (yes / no)

- Revoke all refresh tokens on password change: (yes / no)

Invariant: If refresh token is reused after rotation, invalidate entire token family.

Invariant: Refresh endpoint MUST NOT accept expired access tokens as proof of identity — only valid refresh token.

18C. SESSION STORE INTERFACE

If stateful sessions are used, define the session store contract:

Session store type: (Redis / DB / in-memory / cookie-signed / hybrid)

Session key format: session:{userId}:{sessionId}

Session value schema:

{

sessionId: string (UUID),

userId: string,

tenantId: string (if multi-tenant),

roles: string[],

createdAt: ISO8601,

lastActiveAt: ISO8601,

expiresAt: ISO8601,

deviceFingerprint?: string,

ipAddress?: string,

metadata?: Record<string, unknown>

}

Operations required:

- create(session): Promise<void>

- get(sessionId): Promise<Session | null>

- refresh(sessionId, newExpiry): Promise<void>

- invalidate(sessionId): Promise<void>

- invalidateAll(userId): Promise<void>  ← for global logout

- list(userId): Promise<Session[]>      ← for session management UI

TTL strategy: (sliding window — reset on activity / fixed — expires from creation)

Session store failure behavior: (fail closed — deny access / fail open — allow with warning)

If stateless JWT: declare what claims are embedded and what is looked up per-request.

18D. AUTH ERROR RESPONSE SHAPES

All auth errors MUST return consistent, non-leaking response shapes.

Standard error envelope:

{

error: {

code: string,        // Machine-readable: AUTH_TOKEN_MISSING, AUTH_TOKEN_EXPIRED,

// AUTH_TOKEN_INVALID, AUTH_PERMISSION_DENIED,

// AUTH_ACCOUNT_LOCKED, AUTH_SESSION_EXPIRED,

// AUTH_MFA_REQUIRED, AUTH_TENANT_SUSPENDED

message: string,     // Human-readable (non-sensitive — no stack traces, no DB errors)

retryable: boolean,  // true = client can retry; false = requires user action

action?: string      // REDIRECT_LOGIN / PROMPT_MFA / CONTACT_SUPPORT

}

}

HTTP status mapping (MUST be consistent):

- 401 Unauthorized: missing token / expired token / invalid token / session expired

- 403 Forbidden: valid identity, insufficient permission / tenant mismatch

- 423 Locked: account locked out

- 429 Too Many Requests: rate limit on auth endpoints

Invariant: NEVER return 200 with an error body for auth failures.

Invariant: Error messages MUST NOT reveal whether an email address exists in the system

(prevents user enumeration — return identical message for unknown email vs wrong password).

Invariant: Response timing MUST be normalized on login/reset flows (prevents timing attacks).

position

→ Define permission guards per route

→ Define admin panel isolation

→ Define service account token schema

→ Define auth event log schema

(pass to Section 27)

→ Define account recovery flows

as screens (pass to Section 02)

21. APPLICATION-LEVEL CONTRACTS

[Repository Pattern, Transactions, Pool Init, Migration Runner]

21A. REPOSITORY PATTERN INTERFACE

Define the data access contract that all business logic must use.

No business logic may call the DB directly — only through a repository.

Base repository interface (per entity):

interface Repository<T, ID> {

findById(id: ID, opts?: QueryOpts): Promise<T | null>

findMany(filter: Filter<T>, opts?: QueryOpts): Promise<T[]>

create(data: CreateInput<T>): Promise<T>

update(id: ID, data: UpdateInput<T>): Promise<T>

delete(id: ID): Promise<void>          // or soft-delete if applicable

count(filter: Filter<T>): Promise<number>

exists(filter: Filter<T>): Promise<boolean>

}

QueryOpts shape:

{

tenantId?: string,       // Mandatory for multi-tenant entities

transaction?: TxHandle,  // Pass active transaction handle

forUpdate?: boolean,     // SELECT FOR UPDATE (pessimistic lock)

include?: string[],      // Related entities to eager-load

orderBy?: SortSpec,

limit?: number,

offset?: number

}

Invariant: Repository MUST inject tenantId into every query for tenant-scoped entities.

Invariant: Repository MUST NOT expose raw SQL / query builder to callers.

Invariant: Soft-deleted records MUST be excluded from all findMany results unless

caller passes { includeDeleted: true }.

Declare which entities have repositories:

- One repository per root aggregate (DDD principle, if applicable)

- Cross-aggregate queries → dedicated query service, NOT repository composition

21B. TRANSACTION BOUNDARY DECLARATION

Define where transaction boundaries are enforced.

Transaction ownership layer: (service layer / use-case layer / repository — pick ONE)

Recommendation: service layer owns transactions; repositories participate.

Transaction handle interface:

interface TxHandle {

commit(): Promise<void>

rollback(): Promise<void>

isActive(): boolean

}

Transaction factory:

interface TransactionManager {

run<T>(fn: (tx: TxHandle) => Promise<T>): Promise<T>

// Rolls back automatically on thrown error; commits on success

}

Declare which operations REQUIRE a transaction:

- Multi-table writes (yes — always)

- Balance / quota updates (yes — always, with SELECT FOR UPDATE)

- Idempotency token creation + consumption (yes — within same transaction)

- Audit log + primary write (yes / no — depends on consistency requirement)

- Notification trigger + state change (no — use outbox pattern instead)

Declare which operations MUST NOT span a transaction:

- External HTTP calls (network I/O inside DB transaction = lock duration risk)

- File uploads to object storage

- Email / push notification dispatch

Invariant: Transactions MUST NOT cross service boundaries.

Invariant: Transaction timeout: ___ seconds (align with Section 03 P95 latency target).

21C. CONNECTION POOL INITIALIZATION

Define how the DB connection pool is configured and initialized at startup.

Pool configuration:

{

min: ___,           // Minimum idle connections (suggested: 2)

max: ___,           // Maximum connections (must align with DB server max_connections)

acquireTimeout: ___ ms,   // Time to wait for a connection before error

idleTimeout: ___ ms,      // Close idle connections after this duration

connectionTimeout: ___ ms // Time to establish new connection

}

Initialization order at service startup:

1. Load DB credentials from secret store (NOT env var in production)

2. Create pool with config above

3. Run health-check query (SELECT 1) — fail startup if this fails

4. Run pending migrations (see 21D)

5. Emit "db:ready" signal — only then accept inbound traffic

Pool exhaustion behavior: (queue requests up to acquireTimeout / reject immediately with 503)

Pool failure behavior: (circuit breaker — stop accepting requests / log + retry)

Multi-database handling (if applicable):

- Primary (read-write): pool config above

- Read replica (read-only): separate pool, max connections ___

- Analytics DB (if separate): separate pool, max connections ___

Invariant: Connection pool MUST be initialized once at startup, never per-request.

Invariant: Pool max × number of service replicas MUST NOT exceed DB server max_connections.

Formula: pool.max × replica_count ≤ db_max_connections × 0.8 (leave 20% headroom)

21D. MIGRATION RUNNER CONFIGURATION

Define how schema migrations are applied, tracked, and rolled back.

Migration tool: (Flyway / Liquibase / Knex / Prisma Migrate / Alembic / custom — state choice)

Migration table name: ___ (default: schema_migrations / flyway_schema_history)

Migration file naming convention:

V{timestamp}__{description}.sql   (e.g., V20240115_001__add_user_tenantId.sql)

or

{NNN}_{description}.ts            (e.g., 001_add_user_tenantId.ts)

Migration execution at startup:

- Run automatically on service startup? (yes / no)

If yes: migrations run in transaction; rollback entire migration on error

If no: migrations run as separate deployment step (recommended for production)

Migration locking: (yes — advisory lock prevents concurrent migration runs / no)

Migration failure behavior: (fail service startup / alert ops and continue / rollback)

Rollback strategy:

- Automated rollback: (yes — undo script for each migration / no — manual only)

- Forward-only migrations: (yes — no rollback scripts, use compensating migrations / no)

- Zero-downtime migration pattern: (expand-contract / big-bang — state choice)

Migration environment promotion:

dev → staging → production

- Who approves production migrations: ___

- Dry-run required before production: (yes / no)

- Data migration timeout: ___ seconds (kill if exceeded)

Invariant: NEVER run migrations against production during peak traffic windows

(define off-peak window: ___).

Invariant: Every destructive migration (DROP COLUMN / DROP TABLE) requires

a preceding migration that deploys with the column still present

(expand-contract pattern).

16. APPLICATION-LEVEL CONTRACTS

[Client Reconnect, Event Emitter, Channel Subscription Manager]

16A. CLIENT RECONNECT HANDLER SHAPE

Define the contract for client-side reconnection logic.

ReconnectConfig:

{

initialDelayMs: ___,        // First retry delay (suggested: 1000ms)

maxDelayMs: ___,            // Cap on backoff (suggested: 30000ms)

backoffMultiplier: ___,     // Exponential factor (suggested: 1.5)

jitterFactor: ___,          // Random spread to prevent thundering herd (suggested: 0.2)

maxAttempts: number | "infinite",

reconnectOnCodes: number[], // WebSocket close codes that trigger reconnect

// e.g., [1006, 1012, 1013] — exclude 1000 (normal close), 4001 (auth fail)

}

ReconnectHandler interface:

interface ReconnectHandler {

onDisconnect(code: number, reason: string): void

onReconnecting(attempt: number, delayMs: number): void

onReconnected(resumeToken?: string): void

onGiveUp(lastError: Error): void      // Called after maxAttempts exceeded

getResumeToken(): string | null       // Return last known cursor/sequence for missed events

}

State recovery on reconnect:

- Resume from last event cursor: (yes / no)

- Replay missed events on reconnect: (yes — up to N events / no)

- Re-subscribe to all channels automatically: (yes / no)

- Notify application layer of gap in event stream: (yes — emit "stream:gap" / no)

Invariant: Client MUST NOT attempt reconnect on 4001 (auth failure) — redirect to login.

Invariant: Client MUST implement exponential backoff with jitter (no fixed-interval retry).

Invariant: Reconnect MUST re-authenticate (re-send token) — do not assume prior auth persists.

16B. EVENT EMITTER INTERFACE

Define the server-side event emission contract used by all services.

EventEmitter interface:

interface RealtimeEmitter {

emit(channel: string, event: string, payload: unknown, opts?: EmitOpts): Promise<void>

emitToUser(userId: string, event: string, payload: unknown): Promise<void>

emitToTenant(tenantId: string, event: string, payload: unknown): Promise<void>

emitToRoom(roomId: string, event: string, payload: unknown): Promise<void>

broadcast(event: string, payload: unknown): Promise<void>   // All connected clients

}

EmitOpts:

{

ttl?: number,          // Discard event if not delivered within N seconds

dedupKey?: string,     // Idempotency — skip if same key emitted within window

volatile?: boolean,    // true = skip if no clients connected (no queue)

ack?: boolean,         // true = wait for client acknowledgment

ackTimeout?: number    // ms to wait for ack before marking failed

}

Event envelope (standard shape for all emitted events):

{

id: string,            // UUID — for idempotent processing on client

channel: string,

event: string,

payload: unknown,

tenantId: string,      // Always present for multi-tenant systems

emittedAt: ISO8601,

version: number        // Monotonic sequence number per channel

}

Invariant: Event envelope MUST include tenantId — clients MUST validate against their context.

Invariant: Emitter MUST NOT include PII in the event payload unless the channel is user-private.

Invariant: emitToTenant MUST enforce tenant isolation — never leak events across tenants.

16C. CHANNEL SUBSCRIPTION MANAGER

Define how clients subscribe to and unsubscribe from channels.

SubscriptionManager interface:

interface SubscriptionManager {

subscribe(clientId: string, channel: string, opts?: SubOpts): Promise<SubHandle>

unsubscribe(clientId: string, channel: string): Promise<void>

unsubscribeAll(clientId: string): Promise<void>  // Called on disconnect

getSubscriptions(clientId: string): Promise<string[]>

getSubscribers(channel: string): Promise<string[]>

}

SubOpts:

{

auth?: boolean,        // Require additional channel-level auth check (private channels)

cursor?: string,       // Resume from event cursor (for missed-event replay)

filter?: Record<string, unknown>  // Server-side event filter (reduce client traffic)

}

SubHandle:

{

channelId: string,

clientId: string,

subscribedAt: ISO8601,

cursor: string,        // Current position in event stream

unsubscribe(): Promise<void>

}

Channel authorization rules:

- Public channels (no auth check): ___

- Tenant channels (tenantId match required): ___

- User-private channels (userId match required): ___

- Room channels (membership check required): ___

Channel naming convention:

public:{event_type}

tenant:{tenantId}:{event_type}

user:{userId}:{event_type}

room:{roomId}:{event_type}

Subscription limits:

- Max channels per client: ___

- Max subscribers per channel: ___

- Subscription TTL (auto-unsubscribe after inactivity): ___

Invariant: Server MUST authorize channel access on subscribe — not just on connect.

Invariant: On client disconnect, all subscriptions MUST be cleaned up immediately.

Invariant: Channel names MUST NOT contain user-provided content directly (injection risk).

18. APPLICATION-LEVEL CONTRACTS

[Upload Middleware, Stream Pipeline, Storage Client Interface]

18A. UPLOAD HANDLER MIDDLEWARE SHAPE

Define the contract for file upload handling middleware.

UploadMiddleware configuration:

{

maxFileSize: ___ bytes,     // Hard limit — reject with 413 above this

maxFilesPerRequest: ___,    // Max concurrent files in multipart upload

allowedMimeTypes: string[], // Whitelist — reject unknown types with 415

allowedExtensions: string[],

fieldName: string,          // Multipart field name expected

destination: "memory" | "disk" | "stream",

// memory: buffer (small files only, <10MB)

// disk: temp file (for large files, cleaned up after processing)

// stream: pipe directly to storage (preferred for large files)

virusScanRequired: boolean, // (if yes, scan before writing to permanent storage)

}

Upload lifecycle hooks:

interface UploadMiddleware {

onFileReceived(file: FileInfo): Promise<void>   // Validate metadata, check quota

onChunkReceived(chunk: Buffer, offset: number): Promise<void>

onFileComplete(file: FileInfo): Promise<UploadResult>

onError(error: UploadError, file?: FileInfo): Promise<void>  // Cleanup temp file

onAbort(file: FileInfo): Promise<void>           // Client disconnected mid-upload

}

FileInfo shape:

{

fieldName: string,

originalName: string,   // User-provided — NEVER use directly as storage key

mimeType: string,       // From content-type header — ALWAYS re-validate server-side

encoding: string,

size: number,           // Bytes received so far

tempPath?: string       // If disk destination

}

Invariant: NEVER trust client-provided filename or MIME type — re-detect server-side.

Invariant: Temp files MUST be cleaned up on error, abort, or success.

Invariant: Upload progress updates MUST be throttled (max 1 update per 500ms) to prevent

event loop saturation.

18B. STREAM PIPELINE DECLARATION

Define the processing pipeline for file uploads and downloads.

Upload stream pipeline (ordered steps):

1. Receive multipart stream (from HTTP request body)

2. Validate content-type and extension (reject early — before reading body)

3. MIME type re-detection (magic bytes, not extension)

4. Size gate (reject if content-length header exceeds max — before buffering)

5. Virus scan stream (if required — pipe to ClamAV or equivalent)

6. Transform / compress (resize image / generate thumbnail / transcode)

7. Encrypt (if at-rest encryption required — Section 18)

8. Upload to storage backend (stream — do NOT buffer entire file in memory)

9. Generate storage key and record metadata in DB

10. Emit "file:uploaded" event (if real-time subscribers)

11. Enqueue post-processing job (thumbnail, OCR, indexing — async, not in upload path)

12. Return upload result to caller

Download stream pipeline:

1. Validate requester has permission to access the file (ownership / tenant check)

2. Fetch pre-signed URL from storage client (preferred) OR stream directly

3. Set correct Content-Type, Content-Disposition, Content-Length headers

4. Stream to client (do NOT buffer in application memory)

5. Log download event (if audit required)

Invariant: Upload MUST NOT buffer entire file in application memory for files >10MB.

Invariant: Pipeline steps 1-4 MUST complete before writing any bytes to permanent storage.

Invariant: Post-processing (thumbnails, indexing) MUST run outside the upload request path.

18C. STORAGE CLIENT INTERFACE

Define the abstraction layer between the application and the storage backend.

StorageClient interface:

interface StorageClient {

upload(key: string, stream: Readable, opts: UploadOpts): Promise<UploadResult>

download(key: string): Promise<Readable>

getPresignedUrl(key: string, opts: PresignOpts): Promise<string>

delete(key: string): Promise<void>

deleteMany(keys: string[]): Promise<DeleteResult>

exists(key: string): Promise<boolean>

getMetadata(key: string): Promise<FileMetadata>

copy(sourceKey: string, destKey: string): Promise<void>

move(sourceKey: string, destKey: string): Promise<void>

}

UploadOpts:

{

mimeType: string,

size: number,

tenantId: string,        // For path scoping / ACL

encryption?: EncryptionSpec,

cacheControl?: string,   // "public, max-age=31536000" for static assets

metadata?: Record<string, string>

}

PresignOpts:

{

expiresIn: number,       // Seconds until URL expires

contentType?: string,    // Lock to specific content-type for PUT pre-signed URLs

maxSizeBytes?: number    // Limit upload size via pre-signed URL policy

}

Storage key naming convention (immutable once defined):

{tenantId}/{entity}/{entityId}/{fileId}.{ext}

e.g., acme-corp/invoices/inv_123/file_456.pdf

Invariant: Storage keys MUST be generated server-side (UUID-based) — never from user input.

Invariant: Pre-signed URLs MUST include tenant scope in the key to prevent cross-tenant access.

Invariant: StorageClient MUST NOT be called from HTTP request handlers directly — only

through the Upload/Download service layer.

Invariant: StorageClient implementation MUST be swappable (S3 / GCS / Azure Blob / local)

without changing calling code.

§11 — SEARCH & DISCOVERY

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Yes --- if searchable entities exist

[PURPOSE] → Define indexing model, search

architecture, query contracts,

ranking logic, consistency

guarantees, tenant isolation,

privacy filtering, and lifecycle

alignment across Sections 02--10.

Do NOT choose vendor.

Do NOT write search queries.

Do NOT assume external search engine.

Define indexing contracts, data flow,

isolation rules, consistency guarantees,

and scaling boundaries only.

All decisions must reference:

• Section 02 --- Functional requirements

• Section 03 --- Performance requirements

• Section 05 --- Architecture style

• Section 07 --- Data model

• Section 08 --- API contracts

• Section 09 --- Real-time architecture

• Section 29 --- Data lifecycle

low / medium / high

2\. SEARCH ARCHITECTURE MODEL

Select architecture:

• Database native search

• Dedicated search service

• Hybrid

• In-memory search

• External search cluster

Justify based on:

• Query complexity

• Ranking needs

• Data volume

• Latency requirements

• Multi-tenant isolation

Define:

• Read model separate from write

model? (yes / no)

• Max tolerated indexing delay:

\_\_\_ seconds

• Rebuild index strategy defined?

(yes / no)

SEARCH CONSISTENCY TIER

Select exactly one:

• Strong

(read-after-write guaranteed ---

index updated synchronously)

• Near-real-time

(searchable within \<5 seconds)

• Eventual

(searchable within \<30 seconds)

• Batch

(searchable within \>60 seconds)

User-facing write → searchable

within \_\_\_ seconds.

UI must show indexing disclaimer?

(yes / no)

This drives whether indexing is

synchronous, whether the UI shows

"may take a few seconds to appear",

and whether post-write search is

immediately reliable.

Without this declaration agents

defer the decision --- producing

inconsistent indexing behavior.

INDEX WARM-UP STRATEGY

synthetic queries / pre-load /

gradual traffic shift

• Warm-up completion signal:

latency threshold met /

cache hit ratio threshold /

manual approval

• Traffic served during warm-up:

old index / new index /

split traffic

Cold index nodes produce

dramatically slower first queries.

Declare warm-up strategy to prevent

post-deploy latency spikes.

CURSOR STABILITY & SNAPSHOT

CONSISTENCY

• Cursor stability guaranteed

during pagination? (yes / no)

• Results change mid-pagination:

restart / continue / mark stale

• Search results served from

consistent index snapshot?

(yes / no)

• Cursor bound to index version?

(yes / no)

• Index version encoded in cursor?

(yes / no)

• Snapshot TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

• Snapshot storage strategy:

versioned index /

timestamp-based / other

SNAPSHOT STORAGE CAPS

• Max concurrent active snapshots

per user: \_\_\_

• Max concurrent active snapshots

per tenant: \_\_\_

• Global snapshot cap: \_\_\_

• Snapshot memory / storage cap:

\_\_\_ GB

• Action when cap exceeded:

reject new search /

evict oldest snapshot /

shorten TTL

Heavy users paging large datasets

will quietly exhaust memory without

snapshot caps.

Cursor stability = results don't

shuffle between pages.

Snapshot consistency = index itself

doesn't change between page requests.

Both required for deterministic

pagination under high write volume.

RANKING DETERMINISM

• Deterministic secondary sort

required? (yes / no)

• Tie-breaker rule:

when relevance score equal →

sort by: ID / timestamp /

deterministic hash

• Tie-breaker field must be:

stable / unique / indexed

Without deterministic tie-breaking

pagination duplicates occur even

with snapshot consistency declared.

This is the last remaining source

of ghost shuffle.

Ranking must NEVER override

permission filtering.

20\. SEARCH DOWNGRADE HIERARCHY

When search capacity is degraded,

degrade features in this order

(1 = degrade first):

1\. \_\_\_ (lowest --- e.g. autocomplete)

2\. \_\_\_ (e.g. cross-entity federation)

3\. \_\_\_ (e.g. ranking personalization)

4\. \_\_\_ (e.g. highlight snippets)

5\. \_\_\_ (e.g. full-text search)

6\. \_\_\_ (e.g. advanced filtering)

7\. \_\_\_ (never degrade ---

core entity lookup)

• Fallback for each degraded level:

DB query / cached results /

disabled with user message

• User notified on degradation?

(yes / no)

Declaring this in advance makes

incident response mechanical.

Without it every incident requires

a real-time product decision

under pressure.

18. APPLICATION-LEVEL CONTRACTS

[Index Client Interface, Query Builder, Result Mapper]

18A. INDEX CLIENT INTERFACE

Define the abstraction layer between the application and the search engine.

IndexClient interface:

interface IndexClient {

index(doc: IndexDoc, opts?: IndexOpts): Promise<void>

indexBatch(docs: IndexDoc[], opts?: IndexOpts): Promise<BatchResult>

update(id: string, partial: Partial<IndexDoc>, opts?: IndexOpts): Promise<void>

delete(id: string, tenantId: string): Promise<void>

deleteByQuery(filter: SearchFilter): Promise<DeleteResult>

search(query: SearchQuery): Promise<SearchResult>

suggest(prefix: string, field: string, opts?: SuggestOpts): Promise<string[]>

count(filter: SearchFilter): Promise<number>

healthCheck(): Promise<{ status: "healthy" | "degraded" | "down" }>

}

IndexDoc (base shape — extend per entity):

{

id: string,            // Primary key — same as DB entity ID

tenantId: string,      // MANDATORY for multi-tenant systems

entityType: string,    // "user" | "product" | "document" etc.

createdAt: ISO8601,

updatedAt: ISO8601,

// ... entity-specific fields

}

IndexOpts:

{

refresh?: "true" | "false" | "wait_for",  // Index visibility timing

routing?: string,        // For tenant-based shard routing

pipeline?: string,       // Ingest pipeline name (if applicable)

ifSeqNo?: number,        // Optimistic concurrency — only update if version matches

ifPrimaryTerm?: number

}

Invariant: tenantId MUST be present in every IndexDoc — enforced at index time.

Invariant: IndexClient MUST be called asynchronously (via queue) from write paths

— never inline in a DB transaction.

18B. QUERY BUILDER CONTRACT

Define how search queries are constructed and validated.

SearchQuery shape:

{

tenantId: string,         // Injected by service layer — never from user input directly

q?: string,               // Full-text query string (user-provided)

filters?: SearchFilter[], // Structured filters (field/operator/value)

sort?: SortSpec[],        // [{field, direction}]

pagination: {

from: number,           // Offset (0-based)

size: number            // Page size — MAX enforced server-side

},

facets?: string[],        // Fields to compute facet counts for

highlight?: boolean,      // Return highlighted snippets

explain?: boolean         // Debug mode — never expose in production responses

}

SearchFilter:

{

field: string,

operator: "eq" | "neq" | "gt" | "gte" | "lt" | "lte" | "in" | "contains" | "exists",

value: unknown

}

QueryBuilder interface:

interface QueryBuilder {

forTenant(tenantId: string): this        // ALWAYS called first — sets tenant scope

withText(q: string): this

withFilter(filter: SearchFilter): this

withSort(field: string, dir: "asc" | "desc"): this

paginate(from: number, size: number): this

withFacets(fields: string[]): this

build(): SearchQuery

validate(): ValidationResult             // Check for field existence, type mismatches

}

Server-side query constraints:

- Max page size: ___ results

- Max text query length: ___ characters

- Max filters per query: ___

- Prohibited filter fields (internal): ["_id", "_index", "tenantId" — managed by server]

- Wildcard / regex queries: (allowed / disallowed — performance risk)

Invariant: QueryBuilder.forTenant() MUST be called before build() — throw if not set.

Invariant: User-supplied field names MUST be validated against an allowlist — prevent field injection.

Invariant: explain: true MUST never reach production search queries.

18C. RESULT MAPPER SHAPE

Define how raw search engine responses are transformed to API response shapes.

SearchResult (raw from engine) → MappedSearchResult (returned to client):

SearchResult:

{

total: { value: number, relation: "eq" | "gte" },

hits: RawHit[],

facets?: Record<string, FacetBucket[]>,

took: number     // Engine response time in ms

}

RawHit:

{

_id: string,

_score: number,

_source: Record<string, unknown>,   // Raw indexed document

highlight?: Record<string, string[]>

}

ResultMapper interface:

interface ResultMapper<T> {

map(hit: RawHit): T                  // Map single hit to domain type

mapResult(raw: SearchResult): MappedSearchResult<T>

sanitize(doc: Record<string, unknown>): Record<string, unknown>

// Strip internal fields before returning

}

MappedSearchResult<T>:

{

total: number,

hasMore: boolean,        // total > (from + size)

items: T[],

facets?: Record<string, FacetBucket[]>,

debug?: { took: number } // Only included in non-production environments

}

Fields to STRIP before returning to client (never expose):

- tenantId (already scoped — don't echo)

- Internal metadata fields (_seq_no, _primary_term, routing)

- Fields tagged as INTERNAL or SENSITIVE in Section 07 data classification

Invariant: ResultMapper MUST strip internal/sensitive fields before serialization.

Invariant: ResultMapper MUST handle missing/null fields gracefully — never throw on partial documents.

Invariant: _score values MUST NOT be exposed in production API responses.

§12 — THIRD-PARTY INTEGRATIONS MAP

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Yes --- if external systems exist

[PURPOSE] → Define integration surface area,

idempotency guarantees, compensation

strategy, failure isolation, data

residency compliance, vendor governance,

lifecycle alignment across

Sections 01--11.

Do NOT choose vendor.

Do NOT write integration code.

Do NOT define credentials.

Do NOT assume SaaS availability.

COVERAGE LEVELS:

• Governance --- decisions & policies

• Operational --- runtime behavior

• Application --- what the agent builds

All decisions must reference:

• Section 03 --- Performance & availability

• Section 04 --- Cost projections

• Section 05 --- Architecture boundaries

• Section 06 --- Auth model

• Section 08 --- API contracts

• Section 09 --- Real-time architecture

• Section 10 --- File handling

• Section 11 --- Search & discovery

• Section 13 --- Async processing

• Section 18 --- Security

• Section 19 --- Privacy & governance

• Section 22 --- Resilience

• Section 23 --- Scaling

• Section 27 --- Observability

• Section 29 --- Data lifecycle

1\. INTEGRATION DECLARATION

ANY EXTERNAL INTEGRATIONS? (yes / no)

If No:

• Justification required

• Section marked complete

If Yes, categorize:

• Payments

• Email

• SMS

• Push notifications

• Identity provider / SSO

• Object storage

• Analytics

• CRM

• Accounting

• Maps / geolocation

• AI / ML provider

• Inbound webhooks

• Outbound webhooks

• Other:

For EACH integration define:

• Criticality:

critical / important / optional

• Direction:

inbound / outbound / bidirectional

• Sync or async?

• User-facing impact if unavailable:

• Compliance impact? (yes / no)

• Data sensitivity level:

public / internal /

confidential / sensitive

• PII involved? (yes / no)

• Tenant-scoped? (yes / no)

2\. INTEGRATION AUTHORITY MODEL

[GOVERNANCE]

For EACH integration define:

Is external system authoritative for:

• Identity state?

• Payment state?

• Subscription status?

• Billing totals?

• External records?

Conflict resolution rule:

• Local DB wins

• External system wins

• Version-based reconciliation

Primary system of record declared?

(yes / no)

Source of truth per domain:

• internal / external

• Sync direction:

push / pull / event-based

• Sync frequency:

real-time / near-real-time / batch

No dual-source ambiguity allowed.

Without authority model state drift

becomes inevitable.

3\. ARCHITECTURAL BOUNDARY

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

• Dedicated adapter layer required?

(yes / no)

• Vendor-specific logic allowed

outside adapter? (NO --- never)

• Integration calls allowed from:

adapter module only? (yes)

business layer? (no)

separate service? (optional)

• Provider-agnostic interface

defined? (yes / no)

• Multi-provider support planned?

(yes / no)

Vendor swap requires:

• Drop-in replacement

• Code change only

• Data migration required

• Architectural rewrite

(if rewrite → boundary failed)

VENDOR LOCK-IN ASSESSMENT

For EACH integration declare:

• Swap effort:

drop-in / code change /

data migration / rewrite

• Lock-in risk:

low / medium / high

• Alternative vendor exists?

(yes / no)

• Portability tested? (yes / no)

centralized / choreography / hybrid

(yes / no)

• Saga state persisted? (yes / no)

• Saga timeout: \_\_\_ minutes

• Partial completion visible

to user? (yes / no)

Without this, complex multi-step

flows produce inconsistent system

state under failure.

Must align with Section 13

(Async Processing).

5\. INTEGRATION EVENT STORM PROTECTION

[OPERATIONAL]

• Cross-integration event loop

detection? (yes / no)

• Max cascading integration

depth: \_\_\_

• Event deduplication across

integrations? (yes / no)

• Loop detection response:

break / alert / kill switch

• Event chain audit logged?

(yes / no)

Prevents: webhook triggers outbound

call triggers another webhook →

infinite loop that takes down

production.

6\. INTEGRATION REQUEST/RESPONSE

CONTRACT

[APPLICATION]

For EACH integration define:

• Request schema declared? (yes / no)

• Response schema declared? (yes / no)

• Error response schema declared?

(yes / no)

• Null / empty response handling:

fail / use default / log + continue

• Unexpected field handling:

strict reject / ignore / log

• Schema stored in:

code / schema registry / docs

• Schema version pinned? (yes / no)

Without declared contracts the

agent generates inconsistent

integration shapes across services.

7\. INTEGRATION STATE MODEL

[APPLICATION + OPERATIONAL]

Each integration exists in one of:

• active

• degraded (circuit half-open)

• suspended (circuit open)

• disabled (kill switch)

• deprecated (vendor sunset)

• offboarded (removed)

State transitions must be:

• Logged? (yes / no)

• Audited? (yes / no)

• Owner notified? (yes / no)

• Visible in ops dashboard?

(yes / no)

Without a declared state machine

agents build ad-hoc status flags

that become inconsistent in

production.

[APPLICATION]

• Integration initialization

order declared? (yes / no)

• Critical integrations block

app startup? (yes / no)

• Optional integrations fail

silently on startup? (yes / no)

• Startup timeout per

integration: \_\_\_ ms

• Partial startup allowed?

(yes / no)

• Startup order documented?

(yes / no)

Wrong order causes auth starting

before identity provider is ready

or payments before credential

store is available.

are prohibited.

14\. TIMEOUT AMBIGUITY RESOLUTION

[OPERATIONAL + APPLICATION]

For EACH integration call type

classify timeout semantics:

• safe-to-retry

(idempotent --- no side effects)

• unknown-state

(may or may not have executed)

• unsafe-to-retry

(non-idempotent --- must not retry)

For unknown-state timeouts:

• Reconciliation triggered?

(yes / no)

• Reconciliation SLA: \_\_\_ minutes

• User shown pending state?

(yes / no)

• Manual resolution required?

(yes / no)

Timeout ambiguity on payment

calls is one of the most dangerous

integration bugs in production.

Did the charge go through or not?

18. APPLICATION-LEVEL CONTRACTS

[Request/Response Contracts, Retry State, Health Checks, Local Cache, Init Order]

18A. REQUEST/RESPONSE CONTRACTS

Define the standard contract for all outbound third-party API calls.

OutboundRequest shape (all integrations must use this):

{

integrationId: string,    // Identifier for the integration (e.g., "stripe", "sendgrid")

method: "GET" | "POST" | "PUT" | "PATCH" | "DELETE",

url: string,

headers: Record<string, string>,

body?: unknown,

timeout: number,          // ms — integration-specific (see per-integration config)

idempotencyKey?: string,  // For non-idempotent mutations — send on retry

metadata: {               // For logging / tracing — NOT sent to external service

requestId: string,

tenantId?: string,

userId?: string,

triggeredBy: string     // "user_action" | "background_job" | "webhook" etc.

}

}

OutboundResponse shape:

{

statusCode: number,

body: unknown,

headers: Record<string, string>,

latencyMs: number,

integrationId: string,

requestId: string,

cached: boolean

}

Integration client interface:

interface IntegrationClient {

call(req: OutboundRequest): Promise<OutboundResponse>

callWithRetry(req: OutboundRequest, policy: RetryPolicy): Promise<OutboundResponse>

}

Invariant: All outbound calls MUST go through IntegrationClient — not raw HTTP clients.

Invariant: Credentials MUST be injected from secret store at request time — never hardcoded.

Invariant: Integration client MUST log request ID, integration ID, status code, and latency.

18B. RETRY STATE PERSISTENCE

Define how retry state is tracked for failed integration calls.

RetryRecord schema (persisted in DB or cache):

{

id: string,               // UUID

integrationId: string,

requestId: string,        // Correlation ID

idempotencyKey: string,   // Key to prevent duplicate effects on retry

payload: OutboundRequest, // Serialized request (encrypt if sensitive)

status: "pending" | "in_flight" | "succeeded" | "failed" | "dead",

attempts: number,

nextRetryAt: ISO8601,

lastError?: string,       // Truncated error message (no stack trace)

createdAt: ISO8601,

updatedAt: ISO8601,

expiresAt: ISO8601        // TTL — purge dead records after ___

}

RetryPolicy:

{

maxAttempts: number,

initialDelayMs: number,

backoffMultiplier: number,

maxDelayMs: number,

jitter: boolean,

retryOn: number[],        // HTTP status codes to retry (e.g., [429, 502, 503, 504])

doNotRetryOn: number[]    // e.g., [400, 401, 403, 404, 422] — client errors

}

Invariant: idempotencyKey MUST be generated once and reused across all retry attempts.

Invariant: Retry records with status "dead" MUST trigger an alert (requires human review).

Invariant: Sensitive request payloads in retry records MUST be encrypted at rest.

18C. HEALTH CHECK ENDPOINTS

Define health check contracts for each integration.

Per-integration health check:

interface IntegrationHealthCheck {

integrationId: string,

check(): Promise<HealthResult>

}

HealthResult:

{

integrationId: string,

status: "healthy" | "degraded" | "down",

latencyMs: number,

checkedAt: ISO8601,

detail?: string           // Error message if not healthy

}

Health check types per integration (declare for each):

- Shallow ping (is API reachable? — HTTP GET to /health or equivalent): ___

- Deep check (does auth credential work? — authenticated API call): ___

- Synthetic transaction (end-to-end test — create + delete test record): ___

Aggregated health endpoint (your service exposes this):

GET /health/integrations

Response:

{

overall: "healthy" | "degraded" | "down",

integrations: HealthResult[]

}

Health check cadence:

- Background poll every: ___ seconds

- Health check timeout: ___ ms (short — do NOT use same timeout as production calls)

- Circuit breaker threshold: ___ consecutive failures before opening

Invariant: Health checks MUST NOT perform write operations or consume paid API quota.

Invariant: Health check failures MUST update circuit breaker state (Section 22 resilience).

Invariant: Aggregated /health endpoint MUST be accessible to load balancer without auth.

18D. LOCAL CACHE OF EXTERNAL STATE

Define what external state is cached locally to reduce latency and blast radius.

For each integration, declare:

- What external data is cached: (e.g., Stripe customer ID, feature flags from LaunchDarkly)

- Cache TTL: ___

- Cache invalidation trigger: (TTL expiry only / webhook event / manual refresh)

- Stale-while-revalidate allowed: (yes / no)

- Cache miss behavior: (fetch live / use default / fail open / fail closed)

- Cache store: (in-memory / Redis / DB — state choice)

IntegrationCache interface:

interface IntegrationCache {

get<T>(integrationId: string, key: string): Promise<T | null>

set<T>(integrationId: string, key: string, value: T, ttl: number): Promise<void>

invalidate(integrationId: string, key: string): Promise<void>

invalidateByTenant(tenantId: string): Promise<void>

}

Invariant: Cached credentials / tokens MUST NOT be logged or included in error reports.

Invariant: Cache miss MUST NOT cause a synchronous blocking call in a user-facing request

(use background refresh or accept stale) — unless the data is strictly required.

Invariant: Cache entries MUST be tenant-scoped where data is tenant-specific.

18E. STARTUP INITIALIZATION ORDER

Define the exact sequence in which integrations are initialized at service startup.

Integration startup sequence:

1. Load all integration credentials from secret store (fail-fast if any missing)

2. Initialize DB connection pool (Section 07 §21C)

3. Initialize local cache layer

4. Initialize circuit breakers (set to CLOSED state)

5. Run integration health checks (shallow ping for each)

6. Mark integrations as AVAILABLE or DEGRADED based on health check results

7. Start background retry processor (for pending RetryRecords)

8. Emit "integrations:ready" signal

9. Accept inbound traffic

Startup failure policy (per integration):

Declare for each integration whether it is REQUIRED or OPTIONAL at startup:

- REQUIRED: service refuses to start if this integration is unhealthy

(e.g., primary payment processor)

- OPTIONAL: service starts in degraded mode; feature depending on integration is disabled

(e.g., optional enrichment service)

Invariant: Service MUST NOT accept traffic before step 8.

Invariant: REQUIRED integration failures MUST produce a startup error with integration name

and health check result in the error message.

Invariant: Startup initialization MUST be idempotent (safe to run multiple times —

e.g., on container restart).

2\. DELIVERY SEMANTICS

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Global delivery model declared:

• At-most-once

• At-least-once

• Effectively-once

(idempotent handler required)

Exactly-once across distributed

systems is prohibited unless

formally proven.

For EACH workload:

• Handler idempotent? (yes / no)

• Idempotency key required?

(yes / no)

• Idempotency storage duration:

\_\_\_ hours

• Duplicate processing tolerated?

(yes / no)

Retries without idempotency

are prohibited.

ACKNOWLEDGMENT STRATEGY

• Message ack timing:

ack after DB commit? (yes / no)

ack before commit? (prohibited)

two-phase commit? (yes / no)

• Failure between commit and ack:

idempotency handles duplication?

(yes / no)

• Ack failure retried? (yes / no)

Ack before DB commit = message

lost on crash.

Crash between commit and ack =

duplicate processing.

Without declaring ack timing

the durability model is incomplete.

Agents get this wrong by default.

3\. IDEMPOTENCY STORAGE GOVERNANCE

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

Idempotency store:

• DB / cache / hybrid

Durability tier: \_\_\_

TTL must be ≥ message retention.

(TTL \< retention = unsafe replay)

Idempotency store outage behavior:

• Block processing? (yes / no)

• Process without protection?

(NO --- never)

• Degrade workload? (yes / no)

Idempotency conflict rate

monitored? (yes / no)

IDEMPOTENCY VS REPLAY GUARANTEE

• Replay allowed after idempotency

TTL expiry? (yes / no)

If yes:

• Replay restricted to safe

workloads only? (yes / no)

• Manual override required?

(yes / no)

If no:

• Replay blocked once idempotency

record expired? (yes / no)

Replay at day 6.9 with 7-day TTL

produces duplicate processing at

day 7.1 when idempotency record

expires. Declare this boundary

explicitly.

JOB DEDUPLICATION MODEL

• Deduplication at enqueue time?

(yes / no)

• Deduplication window: \_\_\_ seconds

• Deduplication key source:

payload hash / explicit key / both

• Duplicate enqueue behavior:

reject / accept silently /

return existing job ID

• Deduplication scope:

per-tenant / global

Idempotency = prevents duplicate

processing.

Deduplication = prevents duplicate

enqueueing.

These are different problems

requiring different solutions.

28\. CROSS-SECTION ENFORCEMENT

[GOVERNANCE]

1. DESIGN SYSTEM DECISION

- Library name & version:

- Customization scope: (tokens only / component overrides / full fork)

- Upgrade strategy: (pin version / track minor / track major)

Design system ownership:

- Who owns design system decisions: (design lead / frontend lead / shared)

- Design system lives in: (monorepo / separate package / Figma tokens only)

2. DESIGN TOKEN SYSTEM

- Primary brand color: ___

- Secondary color: ___

- Neutral scale (50/100/200/.../900): ___

- Border colors: default / focus / error

- Dark mode support: (yes / no)

If yes: token values defined for both modes

- Font family: primary / mono / display

- Letter spacing: tight / normal / wide

- none / sm / md / lg / xl / full

- sm / md / lg / xl / none

- Tablet: ___ px — ___ px

- Desktop: > ___ px

- Wide: > ___ px (if applicable)

- Delivery: (CSS variables / Tailwind config / JS object / all)

- Session expired state

- Maintenance mode page

Empty state hierarchy:

1. No data ever created → onboarding CTA

2. All items filtered out → "Clear filters" CTA

3. Search returned nothing → suggestion to broaden search

4. Error loading data → retry button + error message

- Live region announcements for async results: (yes / no)

- Landmark roles used (main / nav / aside / footer): (yes / no)

- Form field labels always visible (not placeholder-only): (yes — required)

Color contrast:

- Normal text: minimum 4.5:1 contrast ratio

- Large text (18pt+): minimum 3:1 contrast ratio

- Interactive element borders: minimum 3:1 against background

- Color NOT used as sole differentiator: (yes — required)

Touch targets (mobile):

- Minimum tap target size: 44x44px (Apple HIG) / 48x48dp (Material)

Invariant: Design system MUST include accessibility review as part of component sign-off.

Invariant: New components MUST NOT ship without keyboard navigation and ARIA attributes.
