§15 — FRONTEND ARCHITECTURE & STATE MANAGEMENT

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No

[PURPOSE] → Define the frontend application structure,

state management model, data fetching strategy,

routing contract, code splitting plan, and

client-side error handling.

Do NOT choose specific libraries here (unless already decided in Section 05).

Do NOT write component code.

Define the architecture contracts only — where state lives,

how data flows, how routing is structured, and how errors surface.

All decisions must reference:

- Section 05 --- Architecture style & platform decision

- Section 06 --- Auth model & token strategy

- Section 07 --- Data entities

- Section 08 --- API contracts

- Section 09 --- Real-time events (if applicable)

- Section 16 --- Component library

- Section 03 --- Performance requirements

1. RENDERING STRATEGY

Select rendering model (per surface):

- CSR (Client-Side Rendering): SPA, no SSR

- SSR (Server-Side Rendering): HTML on every request

- SSG (Static Site Generation): pre-rendered at build time

- ISR (Incremental Static Regeneration): SSG + background revalidation

- Hybrid: different strategies per route

Declare per route category:

- Marketing / landing pages: ___

- Auth pages (login / signup): ___

- Dashboard / app pages: ___

- Public content pages: ___

- Admin pages: ___

SEO requirement: (yes → must use SSR/SSG for public pages / no → CSR acceptable)

Time-to-first-byte target: ___ ms (from Section 03)

2. APPLICATION SHELL & ROUTING

Router type: (file-based / code-defined / hybrid)

Route categories:

- Public routes (no auth required): list

- Protected routes (auth required): list

- Admin routes (admin role required): list

- Tenant-scoped routes (tenantId in URL or context): list

Route structure convention:

- URL pattern: (flat / nested / tenant-prefixed e.g. /[tenantSlug]/dashboard)

- Dynamic segments naming: (camelCase / kebab-case)

- Query params for: (filters / pagination / sort / tab state)

- Hash for: (in-page anchor / modal state / none)

Navigation guards:

- Auth check: (client-side redirect / server-side / middleware)

- Role check: (client-side guard / server-side / both)

- Tenant check: (embedded in guard / separate middleware)

- Redirect after login: (to intended URL / fixed dashboard / role-based)

Route-level code splitting:

- Split at: (every route / grouped by feature / manual)

- Prefetch strategy: (on hover / on viewport / on idle / none)

- Loading fallback: (skeleton / spinner / previous page stays visible)

3. STATE MANAGEMENT ARCHITECTURE

State categories (define where each lives):

SERVER STATE (data from API — use data-fetching library):

- Caching layer: (React Query / SWR / Apollo / RTK Query / custom)

- Cache key strategy: (entity-based / URL-based / custom)

- Stale time: ___ ms (how long cached data is considered fresh)

- Background refetch: (yes / no)

- Optimistic updates: (yes / no — if yes, rollback strategy)

- Pagination model: (cursor / offset / infinite scroll)

- Mutation + cache invalidation pattern: declare per entity

CLIENT/UI STATE (ephemeral — does not sync to server):

- Tool: (useState / useReducer / Zustand / Jotai / Valtio / Context)

- Examples: modal open/close, sidebar collapsed, selected tab, form draft

AUTH STATE (session / identity):

- Stored in: (React context / Zustand store / cookie / server session)

- Refresh trigger: (expiry timer / 401 interceptor / both)

- Global logout handler: declared in Section 06 §18B

URL STATE (shareable / bookmarkable):

- What lives in URL: (filters / pagination / selected item ID / sort)

- Sync strategy: (read from URL on mount, write on change)

FORM STATE:

- Form library: (React Hook Form / Formik / uncontrolled / custom)

- Validation library: (Zod / Yup / custom)

- Draft persistence: (localStorage / sessionStorage / none — state only)

Invariant: Server state MUST NOT be duplicated into a separate client store.

Use the data-fetching library's cache as the single source of truth for server data.

Invariant: Auth state MUST be cleared completely on logout — no stale identity in any store.

4. DATA FETCHING CONTRACT

API client layer:

- Base URL configuration: (env var / runtime config)

- Auth header injection: (interceptor / per-request / automatic from store)

- Token refresh interceptor: (yes — see Section 06 §18B / no)

- Request timeout: ___ ms

- Retry on network error: (yes — N times / no)

- Error normalization: (transform all API errors to standard shape before reaching UI)

Standard fetch patterns (declare for each):

- Single entity fetch: GET /entity/:id → cache by [entityType, id]

- List fetch with filters: GET /entities?filters → cache by [entityType, filters]

- Paginated fetch: cursor or offset strategy (Section 08)

- Mutation: POST/PATCH/DELETE → invalidate related cache keys

- Infinite scroll: accumulate pages in single cache entry

Loading & error states:

- Every async boundary must show: (loading state / error state / both)

- Global error boundary: (yes — catch unexpected errors / no)

- Per-query error handling: (inline message / toast / redirect)

5. REAL-TIME STATE INTEGRATION

(Skip if Section 09 is not applicable)

WebSocket / SSE event → state update contract:

- Event received → update server state cache (not separate store)

- Conflict resolution: (server wins / merge / last-write-wins)

- Optimistic update + real-time update conflict: declare resolution strategy

- Connection status UI: (show "reconnecting" banner / silent / icon only)

- Missed events on reconnect: (refetch full state / apply delta / both)

6. CLIENT-SIDE ERROR HANDLING

Error boundary strategy:

- Root error boundary: catches unhandled render errors → shows error page

- Route-level error boundary: catches errors within a route → shows route error state

- Component-level error boundary: for isolated widgets that must not crash the page

Error categories and UI response:

- Network error (no connection): (offline banner / retry button)

- 401 Unauthorized: (redirect to login with return URL)

- 403 Forbidden: (show permission denied state — do NOT redirect)

- 404 Not Found: (show not found state or redirect to 404 page)

- 422 Validation: (show field-level errors from server response)

- 429 Rate Limited: (show "try again in X seconds" message)

- 500 Server Error: (show generic error with error ID for support)

- Timeout: (show timeout message + retry option)

Error reporting:

- Client errors sent to: (Sentry / Datadog RUM / custom / none)

- PII scrubbing before sending: (yes — required / no)

- Error ID shown to user: (yes — for support reference / no)

- Console errors in production: (suppressed / allowed)

7. PERFORMANCE ARCHITECTURE

Bundle optimization:

- Code splitting: (route-level / component-level / both)

- Tree shaking: (enabled by build tool — confirm)

- Dynamic imports for: (heavy libraries / chart libraries / rich text editors)

- Bundle size budget per chunk: ___ KB (gzipped)

Image optimization:

- Format: (WebP / AVIF with fallback / original)

- Lazy loading: (yes — all below-fold images)

- Responsive images: (srcset / next/image / manual)

- Placeholder: (blur hash / LQIP / skeleton / none)

Web Vitals targets (align with Section 03):

- LCP (Largest Contentful Paint): < ___ ms

- FID / INP: < ___ ms

- CLS (Cumulative Layout Shift): < ___

8. APPLICATION-LEVEL CONTRACTS

[Store Interface, API Client, Route Guard]

8A. STORE INTERFACE

ClientStore interface (UI state only):

interface UIStore {

// Sidebar

sidebarOpen: boolean

setSidebarOpen(open: boolean): void

// Modals

activeModal: string | null

openModal(id: string, props?: unknown): void

closeModal(): void

// Toast / Notifications

toasts: Toast[]

addToast(toast: ToastInput): void

removeToast(id: string): void

// Theme

theme: 'light' | 'dark' | 'system'

setTheme(theme: string): void

}

8B. API CLIENT CONTRACT

interface APIClient {

get<T>(path: string, opts?: RequestOpts): Promise<T>

post<T>(path: string, body: unknown, opts?: RequestOpts): Promise<T>

put<T>(path: string, body: unknown, opts?: RequestOpts): Promise<T>

patch<T>(path: string, body: unknown, opts?: RequestOpts): Promise<T>

delete<T>(path: string, opts?: RequestOpts): Promise<T>

}

RequestOpts:

{

signal?: AbortSignal,     // For cancellation

headers?: Record<string, string>,

skipAuth?: boolean,       // For public endpoints

timeout?: number          // Override default timeout

}

All methods: normalize errors to APIError before throwing:

{

status: number,

code: string,             // Machine-readable from server

message: string,          // Human-readable

fieldErrors?: Record<string, string>  // For 422 validation

}

8C. ROUTE GUARD CONTRACT

interface RouteGuard {

canActivate(route: RouteConfig, context: AuthContext): GuardResult

}

GuardResult:

| { allowed: true }

| { allowed: false; redirect: string; reason: string }

AuthContext:

{

isAuthenticated: boolean,

user: User | null,

roles: string[],

tenantId: string | null,

permissions: string[]

}

§16 — RATE LIMITING, THROTTLING

& RESOURCE GOVERNANCE

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Always

(every production system

requires resource governance)

[PURPOSE] → Define rate limits, quotas,

throttling rules, enforcement

architecture, resource isolation,

fairness enforcement, abuse

prevention, cost containment,

bot detection, graduated penalties,

cross-region coordination,

time source governance,

absolute safety caps,

cap priority ordering,

config rollback safety,

shadow mode rollout,

unified cross-channel quotas,

and cross-layer backpressure

alignment across Sections 01--13.

Do NOT choose vendor.

Do NOT write middleware code.

Do NOT assume specific gateway.

COVERAGE LEVELS:

• Governance --- decisions & policies

• Operational --- runtime behavior

• Application --- what the agent builds

All decisions must reference:

• Section 03 --- Performance

• Section 04 --- Cost

• Section 05 --- Architecture

• Section 09 --- Real-time

• Section 10 --- Files

• Section 11 --- Search

• Section 12 --- Integrations

• Section 13 --- Async

• Section 18 --- Security

• Section 22 --- Resilience

• Section 23 --- Scaling

• Section 27 --- Observability

1\. GOVERNANCE MODEL

[GOVERNANCE]

Rate limiting applied at:

• API layer? (yes / no)

• Authentication layer? (yes / no)

• Async enqueue layer? (yes / no)

• Integration outbound layer?

(yes / no)

• File upload layer? (yes / no)

• Search query layer? (yes / no)

Unified rate governance policy

declared? (yes / no)

Without unified governance limits

conflict across layers and create

bypass opportunities.

2\. TIME SOURCE GOVERNANCE

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Canonical time source:

• NTP-synchronized cluster clock

• External time authority

• Region-local system clock

Max tolerated clock skew: \_\_\_ ms

If skew exceeds threshold:

• Alert? (yes / no)

• Degrade to approximate

counter? (yes / no)

• Block strict enforcement?

(yes / no)

Canonical time source used for:

• Sliding window boundaries

• Retry-After calculation

• Cross-region counter sync

• Penalty reset windows

• Soft limit warning reset

• Token bucket refill timing

• Reset storm jitter calculation

Without canonical time source

rate limits become nondeterministic

across regions and distributed

nodes. Every time-dependent

feature in this section depends

on this declaration.

3\. RATE UNIT STANDARDIZATION

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

All limits expressed in one

canonical unit:

• requests per second (preferred)

• requests per minute

• standardized ISO rate format

One unit used consistently across:

• Enforcement layer

• Response headers

• API documentation

• SDK backoff handler

• Cross-region sync

• Config management

• Billing and cost tracking

Unit normalization enforced

internally? (yes / no)

Documentation exposes unified

format? (yes / no)

Headers use same unit as

enforcement? (yes / no)

SDK uses same unit as headers?

(yes / no)

Mixed units across teams produce

mismatched SDK implementations,

wrong Retry-After calculations,

and cross-region sync bugs.

4\. WINDOW RESET SEMANTICS

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Window model declared:

• Fixed window

• Rolling window

• Token bucket refill

• Leaky bucket drain

Reset behavior:

• Full reset at boundary

• Gradual decay

• Continuous refill

Retry-After based on:

• Remaining window time

• Token refill rate

Fixed window creates burst

oscillation at boundary.

User sends 100 requests at 11:59.

Window resets at 12:00.

User sends 100 more at 12:00.

200 requests in 2 seconds with

no limit violation declared.

Rolling window or token bucket

prevents this entirely.

5\. ABSOLUTE SAFETY CAPS

[GOVERNANCE]

Hard maximum values that cannot

be exceeded regardless of any

other config, override, or

emergency adjustment:

• Hard max RPS per tenant: \_\_\_

• Hard max RPS per user: \_\_\_

• Hard max RPS per API key: \_\_\_

• Hard max async enqueue

per minute: \_\_\_

• Hard max WebSocket connections

per tenant: \_\_\_

• Hard max file upload

per minute: \_\_\_

These values:

• Cannot be overridden by

config? (yes --- always)

• Cannot be overridden by

per-tenant override? (yes --- always)

• Require code change to

modify? (yes --- always)

• Require security review to

modify? (yes / no)

Protects against:

• Config mistake setting limit

to 0 (full outage)

• Config mistake setting limit

to unlimited (cost explosion)

• Malicious override attempt

6\. CAP PRIORITY ORDER

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

When limits conflict the following

priority order always applies

(highest = wins):

1\. Absolute safety caps

(Section 05 --- never overridden)

2\. Global system caps

(Section 21)

3\. Escalation-adjusted limits

(Escalation Model in Section 30

of this document)

4\. Tier subscription limits

(Section 16)

5\. Per-tenant overrides

6\. Burst allowances

Higher priority cap always wins?

(yes --- always)

If global cap \< sum of all

tenant safety caps:

• Global cap enforced first?

(yes --- always)

• Per-tenant caps enforced

within global cap? (yes / no)

Without declared priority order

enforcement layers disagree and

the higher cap wins by accident.

This is a configuration conflict

that is impossible to debug

without a declared hierarchy.

(yes / no)

service token

cap priority order? (yes / no)

Without declaring enforcement layer

agent builds rate limiting in the

wrong place or in multiple

conflicting places simultaneously.

RESET STORM PROTECTION

window start? (yes / no)

• Global throttle active during

first \_\_\_ seconds post-reset?

(yes / no)

• Throttle level during ramp-up:

\_\_\_% of normal cap

System outage causes counter reset.

All tenants retry simultaneously

at window start.

Thundering herd takes system down

again immediately after recovery.

This is a documented production

failure pattern at scale.

C1 CONTRADICTION FIX --- GLOBAL CAP TENANT ISOLATION INVARIANT

GLOBAL CAP TENANT ISOLATION INVARIANT

Global system cap is a CEILING applied AFTER per-tenant allocation

enforcement. Tenant allocations within the global cap are isolated.

Tenant A exhausting its allocation cannot consume Tenant B's allocation.

Enforcement order:

1\. Per-tenant allocation enforced first (isolated per credential +

tenant)

2\. Global cap enforced as aggregate ceiling

3\. No cross-tenant sharing of burst allocation (yes --- always)

Compromised tenant credential cannot exhaust global quota beyond that

tenant's own allocation. Cross-references Section 18 blast radius rate

isolation.

42\. RATE LIMITING ASSUMPTIONS

C3 CONTRADICTION FIX --- SECURITY RATE LIMIT PROTECTED TIER

SECURITY RATE LIMIT PROTECTED TIER

Rate limits declared in Section 18 for auth endpoints constitute a

PROTECTED TIER within this section's enforcement infrastructure.

Protected tier properties:

• Cannot be modified by standard rate config changes

• Cannot be overridden by operator config or shadow mode rollout

• Changes require: security team approval + compliance review +

explicit override (not standard config change)

Protected limits: login per IP / login per user / MFA attempts /

password reset / token refresh.

C4 CONTRADICTION FIX --- RATE LIMIT SERVICE FAILURE AUTH ENDPOINT

BEHAVIOR

RATE LIMIT SERVICE FAILURE --- AUTH ENDPOINT FALLBACK

If rate limit enforcement service fails completely:

• Auth endpoints apply hardcoded minimum safe limits (FAIL-CLOSED, not

fail-open)

• Hardcoded fallback limits declared: \_\_\_ (most restrictive safe

value, not zero, not unlimited)

• Fallback audit logged immediately (yes --- always)

• Security alert fired immediately (yes --- always)

• Recovery SLA: \_\_\_ minutes

Fail-open on auth endpoints is prohibited (aligns with Section 18

fail-open prohibition) even during rate limit service failure.

[CRITICAL] --- breaks security

or fairness

[IMPORTANT] --- impacts cost or scale

[MINOR] --- adjustable

§17 — DATA INTEGRITY &

TRANSACTION BOUNDARIES

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Always

[PURPOSE] → Define transactional

guarantees, consistency model,

atomicity boundaries,

aggregate ownership,

entity lifecycle, bulk operations,

outbox contracts, schema drift,

data sovereignty, tombstone model,

read consistency, saga compensation

ownership, and failure handling

across Sections 01--14.

Do NOT choose database vendor.

Do NOT assume ACID across services.

Do NOT assume single-node architecture.

1\. SYSTEM CONSISTENCY MODEL

[GOVERNANCE]

• Strong consistency

• Eventual consistency

• Hybrid (declare per domain)

• Single entity level? (yes / no)

• Cross-entity level? (yes / no)

• Cross-service level? (yes / no)

• Cross-region level? (yes / no)

If hybrid, for EACH domain declare:

• Consistency type

• Acceptable staleness: \_\_\_ ms

• Read-after-write guarantee?

(yes / no)

• Monotonic read guarantee?

(yes / no)

Without declared model engineers

assume strong consistency

everywhere and build unsafe flows

on eventual stores.

[TRACK] → Both

rate isolation, correlation

response blast radius,

across Sections 01--15.

Assume supply chain compromise.

of this document is violated.

6\. TOKEN TYPE SECURITY MODEL

(yes / no)

• DB lookup per request? (yes / no)

• Lookup cached? (yes / no)

• Cache TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

JWT SIGNING KEY ROTATION

• Key overlap window: \_\_\_ minutes

• Old key accepted for:

\_\_\_ minutes after rotation

• JWKS cache TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

• Forced cache purge on

emergency rotation? (yes / no)

⚠ CRITICAL CONSTRAINT:

Key overlap window MUST be ≤

max revocation window.

If key overlap \> max revocation

window then a revoked token

signed by the old key remains

valid via the overlap window.

This silently defeats revocation.

Declare both values and enforce

the relationship explicitly.

revocation window?

17\. SIGNING KEY DOMAIN SEPARATION

[GOVERNANCE]

INVARIANT --- must never be violated:

Audit log signing key CANNOT

sign application artifacts.

(yes --- enforced always)

Artifact signing key CANNOT

sign audit logs.

(yes --- enforced always)

JWT signing key CANNOT sign

audit logs or artifacts.

(yes --- enforced always)

Each key domain is separate:

• Audit log signing key:

purpose = audit only

stored in: HSM (required)

• Artifact signing key:

purpose = artifacts only

stored in: HSM (required)

• JWT signing key:

purpose = tokens only

stored in: HSM / secret manager

Key domain cross-use detected?

(yes / no --- monitoring required)

Cross-use triggers:

immediate security alert

Single key compromise escalating

across all three domains

simultaneously = catastrophic

loss of audit trail integrity

AND artifact integrity AND

authentication integrity.

Domain separation is an

absolute invariant.

24\. DEGRADED MODE SECURITY INVARIANT

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

INVARIANT --- must never be violated:

Security degraded mode MUST NOT

weaken any of the following:

• Authentication? (must not weaken)

• Authorization? (must not weaken)

• Encryption? (must not weaken)

• Tenant isolation? (must not weaken)

• Rate limiting? (must not weaken)

• Audit logging? (must not weaken)

• Erasure job processing? (must not disable --- GDPR SLA at risk)

• Right to restriction enforcement? (must not disable)

• Consent withdrawal propagation? (must not disable)

C2 CONTRADICTION FIX --- PRIVACY CONTROLS IN DEGRADED MODE:

If degraded mode would pause erasure jobs: check remaining SLA. If SLA

\< \_\_\_ days erasure takes priority over degradation. Alert compliance

team immediately. Escalate to incident.

Privacy controls are legally mandated. They cannot be deprioritized in

degraded mode. Cross-references Section 19 erasure SLA and right to

restriction.

Degraded mode must:

• Reduce attack surface

• Shed non-critical features

• Never relax security controls

Permitted in degraded mode:

• Disable non-critical UI features

• Reduce throughput

• Queue non-urgent writes

• Return 503 for non-essential

endpoints

Prohibited in degraded mode:

• Skip auth checks to

reduce latency

• Disable encryption for

performance

• Relax tenant isolation

• Disable rate limiting

• Stop audit logging

If degraded mode implementation

would require weakening any

security control:

• Reject the degradation?

(yes --- always)

• Alert ops? (yes --- always)

• Escalate to incident? (yes / no)

Degraded mode that disables

auth is not a degraded mode.

It is a security incident.

1\. DATA CLASSIFICATION TAXONOMY

[GOVERNANCE]

All data classified into

declared tiers:

TIER 1 --- PUBLIC

• Definition: intentionally

exposed, no restriction

• Examples: marketing content,

public API docs, anonymized

aggregates

• Encryption at rest: optional

• Cross-region: allowed

• Retention: unlimited

• Subject to erasure: no

TIER 2 --- INTERNAL

• Definition: internal use,

not external exposure

• Examples: system logs without

PII, performance metrics,

internal configs

• Encryption at rest: required

• Cross-region: allowed with

controls

• Retention: declared per type

TIER 3 --- CONFIDENTIAL

• Definition: business-sensitive,

tenant data, financial records

• Examples: tenant configs,

billing records, API usage

• Encryption at rest: required

• Application-layer encryption:

required

• Cross-region: restricted

• Retention: declared per type

TIER 4 --- RESTRICTED (PII)

• Definition: identifies or

can identify a natural person

• Examples: declared in Section 02

• Encryption at rest: required

• Application-layer encryption:

required

• Field-level encryption:

required for Tier 5 subclass

• Cross-region: jurisdiction-locked

• Retention: legally constrained

• Subject to GDPR erasure: yes

TIER 5 --- SENSITIVE PII

• Definition: PII with heightened

legal protection

• Examples: health data, financial

data, biometric data, children's

data, criminal records,

political beliefs, religion,

sexual orientation

• Encryption: field-level always

• Cross-region: prohibited unless

explicit legal basis declared

• Retention: minimum necessary

• Deletion: immediate on request

Classification applied at:

• Data model level? (yes / no)

• Field level? (yes / no)

• Collection level? (yes / no)

• API response level? (yes / no)

• Read model level? (yes / no)

• Async payload level? (yes / no)

• Outbox payload level? (yes / no)

• Analytics pipeline level?

(yes / no)

• Error log level? (yes / no)

Unclassified data defaults to:

Tier 3 (never defaults to public)

2\. PII TAXONOMY

[GOVERNANCE]

Resolves Section 18 open

constraint: PII definition.

PII declared as any of:

• Full name

• Email address

• Phone number

• Physical address

• IP address (Tier 4 in most

jurisdictions)

• Device ID / cookie ID

• User ID (if linkable to person)

• Behavioral data (if linkable)

• Location data

• Session fingerprint data

(device / user-agent + IP)

• JIT access log identifiers

• Error log context with

user identifiers

• Biometric data (Tier 5)

• Health / medical data (Tier 5)

• Financial account data (Tier 5)

• Government ID numbers (Tier 5)

• Children's data (Tier 5)

• Race / ethnicity (Tier 5)

• Political / religious beliefs

(Tier 5)

• Sexual orientation (Tier 5)

PII taxonomy declared in data

model? (yes / no)

Each PII field tagged in schema?

(yes / no)

PII field registry maintained?

(yes / no)

New field classification review

required? (yes / no)

3\. PSEUDONYMIZATION VS ANONYMIZATION

TECHNICAL DECLARATION

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

PSEUDONYMIZATION:

• Definition: replace identifier

with token, mapping stored

separately

• Still counts as PII? YES

• Still subject to GDPR? YES

• Re-identification possible

with key? YES

• Use case: audit logs, analytics

that need re-identification

capability for compliance

ANONYMIZATION:

• Definition: irreversible removal

of identifying information,

no mapping stored

• Still counts as PII? NO

• Subject to GDPR? NO

• Re-identification possible? NO

• Use case: analytics aggregates,

public reporting, cross-region

transfer

For EACH processing activity

declare which technique:

• Audit log PII after deletion:

pseudonymization (must retain

audit capability)

• Analytics pipeline:

anonymization (for cross-region

and GDPR exemption)

• Error log PII on retention

expiry: anonymization or

physical deletion

• Session log IP on retention

expiry: anonymization

Pseudonymized data where

anonymization is needed =

data still counts as PII

= GDPR obligations remain.

Anonymized data where

pseudonymization is needed =

re-identification impossible

= compliance audit trail broken.

Agent must implement each

correctly.

6\. PURPOSE LIMITATION ENFORCEMENT

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

GDPR Article 5(1)(b):

Data collected for one purpose

cannot be used for another

without new legal basis.

This is SEPARATE from

data minimization.

Minimization = collect only

what you need.

Limitation = use only for

declared purpose.

For EACH data field declare:

• Permitted purposes: \_\_\_

• Prohibited purposes: \_\_\_

• New purpose requires: new

consent / legal basis review /

DPA amendment

Technical enforcement:

• Purpose tag on each field?

(yes / no)

• Processing system declares

purpose at query time?

(yes / no)

• Purpose mismatch blocked?

(yes / no)

• Purpose mismatch logged?

(yes / no)

• Purpose mismatch alert?

(yes / no)

Example:

Billing email collected for

contract performance.

Using billing email for

marketing = purpose violation

without new consent.

Must be technically blocked

not just policy-declared.

• Immutable (Section 18)

• May contain PII (Section 19)

(yes / no)

2\. After user deletion:

PII pseudonymized in

security audit log? (yes / no)

authorized modification

(not tamper)? (yes --- always)

by: compliance role only

5\. Pseudonymization itself

audit logged in separate

(yes --- always)

6\. Security team notified?

(yes / no)

(yes / no)

• Regulatory override exists?

(yes --- required)

(yes --- always)

• DEK per user/tenant? (yes / no)

• DEK deletion = unreadable?

(yes / no)

• DEK deletion audit logged?

(yes --- always)

• DEK deletion verified? (yes / no)

C5 CONTRADICTION FIX --- ERASURE PROPAGATION CHAIN CONSTRAINT

ERASURE PROPAGATION CHAIN CONSTRAINT (resolves Section 17 consistency

SLA vs Section 19 GDPR 30-day SLA conflict):

Erasure must propagate to ALL stores within the 30-day SLA. No store may

lag beyond this window. For each store declare:

• Max propagation time to this store: \_\_\_

• Store confirms erasure? (yes / no) --- method: callback / polling /

verification job

If any store cannot confirm erasure within SLA: block data serving from

that store immediately. Alert compliance team. Escalate if confirmation

not received within \_\_\_ hours before SLA breach.

purged? (yes / no)

• Undelivered outbox entries:

cancel delivery / deliver then

purge / purge immediately

(declare)

• PII in outbox scrubbed on

erasure? (yes / no)

If outbox retention \> erasure SLA:

• This is a GDPR violation

• Must reduce retention OR

implement PII scrubbing

on erasure

12\. SCHEMA MIGRATION PII TREATMENT

• Both old and new schema

hold same PII? (yes / no)

level matches new schema?

(yes / no)

• If old schema has weaker

encryption: old schema

fields upgraded before

dual-write? (yes / no)

• PII duplication window: \_\_\_

hours (must be minimized)

• Erasure during dual-write:

applies to both schemas?

(yes --- always)

• Cutover removes old schema

PII immediately? (yes / no)

• Old schema PII verified

deleted after cutover?

(yes / no)

CROSS-TENANT ANALYTICS ISOLATION

Resolves gap 12.

anonymization (not

be disaggregated to identify

individual tenant data?

(yes / no --- must verify)

size before aggregation

is published)

Cross-tenant analytics before

anonymization = one tenant's

user behavior influences

another tenant's aggregate =

cross-tenant PII leakage.

separately? (yes / no)

(yes --- always)

from erasure? (yes / no)

(yes / no)

RIGHT TO RESTRICTION

TECHNICAL IMPLEMENTATION

Resolves gap 13.

Restriction means:

data retained but all processing

halted for that data subject.

Technical implementation:

• Restriction flag per

user/entity? (yes / no)

• Flag checked by:

API layer? (yes / no)

Search? (yes / no)

Analytics pipeline? (yes / no)

Async workers? (yes / no)

Integration outbound? (yes / no)

• Restriction flag propagated

to all services? (yes / no)

• Propagation SLA: \_\_\_ ms

• Restricted data returned

in API responses? (must be no)

• Restricted data included in

analytics? (must be no)

• Processing of restricted data

triggers alert? (yes / no)

• Restriction lifted by:

user request / legal basis

change / court order

Restriction declared but not

technically enforced = right

to restriction is not real.

→ PII definition → Section 18

(resolved)

→ Backup erasure → Section 17

(resolved)

→ Sovereignty → Section 17

(resolved)

→ Async PII → Section 13

(resolved)

→ Tombstone PII → Section 17

(new constraint resolved)

→ Outbox PII → Section 17

(new constraint resolved)

→ Read model PII → Section 17

(new constraint resolved)

→ Security log PII → Section 18

(new constraint resolved)

§20 — COMPLIANCE & LEGAL

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Always

[PURPOSE] → Define terms of service,

acceptable use policy,

licensing model,

intellectual property,

liability limits,

export controls,

age restrictions,

accessibility compliance,

regulatory licenses,

communications compliance,

content moderation liability,

legal document management,

legal entity structure,

AI regulatory exposure,

and compliance audit trail

across all jurisdictions

the app operates in.

Do NOT assume single jurisdiction.

Do NOT assume legal = privacy.

(Privacy is Section 19.)

(This section = everything else.)

Do NOT skip if MVP.

Basic legal posture required

even on Fast Track.

Assume regulators will audit.

Assume users will sue.

Assume IP will be contested.

Assume accessibility will be tested.

Assume sanctions lists will change.

Assume AI regulation will tighten.

All decisions must reference:

• Section 01 --- Product & Business

(jurisdiction, business model,

target users)

• Section 06 --- Auth

(age gate before account creation,

session invalidation on ToS

non-acceptance)

• Section 18 --- Security & Trust

(SBOM must reconcile with OSS

inventory declared here,

audit log tamper protection,

legal hold vs backup purge)

• Section 19 --- Privacy & Data

(GDPR / CCPA / HIPAA --- Section 19

owns those. Section 20 owns

everything else legally.

Data controller per region

must align with DPA structure.)

• Section 27 --- Observability

(compliance audit trails)

• Section 29 --- Data Lifecycle

(legal hold overrides all

automated purge jobs here)

• Section 30 --- Testing

(accessibility testing)

1\. TERMS OF SERVICE & ACCEPTABLE USE

[GOVERNANCE]

Terms of Service (ToS):

Published? (yes --- always)

Location: /terms (standard)

Versioned? (yes --- always)

Version history kept?

(yes --- always)

Effective date declared?

(yes --- always)

User acceptance:

Explicit acceptance required?

(yes --- always)

Acceptance method:

Checkbox at signup /

Click-wrap / Both

Acceptance timestamp stored?

(yes --- always)

ToS version at acceptance stored?

(yes --- always)

Re-acceptance on material change?

(yes --- always)

Grace period on change: \_\_\_ days

⚠ ENFORCEMENT INVARIANT:

If service blocked on non-acceptance:

During grace period --- user has not

accepted new ToS.

Background processing for that user

must be suspended during grace period

if ToS not accepted.

Otherwise: user receives service

without valid acceptance =

enforceability risk.

Align with Section 06 session

invalidation and Section 13 async

job suspension.

Service blocked if not accepted?

(yes / no)

Background jobs suspended on

non-acceptance? (yes --- always

if service blocked = yes)

Separate AUP? (yes / no)

Embedded in ToS? (yes / no)

Prohibited uses declared?

(yes --- always)

Prohibited uses include:

• Illegal activity

• Harassment / abuse

• Spam / scraping

• IP violation

• Reverse engineering

• Security attacks

• Additional per app type: \_\_\_

Enforcement:

Violation response defined?

(yes / no)

Suspension / termination path?

(yes --- always)

Appeals process? (yes / no)

Audit logged? (yes --- always)

⚠ ENFORCEMENT INVARIANT:

Age gate must execute BEFORE:

• Account creation

• Any data processing

• Marketing consent collection

• Any cookie other than necessary

If age gate runs after any of these,

minor data is processed before

compliance check.

This is a COPPA / GDPR / DPDP

violation at the point of collection.

Cross-link to Section 06 Auth

lifecycle --- age check is step 0,

before identity creation.

15\. COMPLIANCE FAILURE MODES

[OPERATIONAL]

Define behavior for:

• ToS acceptance record missing

• Background job runs during

grace period without acceptance

• User bypasses age gate

• Minor found in system without

parental consent

• Minor data processed before

age gate executed

• Sanctioned user detected

at signup

• Sanctioned user detected

at payment

• Sanctioned user detected

on periodic re-screening

(post account creation)

• Sanctions re-screening

service unavailable

• Export-restricted user detected

• OSS license violation found

post-deploy

• SBOM and OSS inventory drift

detected

• SLA credit would exceed

liability cap

• DMCA takedown received and

cannot locate content

• Accessibility scan blocks deploy

• Accessibility override requested

without legal sign-off

• Regulatory license expired

• Legal hold conflicts with

scheduled deletion

• Legal hold conflicts with

automated backup purge

• Communications opt-out not

propagated within SLA

• Unsubscribe overridden by

segmentation logic

• CSAM detected in UGC

• DSA illegal content report

not actioned within deadline

• Regulatory inquiry received

without response owner

• ToS version mismatch between

acceptance record and current

• EU AI Act high-risk system

deployed without conformity

assessment

• Automated decision made

without human review path

• AI training on user data

without consent

• Legal entity / controller

not declared for active region

Fail-open anywhere?

(must be no --- never)

= ALERT + reconcile

[ ] SLA credit \> liability cap

= CONFLICT + legal review

[ ] Legal hold vs purge conflict

= HOLD wins always

[AGENT HINT]

GOVERNANCE:

→ Generate legal document registry

(ToS / AUP / Cookie / SLA / DPA /

BAA / AI disclosure ---

versioned, timestamped)

§21 — CACHING STRATEGY

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Always

[PURPOSE] → Define caching layers,

TTL governance,

cache consistency model,

cache memory tiering,

cache key design,

cache invalidation strategy,

tenant isolation in cache,

security boundaries,

cache-aside vs write-through

vs read-through patterns,

CDN / edge caching,

client-side caching,

session + auth token caching,

database query caching,

cache schema versioning,

role-scoped cache keys,

pagination key completeness,

negative caching policy,

high-cardinality attack

prevention,

idempotency key cache safety,

clock skew handling,

cache amplification risk,

search index coherency,

bulk invalidation safety,

distributed cache quorum,

cross-service namespace

isolation,

async job cache safety,

cache stampede prevention,

PII in cache controls,

and cache failure modes

across all app layers.

Do NOT assume a single cache layer.

Do NOT assume cache is always safe

to populate.

Do NOT assume invalidation is simple.

Do NOT assume cache is tenant-safe

by default.

Do NOT assume schema never changes.

Do NOT assume role changes invalidate

automatically.

Do NOT assume clocks are in sync

across regions.

Do NOT assume negative results are

safe to cache aggressively.

Do NOT assume cache keys are

collision-free by default.

Do NOT assume one Redis instance

is safe for all data types.

Do NOT assume eventual consistency

is acceptable for all data.

Assume stale data will cause bugs.

Assume cache will be a security

boundary violation if not scoped.

Assume cache will fail --- plan for it.

Assume PII will leak through cache

if not explicitly prevented.

Assume schema will evolve and break

cached objects silently.

Assume bulk operations will cause

invalidation storms.

Assume attackers will enumerate

query params to exhaust cache.

Assume search result floods will

evict critical auth keys if

not isolated.

All decisions must reference:

• Section 07 --- Data Model

(what data is cacheable,

schema version tracking)

• Section 08 --- API Design

(cache headers, ETags,

idempotency keys)

• Section 11 --- Search & Discovery

(index update → cache invalidation)

• Section 13 --- Async Processing

(async jobs must read from

source of truth, not cache)

• Section 16 --- Rate Governance

(cache hit rate limit alignment,

bulk invalidation rate limiting,

high-cardinality abuse protection)

• Section 17 --- Data Integrity

(schema migrations → cache

version mismatch handling)

• Section 18 --- Security

(auth token cache, tenant

isolation, no PII in shared cache,

permission change invalidation,

fail-open prohibition)

• Section 19 --- Privacy

(PII classification --- Tier 3/4

must never enter shared cache)

• Section 22 --- Resilience

(cache failure behavior)

• Section 27 --- Observability

(cache hit rate, eviction metrics)

1\. CACHE LAYER DECLARATION

[GOVERNANCE]

Declare every cache layer in use:

CDN / Edge cache:

Used? (yes / no)

Provider: \_\_\_

Caches: static assets /

public API responses /

declare

Application-level cache:

Used? (yes / no)

Technology: Redis / Memcached /

in-process / declare

Shared across services?

(yes / no)

If shared: namespace isolation

enforced? (yes --- always)

See Section 09 below.

Database query cache:

Used? (yes / no)

ORM-level? (yes / no)

Explicit query cache? (yes / no)

Client-side cache:

Browser cache? (yes / no)

Mobile local cache? (yes / no)

Service worker cache? (yes / no)

Session / auth token cache:

Sessions cached? (yes / no)

Token validation cached?

(yes / no)

Cache location: Redis /

in-memory / declare

Each layer declared above must

have TTL, consistency model,

invalidation strategy, security

scope, and schema version

handling defined in sections below.

2\. CACHE PATTERN DECLARATION

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

Pattern per data type --- declare:

Cache-aside (lazy loading):

App checks cache first.

On miss: load from DB,

write to cache.

Used for: \_\_\_

Risk: cold start latency on miss.

Write-through:

Write to cache AND DB together.

Used for: \_\_\_

Risk: write latency increase.

Read-through:

Cache handles DB read on miss.

Used for: \_\_\_

Risk: cache layer complexity.

Write-behind (write-back):

Write to cache first,

async flush to DB.

Used for: \_\_\_

Risk: data loss on cache failure.

⚠ If used: must declare

durability guarantee and

flush failure recovery.

Write-invalidate:

On write: invalidate cache key,

do NOT write new value.

Next read repopulates.

Used for: \_\_\_

Safest for consistency.

Default pattern for this app: \_\_\_

Exceptions declared per data type.

3\. CACHE SCHEMA VERSIONING

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

Cache schema version tracked?

(yes --- always)

⚠ SCHEMA EVOLUTION INVARIANT:

When data model changes

(Section 17 migrations),

cached serialized objects may:

• Miss new required fields

• Contain deprecated fields

• Break deserialization entirely

This causes silent runtime

failures post-deploy if not

handled explicitly.

Cache value includes schema

version? (yes --- always)

Version stored as:

key suffix / embedded field /

declare

On schema version mismatch

at read time:

Auto-invalidate + re-fetch?

(yes --- recommended)

Soft fallback to defaults?

(yes / no)

Hard reject + error?

(yes / no --- for strict types)

Strategy declared per

data type? (yes --- always)

Schema version incremented on:

Any model field added? (yes / no)

Any model field removed?

(yes --- always)

Any field type changed?

(yes --- always)

Any serialization format

change? (yes --- always)

Cache warm after schema

version bump? (yes / no)

Old version keys purged

after migration? (yes --- always)

Align with Section 17 data

integrity and migration strategy.

4\. TTL GOVERNANCE

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

TTL declared per data type

(no undeclared TTLs permitted):

Static assets (immutable):

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

(e.g. 1 year with content

hash in URL)

Static assets (versioned):

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

Public API responses:

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

Authenticated API responses:

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

(short --- data is user-specific)

Session data:

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

Must match Section 06 session

expiry --- no contradiction.

Auth token validation cache:

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

⚠ Must be ≤ token expiry.

Must be ≤ revocation

propagation SLA (Section 18).

Stale token validation cache

= revoked token still accepted.

User profile / preferences:

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

Tenant config / settings:

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

Rate limit counters:

TTL: aligned with Section 16

window size.

Database query results:

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

Search results:

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

Computed / aggregated data:

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

Third-party API responses:

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

(respect upstream cache headers)

Negative cache entries

(404 / null / not found):

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

(must be SHORT --- much shorter

than positive entry TTL)

⚠ TTL INVARIANT:

Zero TTL = no caching (valid).

Infinite TTL = prohibited unless

explicitly justified + invalidation

strategy declared.

Every TTL must have a

corresponding invalidation trigger.

CLOCK SKEW ACROSS REGIONS:

Time source standardised?

(yes --- always for multi-region)

Clock sync enforced (NTP / PTP)?

(yes --- always for multi-region)

⚠ CLOCK SKEW INVARIANT:

Without clock sync:

Region A may expire cache

earlier than Region B.

Invalidation event timestamps

mismatch across regions.

TTL computed differently per

instance = inconsistent cache

expiry = stale data served

in some regions.

All cache TTL must be computed

from a consistent time source.

Max acceptable clock drift:

\_\_\_ milliseconds

5\. CACHE CONSISTENCY MODEL

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

Consistency model declared per

data type? (yes --- always)

Without an explicit consistency

model, correctness expectations

are implicit. Engineers assume

different things. Bugs are filed

for behavior that is intended.

Tests assert the wrong guarantees.

Consistency models:

Strong consistency:

Cache invalidated BEFORE

response returned to caller.

Reader always sees latest write.

Cost: higher write latency.

Use for: permission data /

billing state / security

config / anything where

stale = incorrect behavior.

Eventual consistency:

Cache invalidated async

after write.

Reader may see stale data

for up to TTL or invalidation

lag window.

Cost: stale reads possible.

Use for: public content /

non-critical preferences /

aggregated stats / anything

where brief staleness is

acceptable.

Read-your-own-write (RYOW):

User who just wrote always

reads their own write.

Other users may see stale.

Implementation: route user

to same cache node / bypass

cache for same-session reads /

version token approach.

Use for: profile updates /

settings changes / any UX

where "I just saved this

and it disappeared" is

unacceptable.

Declare per data type:

User profile:

Model: strong / eventual / RYOW

Permissions / roles:

Model: strong

(must be strong --- always)

(stale permission = security

violation)

Auth token validation:

Model: strong

(must be strong --- always)

Tenant config:

Model: strong / eventual /

declare

Public content:

Model: eventual (acceptable)

Search results:

Model: eventual (acceptable)

Rate limit counters:

Model: strong

(must be strong --- always)

(eventual = rate limit bypass)

Billing / subscription state:

Model: strong

(must be strong --- always)

User-generated content:

Model: strong / eventual /

declare

⚠ CONSISTENCY INVARIANT:

Any data type where stale read

= security violation or incorrect

billing MUST use strong

consistency.

Eventual consistency is only

acceptable where staleness has

no security or financial

consequence.

Defaulting everything to

eventual = implicit security

downgrade.

Read-your-own-write guarantee:

Declared per endpoint?

(yes --- always)

Endpoints with RYOW guarantee:

\_\_\_

Endpoints where eventual

is acceptable: \_\_\_

RYOW implementation method:

Cache bypass on same session /

Version token / Sticky routing /

Declare

Cross-region consistency:

Declared? (yes --- always

for multi-region)

Model per data type:

Strong: \_\_\_ (list data types)

Eventual: \_\_\_ (list data types)

None (local only): \_\_\_

Cross-region invalidation

propagation SLA: \_\_\_ seconds

Acceptable staleness window

cross-region: \_\_\_ seconds

Align with Section 04 clock

skew handling.

6\. CACHE MEMORY TIERING

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Cache memory tiering declared?

(yes / no)

⚠ CACHE NOISY NEIGHBOR INVARIANT:

A single Redis instance serving

all data types creates internal

noisy neighbor risk.

Example:

Search result flood populates

thousands of large keys.

Memory pressure triggers LRU

eviction.

Auth token cache keys and rate

limit counter keys are evicted

(they are smaller and less

recently used).

Result:

Auth tokens evicted → users

forced to re-authenticate

unexpectedly.

Rate limit counters evicted →

rate limit window resets →

rate limit bypass.

This is not a cache miss.

This is a security regression

caused by memory pressure

from unrelated data.

Cache tiers declared:

CRITICAL tier:

Dedicated cluster / memory

pool? (yes / no)

Contains:

Auth tokens

Session data

Rate limit counters

Idempotency keys

Permission / role cache

Eviction policy: no eviction

(must never evict --- always)

If memory full: reject write,

alert ops, never silently

evict critical keys.

Memory allocation: \_\_\_ MB / GB

Alert threshold: \_\_\_% full

STANDARD tier:

Contains:

User profile cache

Tenant config cache

API response cache

DB query cache

Eviction policy: LRU / declare

Memory allocation: \_\_\_ MB / GB

BULK tier:

Contains:

Search results

Public content

Aggregated / computed data

CDN-eligible responses

Eviction policy: LRU / TTL /

declare (most aggressive)

Memory allocation: \_\_\_ MB / GB

Tier isolation method:

Separate Redis instances?

(yes / no --- strongest isolation)

Separate Redis databases?

(yes / no --- logical only,

shares memory pool,

weaker isolation)

Separate memory pools

(Redis 7+ memory policies)?

(yes / no)

Declared method: \_\_\_

⚠ TIER ISOLATION INVARIANT:

Separate Redis databases do NOT

provide memory isolation.

All databases in one instance

share the same maxmemory pool.

Eviction from one database

does not protect another.

True isolation requires separate

Redis instances or separate

memory policies per keyspace.

For critical tier: separate

instance is strongly recommended.

Cross-tier access prohibited?

(yes --- always)

Critical tier keys must not

be writable by services that

write bulk tier data.

Access control per tier:

Critical: auth service only

Standard: declared services

Bulk: any service (declare)

7\. CACHE KEY DESIGN

[APPLICATION]

Cache key structure declared?

(yes --- always)

Key components per cache type:

Per-user data:

Key includes: user_id

(yes --- always)

Key includes: tenant_id

(yes --- always for multi-tenant)

Key includes: schema_version

(yes --- always)

Key includes: user role

(yes --- always if RBAC affects

response shape)

⚠ RBAC FIELD-LEVEL CACHE

INVARIANT:

If RBAC affects which fields

are returned in a response:

Role MUST be included in

cache key.

Without role in key:

User role is downgraded →

cached object built under

old elevated role →

user still sees privileged

fields via cache hit.

This is a privilege escalation

via cache.

Per-tenant data:

Key includes: tenant_id

(yes --- always)

Key includes: schema_version

(yes --- always)

Public data:

Key includes: resource_id

Key includes: version / hash?

(yes / no)

API response cache:

Key includes: route + params

Key includes: tenant_id

(if tenant-specific)

Key includes: user role

(yes --- always if RBAC

affects response shape)

Key includes: locale?

(yes / no --- if i18n)

Key includes: schema_version

(yes --- always)

Paginated endpoints:

Key includes: page number

(yes --- always)

Key includes: page size

(yes --- always)

Key includes: sort order

(yes --- always)

Key includes: filter params

(yes --- always)

⚠ PAGINATION KEY INVARIANT:

Missing any pagination param

from cache key = page 1 data

returned for page 2 request.

Silent data correctness bug,

extremely hard to debug

in production.

All pagination parameters

must be in the cache key.

Canonical key format:

{route}:{tenant}:{user}:

{role}:{page}:{size}:

{sort}:{filters}:{schema_v}

Service namespace prefix:

Mandatory prefix per service?

(yes --- always if shared cache)

Format: {service_name}:{env}:

{rest of key}

⚠ NAMESPACE COLLISION INVARIANT:

If multiple services share

the same Redis instance:

Without mandatory namespace

prefix, Service A can

accidentally read, overwrite,

or delete keys belonging

to Service B.

Service namespace prefix

is mandatory --- always.

Cross-service key collision

detection? (yes / no)

⚠ TENANT ISOLATION INVARIANT:

Any cache key for tenant-specific

data MUST include tenant_id.

Cache key without tenant_id

for tenant data = cross-tenant

data leak = critical incident.

Align with Section 18.

⚠ USER ISOLATION INVARIANT:

Any cache key for user-specific

data MUST include user_id.

Missing user_id = user A

sees user B's data.

Key format standardised?

(yes --- always)

Collision detection? (yes / no)

8\. CACHE INVALIDATION STRATEGY

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

Invalidation triggers declared

per data type:

On user data update:

Invalidate: user-scoped keys

Method: delete / update / declare

Propagates to: app cache /

CDN / client / declare

On resource create:

Negative cache for that

resource invalidated?

(yes --- always)

Align Section 09 below.

On admin change affecting

multiple users:

Invalidate: affected scope only

Wildcard invalidation?

(yes / no --- declare blast

radius of wildcard)

On bulk operation:

Bulk invalidation rate limited?

(yes --- always)

Batch purge strategy defined?

(yes --- always)

Batch size: \_\_\_ keys per batch

Delay between batches:

\_\_\_ milliseconds

⚠ BULK INVALIDATION INVARIANT:

Admin bulk update affecting

thousands of records =

thousands of simultaneous

cache invalidations =

Redis CPU spike =

cache layer outage =

cascade to DB.

Bulk invalidation must be

rate-limited and batched.

Never invalidate unbounded

key sets in a single operation.

On tenant config change:

Invalidate: all tenant-scoped

keys? (yes / no)

SLA: \_\_\_ seconds

On tenant offboarding:

ALL tenant cache keys purged?

(yes --- always)

Purge batched + rate limited?

(yes --- always)

Purge verified? (yes / no)

Align with Section 18

tenant offboarding.

On permission / role change:

Auth + RBAC cache invalidated?

(yes --- always)

Role-keyed response cache

invalidated? (yes --- always)

Propagation SLA: \_\_\_ seconds

⚠ Stale permission cache =

revoked access still granted.

Align with Section 18 async

privilege revalidation.

On token revocation:

Token validation cache purged?

(yes --- always)

Align with Section 18 token

revocation propagation SLA.

On schema version bump:

Old version keys purged?

(yes --- always)

Or auto-invalidated on read?

(yes / no)

On search index update:

Search result cache invalidated?

(yes --- always)

⚠ SEARCH COHERENCY INVARIANT:

Search index updated but result

cache not invalidated = stale

search results returned beyond

index refresh window.

Index update event MUST trigger

search result cache invalidation.

Align with Section 11.

On deploy:

Static asset cache invalidated?

(yes --- always)

CDN purge on deploy?

(yes / no)

API cache invalidated?

(yes / no --- declare which)

Invalidation method:

TTL expiry only? (yes / no)

Event-driven invalidation?

(yes / no)

Explicit delete on write?

(yes / no)

Tag-based / surrogate keys?

(yes / no)

⚠ TTL-ONLY INVALIDATION IS

INSUFFICIENT for:

• Security-sensitive data

• Permission / role data

• Revoked tokens

• Offboarded tenant data

• Schema version mismatches

• Search result coherency

• Negative cache after create

• Strong consistency data types

These MUST use event-driven

or explicit invalidation,

not TTL alone.

9\. NEGATIVE CACHING POLICY

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

Negative results caching declared?

(yes / no)

Negative results = 404 /

null / empty / not found

responses.

Negative caching allowed?

(yes / no --- declare per

data type)

If yes:

TTL for negative entries:

\_\_\_ seconds

(must be SHORT --- much shorter

than positive entry TTL)

⚠ NEGATIVE CACHE INVARIANT:

If negative result cached

too aggressively:

• Resource created after

cache populated

• Cache still returns 404

• User sees phantom "not found"

for a resource that exists

Especially bad in multi-tenant

where same user in another

session still gets 404.

Negative cache invalidated

on resource create?

(yes --- always)

Negative cache invalidated

on resource restore?

(yes --- always)

Negative cache invalidated

on permission grant?

(yes --- always)

(User gains access to resource

they previously couldn't see ---

old 404 must not persist.)

Negative cache key includes:

tenant_id? (yes --- always)

user_id? (yes --- if user-scoped)

resource_id? (yes --- always)

Negative cache stored

separately from positive?

(yes / no --- recommended yes

for easier targeted purge)

Empty search result cached?

(yes / no)

If yes:

TTL: \_\_\_ seconds (keep short)

Invalidated on index update?

(yes --- always, align

Section 11 + Section 08

search coherency invariant)

10\. SECURITY & PRIVACY IN CACHE

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

PII in cache:

Tier 3 PII in shared cache?

(prohibited --- always)

Tier 4 PHI / PCI in cache?

(prohibited --- always)

If PII must be cached:

Encrypted at rest in cache?

(yes --- always)

Per-user isolated cache?

(yes --- always)

TTL minimised? (yes --- always)

Audit logged? (yes --- always)

Align with Section 19

PII taxonomy.

Shared cache between tenants:

Allowed? (must be no --- unless

key isolation proven)

Cross-tenant key access

possible? (must be no --- always)

Auth / session data in cache:

Encrypted? (yes / no)

Access restricted to

auth service only? (yes --- always)

Accessible to other services?

(must be no)

Cache rate limiting:

Cache hit counts toward

rate limit? (yes / no --- declare)

⚠ CACHE AMPLIFICATION INVARIANT:

If cache hit does NOT count

toward rate limit:

Attacker can send high volume

of requests that all hit cache.

DB load reduced but API

CPU / network still saturated.

Cache does not equal free

requests from a rate limit

perspective.

Declare explicitly:

Rate-limited: yes / no

If no: justify + declare

compensating control.

Align with Section 16.

Cache poisoning prevention:

Input validation before

caching? (yes --- always)

Untrusted data cached?

(must be no)

Third-party response cached

without validation?

(must be no)

Response cache headers:

Cache-Control: private

for authenticated responses?

(yes --- always)

Cache-Control: no-store

for sensitive responses?

(yes --- always)

Vary header declared?

(yes / no --- required if

response varies by

auth / role / locale / encoding)

11\. HIGH-CARDINALITY CACHE ATTACK

PREVENTION

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

High-cardinality key attack risk

declared? (yes --- always)

⚠ CACHE EXHAUSTION INVARIANT:

Attack vector:

Attacker hits endpoint with

random / enumerated query params.

Each unique param combination

generates a new cache key.

Cache memory fills with

one-time-use keys.

Legitimate hot keys evicted

under memory pressure.

Cache hit rate collapses.

All traffic falls through

to DB simultaneously.

Result: cache-induced DB

overload = service degradation

for all tenants.

Cache-amplified availability

attack.

Align with Section 16

abuse protection.

Mitigations:

Query param normalization:

Enforced before key generation?

(yes --- always)

Params sorted canonically?

(yes --- always)

Unknown params stripped?

(yes --- always)

Declared allowed params only

contribute to cache key:

(yes --- always)

Max unique keys per endpoint:

Declared? (yes / no)

Limit: \_\_\_ keys per endpoint

Limit: \_\_\_ keys per tenant

per endpoint

Enforcement: reject new key

when limit reached /

return uncached response /

declare

High-cardinality key guard:

Enabled? (yes / no)

Detection: new keys per minute

per endpoint \> \_\_\_ = alert

Response: rate limit cache

writes from that source

Burst of new keys \> \_\_\_

per minute = suspect +

alert + throttle

Key TTL for low-value entries:

Short TTL for infrequently

accessed keys? (yes / no)

Auto-evict single-use keys?

(yes / no)

Cache write rate limiting:

Max cache writes per second

per user / IP: \_\_\_

Align with Section 16

rate governance.

12\. IDEMPOTENCY KEY CACHE

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

(Skip if POST responses are

never cached.)

Idempotency response caching

used? (yes / no)

If no --- skip this section.

⚠ IDEMPOTENCY CACHE INVARIANT:

If idempotency key does NOT

include tenant_id:

Tenant A submits request with

key "pay-123".

Tenant B submits different

request with same key "pay-123".

Tenant B receives Tenant A's

cached response.

Cross-tenant data leak via

idempotency cache.

Idempotency key includes

tenant_id? (yes --- always)

Idempotency key includes

user_id? (yes / no)

Idempotency key format:

{tenant_id}:{user_id}:

{client_key} (recommended)

Idempotency cache TTL:

Declared? (yes --- always)

TTL ≤ idempotency window?

(yes --- always)

If TTL \> idempotency window:

Cache expires before window

closes = duplicate request

not deduplicated = double

execution risk.

Idempotency window: \_\_\_ seconds

Cache TTL: \_\_\_ seconds

(must be ≤ window above)

Idempotency cache storage:

Same cache as general?

(yes / no)

Namespace isolated?

(yes --- always)

Encrypted? (yes / no --- required

if response contains PII)

Idempotency response contains

PII? (yes / no)

If yes: encrypted in cache?

(yes --- always, align

Section 10 PII in cache rules)

Idempotency key reuse across

tenants blocked?

(yes --- always)

Enforcement: tenant_id in key

\+ validated at read.

15\. DISTRIBUTED CACHE RESILIENCE

[OPERATIONAL]

Distributed cache (Redis cluster

or equivalent)? (yes / no)

If no --- skip cluster section.

Cluster quorum:

Quorum enforced? (yes --- always)

Writes allowed without quorum?

(must be no --- always)

⚠ SPLIT-BRAIN INVARIANT:

Redis cluster network partition

creates two partitions that

both accept writes.

After partition heals:

Two nodes hold different values

for the same key.

One overwrites the other

silently.

Writes must require quorum.

Without quorum enforcement,

split-brain = silent data

inconsistency = correctness

failures.

Replication:

Sync replication? (yes / no)

Async replication? (yes / no)

Replication lag declared:

\_\_\_ milliseconds max

Replication lag alert? (yes / no)

RDB snapshots? (yes / no)

AOF (append-only file)?

(yes / no)

Persistence required?

(yes / no --- declare per layer)

If write-behind used:

persistence required --- always

Failover:

Sentinel / cluster auto-failover?

(yes / no)

Failover SLA: \_\_\_ seconds

During failover:

Read from replica? (yes / no)

Fall back to DB? (yes --- always)

16\. CACHE STAMPEDE & THUNDERING

(yes / no)

Occurs when: cache expires,

many requests hit DB

simultaneously.

(yes / no)

previous cache / declare

17\. ASYNC JOBS & CACHE SAFETY

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

Async jobs reading cached data?

(yes / no)

⚠ ASYNC CACHE SAFETY INVARIANT:

Async jobs that read from cache

then write derived data are

particularly dangerous:

• Job reads stale cache

• Writes incorrect derived result

• Result persisted to DB

• Stale data now in source of

truth, not just cache

Harder to detect than a stale

API response because the

corrupted value is written

back permanently.

For critical async operations:

Bypass cache entirely?

(yes --- recommended always)

Read from source of truth

(DB) directly? (yes --- recommended)

If cache used in async job:

Justify explicitly why.

Declare staleness tolerance.

Declare recovery if stale

value detected.

Align with Section 13 async

processing integrity guarantees.

18\. CACHE FAILURE BEHAVIOR

[OPERATIONAL + GOVERNANCE]

Cache layer unavailable:

App falls back to DB?

(yes --- always for read path)

Fail-closed for security-

sensitive cache? (yes --- always)

Declare which caches

fail closed vs open.

⚠ CACHE FAILURE INVARIANT:

Cache is a performance layer.

App must be functionally correct

with cache fully disabled.

If app cannot operate without

cache = architectural dependency

that must be declared explicitly.

Auth token validation cache

failure = fail CLOSED always.

Fall through to live token

validation. Never assume valid.

Align with Section 18

fail-open prohibition.

Cache corruption:

Detected? (yes / no)

Response: flush + rebuild

Fallback to DB during rebuild?

(yes --- always)

On eviction: DB fallback

transparent to user? (yes / no)

Write-behind flush failure:

(if write-behind pattern used)

Max retries: \_\_\_

On permanent failure:

alert + manual recovery

Data loss window declared: \_\_\_

• Eventual consistency used

• Redis database isolation

• Negative cache returns 404

response

auth endpoint

• High-cardinality key flood

• Idempotency key collision

cross-tenant

idempotency window

• Cluster split-brain detected

• Cache stampede on cold start

• Write-behind flush permanent

failure

• Cache layer fully unavailable

• Clock drift causes TTL

inconsistency across regions

• Namespace collision between

services on shared cache

• Search result stale after

index update

Fail-open anywhere?

(must be no --- never)

Exception: read path DB fallback

is fail-open by design and is

safe. Auth cache must always

fail closed.

§22 — RESILIENCE & FAILURE

CONTAINMENT

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Always

[PURPOSE] → Ensure the system survives

dependency failure, overload,

retry storms, regional outages,

partial degradation, cascading

collapse, split-brain conditions,

deployment instability, resource

exhaustion, write amplification,

third-party quota exhaustion,

brownout oscillation,

compound multi-dependency failure,

observability blackout,

and graceful shutdown ---

without violating security,

financial correctness, or

data integrity.

When something fails ---

how does the system prevent

making it worse?

Do NOT assume:

DB is always available.

Cache is always reachable.

Message broker is stable.

Third-party APIs respond.

Network partitions are rare.

Traffic stays predictable.

Retries are harmless.

Region outages are impossible.

Partial degradation won't cascade.

Health checks are always correct.

Deploys are instantaneous.

Memory never leaks.

Upstream quotas are infinite.

Automated systems catch everything.

One failure happens at a time.

Monitoring is always available.

Recovery is immediate and stable.

Assume:

Latency will spike.

Clients will retry.

Queues will back up.

Memory will saturate.

Circuit breakers will trip.

One dependency failure will

attempt to cascade.

Retries will amplify load.

Graceful shutdown will be

interrupted.

Health checks will lie.

Rolling deploy will create

version mismatch windows.

Two failures will combine

to create a third.

Monitoring will fail during

the incident that needs it most.

Recovery will oscillate before

it stabilises.

Design for containment.

All decisions must reference:

• Section 07 --- Data Model

(write amplification, deadlock)

• Section 08 --- API Design

(idempotency, timeout headers)

• Section 13 --- Async Processing

(queue containment, dead letter)

• Section 16 --- Rate Governance

(load shedding, backpressure)

• Section 18 --- Security

(fail-closed invariants)

• Section 21 --- Caching

(cache failure, critical tier

eviction as resilience failure,

stampede, consistency under load)

• Section 24 --- Deployment

(deploy failure, rollback,

graceful shutdown)

• Section 27 --- Observability

(all resilience metrics)

1\. FAILURE TAXONOMY (MANDATORY)

[GOVERNANCE]

All services must classify failures:

A. Hard Dependency Failure

DB unreachable

Cache cluster down

Message broker unavailable

Third-party API down

Search cluster unavailable

Internal service unreachable

B. Soft Degradation

Latency spike

Replication lag

Lock contention

Thread pool saturation

Slow external API

Connection pool pressure

C. Resource Exhaustion

CPU \> \_\_\_% threshold

Memory \> \_\_\_% threshold

Connection pool exhausted

Queue depth exceeded

File descriptor exhaustion

Memory leak progression

(slow OOM path)

D. Traffic Pathology

Traffic spike

Retry storm

Thundering herd

Bot abuse

High-cardinality attack

(align Section 21)

E. Distributed System Pathology

Network partition

Split-brain detected

Cross-region invalidation delay

Clock drift beyond SLA

Version mismatch during

rolling deploy

F. Write Pathology

Non-idempotent write retried

Duplicate financial transaction

Write amplification spike

Deadlock surge

G. Operational Pathology

Health check lying

(false healthy / false sick)

Graceful shutdown interrupted

Third-party quota exhausted

Upstream rate limited

Observability pipeline failure

H. Compound Failure

Multiple dependencies degraded

simultaneously

Individual Tier 3 failures

combining to Tier 1 risk

No fallback available because

primary and fallback both fail

Each service must declare:

Which classes it is vulnerable to

Which class is survivable

vs catastrophic

Containment behavior per class

2\. FAILURE IMPACT TIERS

[GOVERNANCE]

All subsystems must map to

impact tier:

Tier 0 → Security compromise risk

Tier 1 → Financial correctness risk

Tier 2 → Data integrity risk

Tier 3 → Availability degradation

Tier 4 → UX-only degradation

Tier determines:

Fail closed vs fail open

Degrade vs disable

Retry vs abort

Write block vs queue

Human escalation SLA

⚠ TIER INVARIANT:

Tier 0 and Tier 1 operations

must NEVER degrade to eventual

or fail-open.

No exception. No override.

Align with Section 21

consistency model --- strong

consistency data types are

all Tier 0 or Tier 1.

Declare per subsystem:

Auth → Tier: \_\_\_

Payments → Tier: \_\_\_

Rate limiting → Tier: \_\_\_

Permissions → Tier: \_\_\_

Search → Tier: \_\_\_

Notifications → Tier: \_\_\_

Analytics → Tier: \_\_\_

Observability pipeline → Tier: \_\_\_

(recommended: Tier 1)

(declare all subsystems)

3\. DEPENDENCY BLAST RADIUS MAP

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Dependency graph declared?

(yes --- always)

⚠ BLAST RADIUS INVARIANT:

Without a dependency map,

failure containment is reactive.

You discover cascade paths

during incidents, not before.

Every service must declare:

• What it depends on

• What depends on it

• What fails if it goes down

• What degrades vs what stops

For each critical service:

Upstream dependencies: \_\_\_

Downstream consumers: \_\_\_

If this fails:

Immediate impact: \_\_\_

Cascade risk: \_\_\_

Containment: \_\_\_

Shared dependency risk:

Which services share the DB? \_\_\_

Which services share Redis? \_\_\_

Which services share the

message broker? \_\_\_

Single shared dependency =

single point of cascade.

Isolate where possible.

Declare where not.

Critical path declared?

(yes --- always)

Critical path = minimum set of

services required for core

user flow to function.

Everything else = non-critical.

Non-critical failure must NOT

take down critical path.

4\. SLA BUDGET PER OPERATION

[GOVERNANCE]

Latency budget declared per

operation? (yes --- always)

⚠ LATENCY BUDGET INVARIANT:

Without declared latency budgets,

timeout values are arbitrary.

Engineers pick numbers that

feel reasonable.

Result: outer timeout fires

before inner operation completes,

or inner operation holds resources

long after outer client gave up.

Total budget: \_\_\_ ms

Breakdown:

Network: \_\_\_ ms

API layer: \_\_\_ ms

Service logic: \_\_\_ ms

DB query: \_\_\_ ms

Cache: \_\_\_ ms

Third-party: \_\_\_ ms

Auth flow:

Total budget: \_\_\_ ms

Payment flow:

Total budget: \_\_\_ ms

Search query:

Total budget: \_\_\_ ms

Async job (per step):

Total budget: \_\_\_ ms

Budgets drive timeout values

in Section 05.

If a dependency cannot meet

its budget SLA:

Circuit breaker trips? (yes)

Fallback used? (yes --- declare)

Budget reviewed? (yes)

5\. TIMEOUT GOVERNANCE (LAYERED)

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Timeout hierarchy MUST be:

Client timeout (outermost)

\> API gateway timeout

\> Service timeout

\> Downstream service timeout

\> DB / cache timeout

(innermost)

⚠ TIMEOUT HIERARCHY INVARIANT:

If outer layer timeout

inner operation timeout:

Inner operation continues

after outer client gave up.

Client retries.

Duplicate write risk.

Resource leak risk.

Each layer timeout must be

SHORTER than the layer above.

Declare per dependency:

Client timeout: \_\_\_ ms

API gateway timeout: \_\_\_ ms

Service handler timeout: \_\_\_ ms

Service-to-service timeout: \_\_\_ ms

DB query timeout: \_\_\_ ms

DB connection timeout: \_\_\_ ms

Cache operation timeout: \_\_\_ ms

Message broker timeout: \_\_\_ ms

Third-party API timeout: \_\_\_ ms

Search query timeout: \_\_\_ ms

Service-to-service timeout chain:

Service A calls Service B

calls Service C.

A timeout: \_\_\_ ms

B timeout: \_\_\_ ms (\< A)

C timeout: \_\_\_ ms (\< B)

If not enforced:

A times out.

B still waiting for C.

B holds thread + connection.

Multiplied across all A callers.

= thread pool exhaustion in B.

⚠ I/O TIMEOUT INVARIANT:

No dependency may block longer

than the API handler timeout.

No blocking I/O without timeout.

No default infinite timeouts.

Infinite timeout = guaranteed

eventual thread pool exhaustion.

6\. RETRY GOVERNANCE

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Retries must be:

Bounded

Jittered

Respect circuit breaker state

Idempotency-aware

Not mutually amplifying

Declare per operation:

GET / read operations:

Max retries: \_\_\_

Backoff: exponential + jitter

Total retry window ≤ \_\_\_ ms

POST / write (idempotent):

Retry allowed? (yes)

Idempotency key required?

(yes --- always)

Max retries: \_\_\_

Backoff: exponential + jitter

POST / write (non-idempotent):

Retry allowed? (must be no)

⚠ Non-idempotent write

retried = duplicate execution.

For financial operations:

duplicate = double charge.

Non-idempotent writes must

NOT be retried automatically.

Manual retry only with

explicit user confirmation.

Async jobs:

Max retries: \_\_\_

Dead-letter after: \_\_\_ attempts

Backoff: exponential + jitter

Idempotency at receiver:

Receiver deduplicates

retried requests? (yes --- always)

Idempotency key checked

at receiver, not just sent

by caller? (yes --- always)

⚠ IDEMPOTENCY RECEIVER INVARIANT:

Sender using idempotency key

is necessary but not sufficient.

If receiver does not check and

deduplicate the key:

Retry still causes duplicate

execution.

Both sender AND receiver must

enforce idempotency.

Align with Section 08

API design idempotency contract.

Retry between services:

Service A retries → Service B

retries → Service C.

Multiplied load:

100 requests × 3 retries

× 3 services = 900 requests.

No retry loops between services.

No mutual retry amplification.

Retry budget per call chain

declared: \_\_\_

⚠ RETRY STORM INVARIANT:

Retries multiply traffic.

1000 clients × 3 retries =

3000 requests.

Retries must reduce load,

not amplify it.

All retries bounded + jittered.

7\. CIRCUIT BREAKER MODEL

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Each external dependency must have

a circuit breaker:

DB

Cache

Message broker

Each third-party API

Each internal service call

Declaration per dependency:

Failure threshold: \_\_\_ failures

per \_\_\_ seconds

Sliding window: \_\_\_ seconds

Open duration: \_\_\_ seconds

Half-open probe count: \_\_\_

Fallback behavior: \_\_\_

If circuit OPEN:

Fail fast? (yes --- always)

Return 503 / 429? (declare)

Enter brownout? (declare)

Fallback content served?

(declare per endpoint)

⚠ FALLBACK CONTENT INVARIANT:

When circuit is open,

what does the user see?

Blank screen = poor UX and

may look like a bug.

Stale cached response =

acceptable for Tier 3/4.

Graceful degradation message =

acceptable for Tier 3/4.

Error with retry guidance =

acceptable.

Silent incorrect result =

never acceptable.

Declare per endpoint:

Fallback: cached response /

empty state / error message /

feature hidden / declare.

⚠ CIRCUIT BREAKER INVARIANT:

Circuit breaker must trip

BEFORE resource exhaustion.

If circuit trips after thread

pool is exhausted, it is

too late to prevent cascade.

Threshold must be conservative.

8\. BULKHEAD PATTERN

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

(yes / no)

⚠ BULKHEAD INVARIANT:

Circuit breaker isolates by time.

Bulkhead isolates by resource pool.

Without bulkheads:

A slow search query consumes

all available DB connections.

Auth queries queue behind

search queries.

Auth fails.

Tier 4 failure causes Tier 0

failure.

Separate resource pools for:

Thread pool: \_\_\_

Search operations:

DB connection pool: \_\_\_

Thread pool: \_\_\_

Background / async jobs:

Thread pool: \_\_\_

Bulk operations:

Separate pool: \_\_\_

Cannot share with critical:

(yes --- always)

Pool exhaustion behavior:

Critical pool exhausted:

Reject non-critical requests?

(yes --- always)

Alert immediately? (yes --- always)

Non-critical pool exhausted:

Queue? (yes / no)

Reject + degrade? (yes / no)

Never affect critical pool?

(yes --- always)

9\. BACKPRESSURE & LOAD SHEDDING

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Unbounded queues are prohibited.

Declare:

Max queue depth: \_\_\_

Max DB connections: \_\_\_

Max async job backlog: \_\_\_

Max in-flight requests

per service: \_\_\_

When limit exceeded:

Reject new requests?

(yes --- recommended)

Return 429 or 503?

(declare per scenario)

Drop low-priority traffic?

(yes / no)

Disable expensive endpoints?

(yes / no)

Priority of what to shed:

Shed: bulk exports first

Shed: search before auth

Shed: analytics before payments

Never shed: auth / payments /

security operations

⚠ CASCADE INVARIANT:

Slow DB → threads block →

queue grows → memory spikes →

GC thrash → CPU saturates →

node crash → traffic shifts →

cluster collapse.

Backpressure must occur before

thread pool exhaustion.

Shedding order must be declared

and respect impact tiers.
