11\. BROWNOUT OSCILLATION PREVENTION

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Brownout oscillation risk declared?

(yes --- always)

⚠ BROWNOUT FLAPPING INVARIANT:

Individual components each

work correctly:

DB latency spikes →

Circuit opens →

Brownout activates →

Load drops →

DB recovers →

Circuit half-opens →

Traffic restored →

DB spikes again →

Circuit reopens →

Repeat indefinitely.

This is not a component failure.

This is an emergent system

failure caused by correct

components interacting badly.

Autoscaling amplifies it:

Scale up during spike →

scale down during recovery →

scale up again on next spike →

thundering herd on each

scale-up event.

Users see flickering behavior.

Metrics thrash.

On-call gets paged repeatedly

for events that auto-resolve

before investigation completes.

Brownout cooldown declared:

Minimum brownout duration:

\_\_\_ seconds

(once activated, brownout

cannot exit before this

duration regardless of

apparent recovery)

Recovery stability window:

Health must be stable for

\_\_\_ seconds continuously

before brownout exits.

Single healthy check is

not sufficient to exit.

Cooldown between brownout

activations:

Minimum gap between

brownout entry events:

\_\_\_ seconds

(prevents rapid re-entry)

Circuit breaker rate limiting:

Open/close rate limited?

(yes --- always)

Max state transitions per

\_\_\_ seconds: \_\_\_

If rate limit exceeded:

Force hold in current state

for \_\_\_ seconds

Alert: oscillation detected

Escalate to human review?

(yes --- always)

Recovery validation:

Before exiting brownout:

Check: DB p99 \< \_\_\_ ms

Check: error rate \< \_\_\_%

Check: queue depth \< \_\_\_

Check: CPU \< \_\_\_%

All checks must pass for

\_\_\_ seconds continuously.

Partial recovery = stay

in brownout.

Autoscaling lockout during

oscillation:

Autoscaling suspended during

brownout? (yes / no)

Autoscaling suspended during

circuit breaker oscillation?

(yes --- recommended)

Resume autoscaling after

stable for \_\_\_ seconds.

12\. COMPOUND MULTI-DEPENDENCY

FAILURE ESCALATION

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Compound failure detection

declared? (yes --- always)

⚠ COMPOUND FAILURE INVARIANT:

Your impact tier model assumes

one failure at a time.

Reality: the most dangerous

incidents are combinations.

Example 1:

DB slow + Cache down =

brownout fallback (use DB)

also fails. No fallback exists.

Two Tier 3 failures → Tier 1.

Example 2:

Broker lag + Third-party 429 =

async jobs can't process

and can't call upstream.

Queue backlog explodes.

Two soft failures → hard outage.

Example 3:

Region partition + Quota

exhaustion = failover target

also rate-limited.

Cannot serve from either region.

Individual systems each respond

to their own failure correctly.

No system sees the combination.

Compound failure is invisible

to single-dependency monitors.

Compound failure detection:

Active dependency health

scoreboard? (yes / no)

(real-time count of degraded

dependencies)

Threshold for escalation:

If \_\_\_ or more dependencies

degraded simultaneously:

Auto-escalate impact tier

by \_\_\_ levels

Alert: compound failure

Page on-call: P0 / P1

regardless of individual

tier levels

Specific compound scenarios

declared:

DB slow + Cache down:

Combined impact: Tier \_\_\_

Response: \_\_\_

No fallback available →

enter read-only or

return 503? (declare)

Broker unavailable + Third-party

rate limited:

Combined impact: Tier \_\_\_

Response: \_\_\_

Queue locally? (yes / no)

Block writes? (yes / no)

Region partition + Quota

exhausted:

Combined impact: Tier \_\_\_

Response: \_\_\_

Serve stale? (yes / no)

Return 503? (yes / no)

Cache critical tier evicted +

DB slow:

Combined impact: Tier 0

(must be --- always)

Response: fail closed

Auth falls back to DB ---

but DB is slow →

auth latency spikes →

Max acceptable auth

latency: \_\_\_ ms

Beyond that: return 503,

do not silently delay.

Auto kill switch on compound

failure:

Two or more Tier 1 dependencies

degraded simultaneously:

Auto-trigger kill switch?

(yes / no --- declare)

Requires human confirmation?

(yes / no)

If auto: which features

disabled? (declare --- never

disable auth / security)

Compound failure recovery:

ALL degraded dependencies must

recover before compound alert

clears? (yes --- always)

Partial recovery not sufficient

to clear compound alert.

13\. STRONG CONSISTENCY UNDER FAILURE

[GOVERNANCE]

If system under stress:

Strong consistency must NOT

silently degrade to eventual.

Examples that must never degrade:

Permission change:

Must not delay invalidation

Must not fallback to stale cache

Must not queue behind other ops

Rate limit counters:

Must not reset due to failover

Must not evict from critical tier

Must not fall to eventual model

Billing state:

Must not serve stale state

Must not queue write → fail open

Auth token revocation:

Must not delay propagation

Must fail closed if uncertain

Cross-region strong writes:

Must not accept concurrent

writes during partition

⚠ CORRECTNESS INVARIANT:

System may degrade UX.

System may reduce features.

System may return 503.

System must NEVER degrade

correctness for Tier 0 / Tier 1.

Align with Section 21

consistency model declarations.

14\. WRITE AMPLIFICATION &

DUPLICATE WRITE CONTAINMENT

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Write amplification risk declared?

(yes --- always)

⚠ WRITE AMPLIFICATION INVARIANT:

Write amplification scenarios:

1\. Client retries non-idempotent

write on timeout.

2\. Service retries downstream

write after partial success.

3\. Async job reprocesses

already-processed message.

4\. Deploy triggers re-indexing

or cache rebuild flood.

5\. Bulk import creates N²

downstream writes.

For financial operations:

Any duplicate write = potential

double charge or double credit.

Must be prevented at both

sender and receiver.

Detection:

Write deduplication at DB layer?

(yes / no)

Idempotency enforced at

receiver? (yes --- always for

financial operations)

Audit log for duplicate

detection? (yes --- always)

Async job deduplication:

Message deduplication ID?

(yes / no)

At-least-once delivery handled?

(yes --- always)

Exactly-once declared where

required? (yes --- for Tier 1)

Bulk write rate limiting:

Max writes per second: \_\_\_

Bulk write throttled? (yes / no)

Bulk write isolated to

bulk pool? (yes --- align

Section 08 bulkhead)

16\. HEALTH CHECK GOVERNANCE

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

(yes --- always)

⚠ HEALTH CHECK INVARIANT:

A lying health check is more

dangerous than no health check.

False healthy = load balancer

keeps routing to broken node.

False sick = load balancer

removes healthy node =

unnecessary capacity loss =

load spikes on remaining nodes

= cascade.

Liveness check:

Purpose: is the process alive?

Check: process running + can

respond to HTTP

Used by: container orchestrator

to restart crashed containers

Must NOT check: DB / cache /

external dependencies

(external dependency failure

must not cause restart loop)

Response time: \< \_\_\_ ms

Purpose: is instance ready

to serve traffic?

Check: can reach DB? /

can reach cache? /

warm? / migrations complete?

Used by: load balancer to

route or not route traffic

Failure = remove from rotation

(not restart)

Response time: \< \_\_\_ ms

Startup probe:

Purpose: is startup complete?

Check: migrations done /

cache warmed / connections

established

Used by: orchestrator to

delay liveness checks during

slow start

Timeout: \_\_\_ seconds

(prevents premature restart

during cold start)

Health check abuse prevention:

Health endpoints rate limited?

(yes --- always)

Health endpoints auth-free?

(yes --- but rate limited)

Health check not cacheable?

(yes --- always)

17\. GRACEFUL SHUTDOWN

[OPERATIONAL]

Graceful shutdown declared?

(yes --- always)

⚠ GRACEFUL SHUTDOWN INVARIANT:

Without graceful shutdown:

Deploy or restart sends SIGTERM.

In-flight requests are dropped.

DB transactions mid-flight

rolled back or left open.

Queue consumers mid-processing

leave messages unacked.

Messages requeued = duplicate

processing risk.

Clients see 502 / 503 errors

during every deploy.

Shutdown sequence:

1\. Stop accepting new requests

(remove from load balancer

rotation or set readiness

to false)

2\. Wait for in-flight requests

to complete:

Drain timeout: \_\_\_ seconds

If not drained by timeout:

Force close? (yes / no)

Log incomplete: (yes)

3\. Flush async job queue:

Ack in-progress messages

before shutdown

4\. Close DB connections cleanly

5\. Close cache connections cleanly

6\. Exit

SIGTERM handling:

Caught? (yes --- always)

Drain initiated on SIGTERM?

(yes --- always)

Drain timeout: \_\_\_ seconds

SIGKILL after drain timeout?

(yes --- orchestrator handles)

In-flight request protection:

New requests rejected during

drain? (yes --- always)

503 returned during drain?

(yes --- with Retry-After header)

In-flight requests allowed

to complete? (yes --- up to

drain timeout)

Queue consumer shutdown:

Stop polling on SIGTERM?

(yes --- always)

Complete current message

before stopping? (yes --- always)

Ack only on clean completion?

(yes --- always)

Nack / requeue on interrupt?

(yes --- always)

⚠ VERSION MISMATCH INVARIANT:

backward compatible.

All schema changes must use

expand-contract pattern.

If migration fails:

Rollback safe? (yes --- always)

Cache invalidation safe

during rollback? (yes --- always)

Cold start protection:

Pre-warm cache on deploy?

(yes / no)

Gradual traffic shift?

(yes --- always for canary)

Deploy must not:

Cause invalidation storm

Trigger stampede

Re-index everything at once

Exhaust connection pool

on startup

Analytics ingestion

Propagation SLA: \_\_\_ seconds

Audit logged? (yes --- always)

⚠ KILL SWITCH INVARIANT:

and operate even during

partial outage.

in production.

24\. RESOURCE PROTECTION

[OPERATIONAL]

CPU guard:

If CPU \> \_\_\_% for \_\_\_ seconds:

Shed non-critical load

If CPU \> \_\_\_% for \_\_\_ seconds:

Emergency load shed

Memory guard:

If memory \> \_\_\_%:

Reject new requests

If memory \> \_\_\_%:

Alert + prepare restart

Memory leak detection:

Leak pattern detected?

(yes / no)

Threshold: \_\_\_MB growth

per \_\_\_ minutes with no

traffic increase

Response: alert + schedule

rolling restart

Auto-restart on OOM:

(yes --- always)

⚠ MEMORY LEAK INVARIANT:

Slow memory leak causes

eventual OOM crash.

Sudden crash under load is

worse than scheduled restart.

Detect leak pattern early.

Schedule restart during

low-traffic window.

Never wait for OOM.

Connection pool guard:

If DB pool \> \_\_\_%:

Degrade endpoints (bulkhead)

If DB pool \> \_\_\_%:

Emergency reject

Thread pool guard:

If blocked threads \> \_\_\_:

Reject new traffic

If blocked threads \> \_\_\_:

Alert + circuit break

No automatic scaling without

rate limiting.

Scaling does not fix retry storms.

Scaling amplifies retry storms.

§23 — PERFORMANCE ENGINEERING &

CAPACITY GOVERNANCE

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Always

[PURPOSE] → Ensure predictable latency,

sustainable growth, bounded

cost, saturation prevention,

tenant fairness, and capacity

stability under growth, burst,

imbalance, and cold-start

conditions --- without relying

on reactive resilience

mechanisms.

Do NOT assume:

Horizontal scaling fixes DB

contention.

Autoscaling reacts instantly.

Traffic growth is linear.

Peak = 2× baseline.

p50 represents user experience.

CPU saturation is primary

failure mode.

GC pauses are negligible.

Lock contention scales linearly.

Cold starts are harmless.

Queue growth is slow.

Cost scales proportionally

to traffic.

Read path and write path have

the same bottleneck.

Query plans are stable over time.

Connection pool size is arbitrary.

Network bandwidth is infinite.

Cache hit rate is constant.

Cache key cardinality is stable.

Third-party latency fits in

your total budget.

Logging is free on hot paths.

Performance regressions are

always visible.

Seasonal spikes can be handled

reactively.

Load test results are truthful

without open-loop mode.

End-to-end p99 = worst

component p99.

OS resource limits are

never hit.

TLS overhead is negligible

under burst.

All threads in a pool are

equal priority.

App metrics tell the whole story.

Response buffering is harmless.

JIT-compiled code is optimized

from first request.

Timestamps are always accurate.

Assume:

10× burst events occur.

Tenants are imbalanced.

Traffic spikes faster than

scaling reacts.

Hot keys appear.

Lock contention becomes

dominant bottleneck.

Performance regresses over time.

Error budgets get consumed

silently.

Cost grows superlinearly.

Query plans change silently

after data volume growth.

One slow endpoint drags p99

for the entire service.

CDN hit rate degradation

causes origin overload.

Performance cliffs occur at

70-80%, not at 100%.

Fan-out multiplies tail latency

superlinearly.

File descriptors and ports

exhaust before CPU does.

TLS dominates CPU during

burst and cold reconnect.

Long tasks starve short tasks

inside shared pools.

Cache key cardinality explosion

collapses hit rate math.

Response buffering causes

memory spikes independent

of payload size limits.

Shared infrastructure contends

silently outside app layer.

Design for predictability,

not just peak survival.

All decisions must reference:

• Section 07 --- Data Model

(index design, query patterns,

write amplification)

• Section 08 --- API Design

(payload size, response shape,

streaming)

• Section 11 --- Search & Discovery

(search query performance)

• Section 13 --- Async Processing

(job throughput, worker math)

• Section 16 --- Rate Governance

(per-tenant caps, fairness)

• Section 21 --- Caching

(cache hit rate math, cache miss

→ DB load, key cardinality

attack prevention)

• Section 22 --- Resilience

(brownout, backpressure,

autoscale stability, clock sync)

• Section 27 --- Observability

(all performance metrics)

1\. SLO & ERROR BUDGET GOVERNANCE

[GOVERNANCE]

SLO per critical path declared?

(yes --- always)

User sync request:

p50 ≤ \_\_\_ ms

p95 ≤ \_\_\_ ms

p99 ≤ \_\_\_ ms

Auth:

p99 ≤ \_\_\_ ms

Payment:

p99 ≤ \_\_\_ ms

Search:

p95 ≤ \_\_\_ ms

p99 ≤ \_\_\_ ms

Async job end-to-end:

≤ \_\_\_ seconds

Availability SLO:

≥ \_\_\_%

Error budget per 30 days:

\_\_\_ minutes downtime allowed

⚠ ERROR BUDGET INVARIANT:

Error budget consumption must

be tracked continuously.

Silent consumption = sprint-end

surprise.

If error budget consumed

\> \_\_\_%:

Feature releases slowed?

(yes / no)

Performance work prioritized?

(yes --- recommended)

Percentile measurement accuracy:

p99 window: \_\_\_ minutes

(too short = noisy,

too long = masks regression)

Histogram bucket resolution:

\_\_\_ ms

⚠ PERCENTILE ALIASING INVARIANT:

p99 over a 1-hour window hides

a 10-minute spike affecting

thousands of users.

Recommended: 5-minute rolling

window, ≤ 10ms bucket resolution.

Clock skew impact on metrics:

⚠ CLOCK SKEW METRICS INVARIANT:

Latency is measured as:

response_time - request_time.

If timestamps from different

nodes have clock drift:

Latency calculations are wrong.

p99 can appear to improve when

it is actually worsening ---

or vice versa.

SLO violations become invisible.

Histograms mis-bucket events.

NTP enforced? (yes --- always)

Max clock drift: \_\_\_ ms

(align Section 22 clock sync)

Clock drift \> threshold →

alert: metrics unreliable

Clock drift monitoring:

Enabled? (yes --- always)

Align with Section 22

distributed clock sync.

Performance regression allowed

per release:

Max p99 increase: \_\_\_%

Max memory increase: \_\_\_%

Max CPU increase: \_\_\_%

Max error rate increase: \_\_\_%

Deploy blocked on regression?

(yes / no)

SLO ownership:

Owner: \_\_\_

Review cadence: \_\_\_ weeks

SLO missed → escalation: \_\_\_

2\. PER-ENDPOINT PERFORMANCE BUDGET

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

Per-endpoint SLO declared?

(yes --- always)

⚠ ENDPOINT DRAG INVARIANT:

A single slow endpoint drags

p99 for the entire service.

Service-level p99 is the

worst-performing endpoint's

p99 weighted by traffic.

Without per-endpoint SLOs,

you cannot identify which

endpoint causes SLO violations.

Declare per endpoint:

Endpoint: \_\_\_

Traffic %: \_\_\_

p50 budget: \_\_\_ ms

p99 budget: \_\_\_ ms

Max payload size: \_\_\_ KB

Cache eligible? (yes / no)

Read or write path? (declare)

Top contributors to p99:

Top 5 by traffic × latency: \_\_\_

Top 3 by p99 latency: \_\_\_

Monitored individually:

(yes --- always)

Endpoint performance contract:

Locked per release? (yes / no)

Regression = deploy blocked?

(yes / no)

3\. LATENCY BUDGET MATHEMATICS

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

Total latency budget must equal

sum of all components.

Component breakdown:

Total API p99: \_\_\_ ms

Network: \_\_\_ ms

Gateway: \_\_\_ ms

App logic: \_\_\_ ms

Cache: \_\_\_ ms

DB (read): \_\_\_ ms

DB (write): \_\_\_ ms

Third-party: \_\_\_ ms

Serialization: \_\_\_ ms

TLS handshake: \_\_\_ ms

Sum must equal total.

⚠ LATENCY MATH INVARIANT:

If component budgets exceed

total --- SLO is violated

under ideal load.

This is a design-time error.

Check the math before building.

Cross-service tail latency

amplification:

⚠ TAIL AMPLIFICATION INVARIANT:

End-to-end p99 is NOT the

worst individual component p99.

It is worse --- often much worse.

Sequential calls:

A (p99=200ms) → B (p99=200ms)

→ C (p99=200ms)

End-to-end p99 ≈ sum of

component p99s in worst case.

≈ 600ms, not 200ms.

Parallel / fan-out calls:

A calls B, C, D in parallel.

End-to-end p99 = p99 of

SLOWEST of B, C, D.

With 10 parallel calls each

at p99=50ms:

End-to-end p99 \>\> 50ms.

Each additional parallel call

increases the probability that

at least one is slow.

Fan-out factor declared:

Max parallel downstream

calls per request: \_\_\_

End-to-end p99 modeled?

(yes --- required)

Tail amplification budget:

\_\_\_ ms added for fan-out

Fan-out p99 formula declared:

(statistical model /

empirical measurement /

declare)

⚠ FAN-OUT INVARIANT:

Any request that fans out to

N parallel services will

have end-to-end p99 worse

than any individual service.

Latency budget must account

for this mathematically,

not assume best case.

If fan-out p99 budget exceeds

total: redesign call pattern

(sequential hedging /

async fan-out / declare).

Third-party in latency budget:

Third-party p99: \_\_\_ ms

⚠ If third-party p99 \>

remaining budget after

other components:

SLO violation is guaranteed.

Move non-critical third-party

calls to async.

Third-party on sync path: \_\_\_

Third-party moved to async: \_\_\_

Serialization cost:

Format: JSON / Protobuf /

MessagePack / declare

Max response payload: \_\_\_ KB

Max request payload: \_\_\_ KB

Serialization p99: \_\_\_ ms

at max payload

Pagination enforced?

(yes --- always for lists)

Max page size: \_\_\_

Response streaming:

Large responses streamed?

(yes / no)

⚠ STREAMING INVARIANT:

Without streaming:

Full response buffered in

memory before first byte sent.

Large response × many

concurrent requests =

memory spike independent

of payload size limit.

Pagination limits size.

Streaming limits memory.

Both are needed.

Max in-memory response

buffer: \_\_\_ KB

Chunked transfer supported?

(yes / no)

Streaming on endpoints with

response \> \_\_\_ KB:

(yes --- recommended)

TLS cost in latency budget:

Edge / app / declare

TLS handshake overhead: \_\_\_ ms

Keep-alive enabled?

(yes --- always)

Connection reuse ratio

target: \_\_\_%

⚠ TLS SATURATION INVARIANT:

Under burst traffic, cold

start, or CDN failover:

All clients reconnect

simultaneously.

TLS handshake dominates CPU

before application logic runs.

CPU saturates on TLS, not app.

You add app nodes.

TLS overhead does not decrease.

You are solving the wrong

problem.

Keep-alive and connection reuse

eliminate most TLS overhead.

TLS handshake CPU monitored?

(yes / no)

Ephemeral port exhaustion:

Monitored? (yes / no)

⚠ EPHEMERAL PORT INVARIANT:

Each outbound connection uses

one ephemeral port.

High volume of outbound calls

(third-party APIs, internal

services, DB connections):

Port range: 32768-60999

= \~28000 ports available.

At high call rate, ports

exhaust before CPU does.

System can no longer make

outbound connections.

TCP TIME_WAIT holds ports

for 2× MSL (typically 60s).

Mitigation: connection reuse /

keep-alive / declare

(SO_REUSEPORT / declare)

9\. CACHE PERFORMANCE MATH

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

Cache performance math declared?

(yes --- always)

⚠ CACHE MISS AMPLIFICATION

INVARIANT:

DB queries/sec =

total_rps × (1 - hit_rate)

1000 rps at 95% hit rate

= 50 DB queries/sec

1000 rps at 80% hit rate

= 200 DB queries/sec

15% hit rate drop = 4× DB load.

DB may not survive this.

Cache performance targets:

Normal load hit rate: \_\_\_%

Peak load hit rate: \_\_\_%

Minimum acceptable: \_\_\_%

Below minimum → alert

Below minimum → DB protection

mode? (yes / no)

At minimum hit rate:

DB queries/sec = \_\_\_

DB capacity sufficient?

(yes / no)

If no: declare mitigation.

Cache key cardinality explosion:

⚠ CARDINALITY EXPLOSION INVARIANT:

Cache hit rate math assumes

stable key cardinality.

If cardinality explodes:

Cache fills with unique keys.

Eviction storm.

Hit rate collapses.

DB load spikes as if hit rate

dropped --- but root cause is

cardinality, not traffic.

Cardinality explosion is

invisible in hit rate metrics

until after collapse.

Section 21 defines the attack

prevention mechanism.

Section 23 must declare the

performance math consequence.

Key cardinality per endpoint:

Declared? (yes / no)

\_\_\_

(yes --- always)

alert linkage declared?

(yes --- always)

reject / declare

total × (1 - CDN_hit_rate)

CDN degradation threshold:

below \_\_\_% → origin overload

CDN hit rate monitored?

(yes --- always)

CDN hit rate drops →

origin pre-scale triggered?

(yes / no)

⚠ CDN OFFLOAD INVARIANT:

CDN 90% hit rate → 10% to origin.

Hit rate drops to 50%:

Origin traffic increases 5×

instantaneously.

Autoscaling cannot react.

CDN degradation must trigger

pre-emptive origin scaling.

Bulkheads separate pools by

service type.

Long tasks block short tasks.

A few 30-second export jobs

occupy all threads.

Auth requests queue behind them.

Pool utilization: 100%.

Auth p99: degraded.

Cause: not pool exhaustion ---

priority inversion within

the pool.

Visible only if task duration

is monitored independently

of pool utilization.

16\. SHARED INFRASTRUCTURE

⚠ SHARED INFRASTRUCTURE INVARIANT:

Application metrics --- CPU,

memory, thread pool --- can all

look healthy while the system

degrades from outside the

app layer.

Root cause: shared physical or

virtual infrastructure.

Examples:

Shared VPC bandwidth: two

services on same host compete

for NIC bandwidth.

Service A's bulk export

saturates the NIC.

Service B's auth responses

are delayed.

App metrics: both healthy.

Symptom: latency correlation

between unrelated services.

Shared storage IOPS: DB and

log volume on same disk.

Log flush saturates IOPS.

DB writes queue.

DB CPU looks fine.

DB write latency spikes.

Shared Kubernetes node:

Resource contention between

pods on same node.

CPU throttling from other

pod's burst.

Node-level noisy neighbor.

Declare:

Shared VPC bandwidth

monitored? (yes / no)

Per-node bandwidth usage

monitored? (yes / no)

\_\_\_ IOPS

21\. LOAD TESTING CORRECTNESS

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Load testing mode declared?

(yes --- always)

⚠ COORDINATED OMISSION INVARIANT:

This is the most common and

dangerous load testing flaw.

If your load generator waits

for a response before sending

the next request (closed-loop):

When the system stalls for 3s,

the load generator also stalls.

It does not send the requests

that real users are sending.

You measure low average latency.

Real users experienced a 3s stall.

Your load test says: system fine.

Your production users say:

system broken.

The test is lying.

Coordinated omission hides:

• Latency under saturation

• Queue buildup behavior

• Thundering herd recovery time

• Real p99 under sustained load

Load generator mode:

Open-loop (constant arrival

rate)? (yes --- required for

saturation tests)

Closed-loop (wait for response)?

(allowed only for: \_\_\_ tests)

Tool: k6 / Gatling / wrk2 /

Locust (open-loop mode) /

declare

⚠ wrk without -R flag is

closed-loop. wrk2 with -R

is open-loop. Declare

explicitly which is used.

Arrival rate declared:

Baseline test: \_\_\_ req/sec

Peak test: \_\_\_ req/sec

Saturation test: \_\_\_ req/sec

(arrival rate fixed,

latency measured)

2× peak

(FD / port exhaustion)

(if applicable)

end-to-end budget

(no new connections)

(no outbound calls possible)

(keep-alive disabled /

saturated by co-tenant

= DB meltdown

shared DB

§24 — DEPLOYMENT & RELEASE

GOVERNANCE

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Always

[PURPOSE] → Ensure deployments,

migrations, config changes,

dependency upgrades, secret

rotation, feature rollouts,

region rollouts, and rollbacks

cannot violate correctness,

performance, availability,

security, compatibility,

residency, or observability

guarantees --- even under version

skew, partial rollout, autoscale

interaction, rate limit state,

or failure.

Design for:

Version skew (sync + async)

Schema skew

Semantic data skew

Cache schema skew (Section 21)

Event schema skew

Token structure skew

In-flight job skew

Region skew

Feature flag skew

Config skew (v1 app + v2 config)

Config drift

Secret rotation overlap

Autoscaler race

Deploy under load

Canary false negative

Rollback under load

Rollback into v2 schema

Dependency default change

Backup restore incompatibility

Certificate rotation skew

Clock skew from image change

Shadow traffic side effects

Data residency violation

Rate limit state during deploy

DB connection surge on deploy

Observability gap during deploy

Supply chain attack surface

Environment parity gap

Async consumer deploy ordering

Flag lifecycle debt

Non-DB global state migration

Post-deploy correction job

Audit log compliance gap

Assume:

Old and new versions run

simultaneously.

Deploy fails mid-way.

Rollback happens under load.

Migrations partially applied.

Async jobs span deploy window.

Autoscaler active during rollout.

Feature flags toggled mid-rollout.

Secrets rotate mid-deploy.

Library upgrades change behaviour

silently.

Metrics renamed accidentally.

Backup restore attempted under

newer schema.

DB connection pool × new instances

can exceed DB max_connections.

Rate limit state is per-instance

unless explicitly global.

Canary traffic is not

automatically representative.

Staging is not automatically

identical to production.

Consumer deployed after producer

= event version mismatch.

Config key removed during skew

window = v1 crash.

New config key without safe

default = silent misconfiguration.

Redis key format change without

dual-write = cache miss storm.

Rate limit key format change

= counter split = bypass window.

Post-deploy correction job

unthrottled = DB overload.

Audit log format change =

silent compliance gap.

Do NOT assume:

Rollback restores DB schema.

Schema compatibility implies

semantic compatibility.

Cache entries are version-neutral.

Event consumers upgrade instantly.

Canary traffic is representative.

Health check implies semantic

correctness.

Default timeout values remain

stable after dependency upgrade.

Infrastructure identical across

regions.

TLS rotation is atomic.

Clock drift cannot be introduced

via container image change.

Rate limits survive rolling deploy

if stored per-instance.

Staging parity is maintained

automatically.

Deploy pipeline is not an

attack surface.

Config backward compatibility

is automatic.

Global state survives key format

change without migration.

Correction jobs are harmless

background work.

Audit log breakage is visible

in monitoring.

All decisions must reference:

• Section 06 --- Auth & Sessions

(session key format migration)

• Section 13 --- Async Processing

(correction job governance;

secret rotation overlap)

• Section 16 --- Rate Governance

(rate limit key format must be

global, not per-instance)

• Section 18 --- Security

(audit log governance)

• Section 19 --- Privacy & Compliance

(residency; audit compliance)

• Section 21 --- Caching

(cache schema version scheme ---

Section 24 must use same scheme;

global state key versioning)

• Section 22 --- Resilience

(graceful shutdown drain timeout

must be \< rollback SLA;

autoscaler suspension;

brownout during deploy;

config drift detection)

• Section 23 --- Performance

(connection surge on deploy;

autoscale cold start;

JIT warmup; DB CPU protection

for correction jobs)

• Section 27 --- Observability

(deploy markers; metric rename

dual-emit; alert continuity;

audit log pipeline health)

CHANGE CONTROL

(yes --- always)

Undeclared deploy authorization

means anyone can deploy anything

at any time.

In production this is a security

and availability risk.

PR review / deploy gate /

declare

(yes / no)

If yes: post-deploy review

required? (yes --- always)

Hotfix approver: \_\_\_

Hotfix audit logged?

(yes --- always)

Periods declared? (yes / no)

Examples: major releases /

holidays / end-of-quarter /

declare

Freeze override process: \_\_\_

Override audit logged?

(yes --- always)

Prohibited unless hotfix?

(yes --- recommended)

can worsen incident.

Change freeze during P0/P1?

(yes --- recommended)

Exception: hotfix for the

active incident only.

2\. VERSIONING & COMPATIBILITY MODEL

[GOVERNANCE]

Backward compatibility enforced?

(yes --- always)

Supported concurrent versions: \_\_\_

Breaking change policy:

No required field removal

No semantic mutation without

version bump

Additive changes preferred

Major version required for

breaking API change

⚠ VERSION SKEW INVARIANT:

During rolling deploy:

Service A (v2) ↔ Service B (v1)

All interactions must tolerate

version skew for the full

skew window duration.

2A. SEMANTIC DATA COMPATIBILITY

⚠ SCHEMA COMPATIBLE ≠

SEMANTICALLY SAFE:

A column can be added without

breaking deserialization.

But its semantic meaning can

change behavior silently.

Enum evolution:

Unknown enum values:

Ignored / mapped / rejected /

declare

Old nodes tolerate new enum?

(yes --- required)

State machine evolution:

New states backward-compatible?

(yes --- required)

Old version tolerates new states?

(yes --- required)

Data contract version embedded?

(yes / no)

2B. TOKEN & AUTH STRUCTURE

COMPATIBILITY

JWT / token schema versioned?

(yes --- required)

Claim additions:

Backward-compatible? (yes)

Claim removals:

Prohibited without version bump.

Validation rules version-aware?

(yes --- required)

2C. RATE LIMIT STATE COMPATIBILITY

⚠ RATE LIMIT STATE INVARIANT:

During rolling deploy, instance

count changes.

If rate limit counters are stored

per-instance (in-process memory):

New instances start at zero.

Old instances have full counters.

Effective rate limit fluctuates

during deploy.

Users may get more or fewer

requests allowed mid-deploy.

Rate limits must be stored

globally (Redis-backed) to

survive rolling deploy correctly.

Align with Section 16.

Rate limit storage: global

(Redis-backed)? (yes --- required)

Rate limit state preserved

through rolling deploy?

(yes --- required)

Per-instance rate limit counters

prohibited? (yes --- always)

1\. Expand (nullable / additive)

closed)

Blocking DDL prohibited under

peak load? (yes --- must be yes)

DDL lock safety:

⚠ DDL LOCK INVARIANT:

ALTER TABLE on a large table

acquires a full table lock.

Duration: seconds to hours

depending on table size.

All reads and writes queue

behind the lock.

This is an outage, not a

migration.

Lock timeout: \_\_\_ ms

Lock wait timeout: \_\_\_ ms

Online DDL tool required for

tables \> \_\_\_ rows:

pg_repack / gh-ost /

pt-online-schema-change /

declare

production-volume data?

(yes --- required)

Migration duration estimate: \_\_\_

Deploy window accounts for

migration duration? (yes --- always)

Backfill throttle:

\_\_\_ rows/sec

Pause if DB CPU \> \_\_\_%

Rollback possible during expand?

(yes --- required)

Rollback into v2 schema:

⚠ SCHEMA ROLLBACK INVARIANT:

App v1 rolled back.

Schema remains at v2.

App v1 was tested against

v1 schema --- not v2.

New columns must be nullable

or have defaults.

New tables must be ignorable

by v1.

New enum values handled by v1

(ignored or mapped to default).

v1 ↔ v2 schema compatibility

explicitly tested?

(yes --- required)

Tested in: staging with

v2 schema + v1 app.

(yes --- required)

Explicit human approval required

before irreversible migration.

Seed data ordering declared?

(yes --- required)

(yes / no)

4\. DATABASE CONNECTION SURGE

ON DEPLOY

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

⚠ DEPLOY CONNECTION SURGE

INVARIANT:

During rolling deploy, new

instances start simultaneously

within the surge window.

Each opens its connection pool

on startup.

pool_size × new_instances_at_once

= connection burst to DB.

If burst \> DB max_connections:

DB refuses connections.

New instances fail to start.

Deploy fails.

Align with Section 23 connection

pool math.

Pre-deploy connection headroom

check:

Current connections: \_\_\_

Max DB connections: \_\_\_

New instances in surge: \_\_\_

Connections per instance: \_\_\_

Surge total =

current + (new × pool_size)

Must be ≤ DB max_connections.

Deploy blocked if headroom

insufficient? (yes --- always)

Max new instances per surge: \_\_\_

Lazy connection init?

(yes / no --- lazy reduces surge)

Min pool on startup: \_\_\_

Max pool after warmup: \_\_\_

5\. CACHE SCHEMA VERSIONING

DURING DEPLOY

⚠ CACHE SCHEMA ALIGNMENT

INVARIANT:

versioning scheme as Section 21.

Two independent cache versioning

systems = contradictory behavior

during deploy.

Single source of truth:

Section 21 cache schema version

registry governs both normal

operation and deploy-time

compatibility.

Cache key version suffix:

Required? (yes --- align Section 21)

Cache value schema version

embedded? (yes --- align Section 21)

On schema mismatch during deploy:

Invalidate + re-fetch /

fallback / declare

(strategy aligns Section 21

mismatch handling)

Cache compatibility tested in

deploy rehearsal?

(yes --- required)

Old version keys purged after

deploy completes?

(yes --- align Section 21)

⚠ EVENT VERSION SKEW INVARIANT:

Async skew window is longer

than sync skew window.

Messages produced under v1

may be consumed under v2

and vice versa.

Async consumer deploy ordering:

⚠ CONSUMER ORDERING INVARIANT:

Correct order:

Deploy consumer BEFORE producer.

If producer deployed first:

New event schema emitted.

Old consumer receives it.

Old consumer fails or corrupts.

Consumer-first order enforced?

(yes --- always)

Deploy order documented?

(yes --- always)

Pipeline enforces ordering?

(yes / no)

12A. CONFIG VERSION SKEW

COMPATIBILITY

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

Config backward compatibility

across rolling deploy declared?

(yes --- always)

⚠ CONFIG VERSION SKEW INVARIANT:

Config skew is as dangerous

as schema skew.

During rolling deploy:

v2 instances read v2 config.

v1 instances read same config.

If v2 config adds a key:

v1 uses hardcoded default ---

which may be wrong or missing.

If v2 config removes a key:

v1 still expects it.

v1 crashes or uses stale value.

Config backward compatibility

window:

\_\_\_ versions supported

(must equal or exceed rolling

deploy version skew window)

New config keys:

Must have safe defaults?

(yes --- required)

Safe default declared per

new key? (yes --- always)

v1 app + v2 config with new key:

uses declared default,

does not crash.

Config key removal policy:

Only after full skew window?

(yes --- required)

Sequence:

1\. Mark key deprecated

2\. Verify no v1 instances

reading key

3\. Wait full skew window:

\_\_\_ minutes

4\. Remove key

Premature key removal =

v1 crash. Non-negotiable.

Config schema version:

Embedded in config payload?

(yes / no)

Validated on load?

(yes --- required)

Unknown version:

Reject / fallback / declare

Config compatibility testing:

v1 app + v2 config tested?

(yes --- required)

v2 app + v1 config tested?

(yes --- required)

Both directions required.

Tested in staging with

mixed-version deploy.

Tested before every config

schema change deploy.

Config skew window =

version skew window from

Section 08 (deploy strategy).

Config changes must be safe

throughout the transition ---

not just at start or end.

Align with:

Section 12 (config governance)

Section 22 (config drift)

Section 08 (version skew window)

DB load spikes 2×.

Effective rate limit halved.

Rate limit bypass window open

for entire deploy duration.

v2 writes new session format.

v1 cannot read it.

Users on v1 instances logged

out mid-session.

Tier 0 failure.

change:

v2 reads new format.

v1 reads old format.

Some instances: flag ON.

Some instances: flag OFF.

Unpredictable behavior.

(yes --- required)

⚠ POST-DEPLOY CORRECTION INVARIANT:

A deploy fixes a bug.

to correct affected data.

Different from migration backfill:

• Runs after deploy completes

• Touches millions of rows

• Competes with live traffic

• Not always in migration files

• Engineers forget to throttle

• DB CPU spikes = p99 degrades

= SLO violated by the fix,

not the original bug

Rollback interaction:

App rolled back after correction

ran = corrected data + v1 logic

= untested combination.

(yes --- required)

(yes --- required)

(align Section 23 SLO)

(yes --- required)

p99 \< \_\_\_ ms for \_\_\_ sec

Off-peak preferred?

(yes --- recommended)

Off-peak window: \_\_\_

Can run during peak if

throttled? (yes / no)

Stoppable mid-run?

(yes --- required)

(yes / no)

24\. DEPLOYMENT FAILURE MODES

[GOVERNANCE]

Define explicit response for:

Canary regression detected:

→ auto rollback canary

→ scope decision matrix

→ data corruption = full fleet

→ financial issue = full fleet

\+ freeze writes

Migration partial apply:

→ pause deploy

→ assess forward vs rollback

→ irreversible = escalate

DDL lock timeout exceeded:

→ abort DDL immediately

→ retry with online DDL tool

→ never hold lock indefinitely

DB connection surge on deploy:

→ pre-deploy check failed

→ reduce surge wave size

→ increase DB connection limit

Schema v1 app + v2 schema

(rollback into v2 schema):

→ v1 app must tolerate v2

→ verify before deploy

→ if not tolerable:

forward-only, no rollback

Seed data missing:

→ block deploy

→ run seed first

Feature flag misfire:

→ disable flag immediately

→ rollback if needed

→ audit log reviewed

Config invalid at deploy:

→ reject deploy

→ validation gate catches

Config key removed during

skew window:

→ v1 instance crashes

→ deploy blocked: key removal

only after skew window

→ rollback config if removed

New config key has no safe

default:

→ v1 gets nil / zero / wrong

→ silent misconfiguration

→ block deploy: default required

v1 app + v2 config incompatible:

→ v1 crash or wrong behavior

→ deploy blocked: compat test

required

Redis key format changed

without dual-write:

→ cache miss storm

→ DB load spikes 2×

→ expand--contract required

for all key format changes

Rate limit key format split

during deploy:

→ counters split across formats

→ effective rate limit halved

→ rate limit bypass window

→ emergency: consolidate

to single format immediately

→ align Section 16

Session key format change

without migration:

→ v1 users logged out

→ Tier 0 failure

→ rollback session format

or complete deploy immediately

Feature flag state inconsistent

across versions:

→ disable flag immediately

→ investigate + re-enable

after full deploy

Cache eviction policy changed

mid-deploy:

→ defer to post-deploy

→ mixed eviction = unexpected

evictions on some instances

Secret rotation overlap failure:

→ hold both keys

→ alert + manual intervention

→ never drop old key during

active sessions

Token schema mismatch:

→ version-aware validation

→ reject unknown version

→ alert

Cache schema mismatch on deploy:

→ auto-invalidate (Section 21)

→ re-fetch from source

Event version mismatch:

→ consumer tolerates unknown

→ DLQ for unprocessable

→ alert

Consumer deployed after producer:

→ event version mismatch

→ DLQ fills

→ rollback producer or

deploy consumer immediately

Long-running job conflict:

→ state machine compatible

→ escalate if not

Post-deploy correction job

unthrottled:

→ DB CPU spike → p99 degrades

→ kill job immediately

→ reschedule throttled off-peak

Post-deploy correction job

cannot be stopped:

→ escalate immediately --- P0

→ data integrity risk

→ runbook must exist before

job runs

App rolled back after

irreversible correction ran:

→ v1 app + corrected data

→ untested combination

→ escalate immediately

→ may require forward-only

Audit log gap during deploy:

→ compliance violation risk

→ alert immediately

→ investigate: format mismatch /

destination change /

encryption mismatch

→ notify compliance team

Audit log format incompatible

with pipeline:

→ silent rejection by pipeline

→ deploy blocked or rolled back

→ dual-format acceptance

required during transition

Audit log encryption key changed

without overlap:

→ v1 writes unreadable

→ dual-key period required

→ align Section 13

Audit pipeline fails deploy

gate validation:

→ deploy blocked

→ fix pipeline before proceeding

Autoscaler race with deploy:

→ autoscaler suspended during

deploy window + buffer

Brownout during deploy:

→ deploy pauses immediately

→ resume after brownout exits

\+ stability window

→ align Section 22

DNS propagation delay:

→ health check before route

→ not routed until ready

Cert renewal failure:

→ dual cert active

→ fallback to old cert

→ alert + manual

Backup restore incompatibility:

→ schema version mismatch

→ restore to schema-matched env

→ alert

Clock drift after deploy:

→ traffic not accepted

→ clock sync required first

→ align Section 23 metrics

Shadow traffic side effect:

→ suppress + alert

→ handler audit required

Residency misroute post-deploy:

→ route blocked

→ DPO alerted

→ deploy rolled back

Rate limit state lost:

→ per-instance counter risk

→ enforce global Redis-backed

rate limits always

Metric renamed without dual-emit:

→ alert gap for that metric

→ deploy hold until dual-emit

configured

\`latest\` tag deployed:

→ unknown version in production

→ rollback impossible

→ block deploy: commit hash

required

Stale feature flag active:

→ review + cleanup required

→ flag age \> max age = alert

Pipeline compromise:

→ artifact signature invalid

→ deploy blocked

→ security incident declared

Each mapped to:

Pause / Rollback / Forward-only /

Freeze traffic / Alert /

Escalate / Block

§25 — SECURITY HARDENING &

THREAT MODELING

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Always

[PURPOSE] → Ensure the system remains

confidential, correct,

available, compliant,

economically sustainable,

and tenant-isolated under

intentional adversarial

behavior --- including exploit

chaining, privilege escalation,

skew abuse, partial compromise,

economic DoS, cross-layer

desynchronization, deploy-window

attacks, and compliance

operation abuse --- even during

deploy transitions and partial

failures.

DESIGN ASSUMPTIONS

Assume:

Attackers understand distributed

systems.

Attackers test skew windows

(Section 24).

Attackers time attacks to rolling

deploy windows.

Attackers test rate limit format

splits (Section 16 +

Section 24 §12B).

Attackers test cache key version

mismatches (Section 21 +

Section 24 §5).

Attackers test autoscale cost

amplification (Section 23).

Attackers chain small

misalignments across layers.

Internal services can be

compromised.

Supply chain can be compromised.

One tenant can attempt to degrade

others --- economically and

operationally.

Secrets will eventually leak

unless rotated.

Background jobs can be abused.

Side-channels leak information

unless normalized.

Config skew can silently disable

auth controls.

Feature flags can accidentally

gate security controls.

Canary deploy exposes partially

migrated auth logic.

Async revocation can be bypassed

via event version skew.

Correction jobs can bypass

application-layer auth.

Compliance operations (DSAR,

erasure) are attack vectors

if not identity-verified.

Observability pipeline leaks

tenant metadata as

reconnaissance.

Webhook URLs are attacker-

controlled SSRF vectors.

Admin sessions are highest-value

XSS targets.

Pagination endpoints enable

full dataset enumeration.

Job fan-out is an economic

amplification vector.

Do NOT assume:

Gateway guarantees security.

Internal network is trusted.

Performance controls imply

security.

Rate limits cannot be bypassed.

Canary deploy is safe from

exploitation.

Audit logs are always correct.

Feature flags are harmless to

security controls.

Config skew cannot disable auth.

Async revocation propagates

instantly or reliably.

Autoscaler cannot be abused

economically.

Correction jobs are

authorization-exempt.

Timing differences between error

paths are harmless.

Webhook URLs are safe to follow.

Admin panel XSS has limited

blast radius.

DSAR / erasure requests are

self-authenticating.

Heap dumps and crash reports are

not exfiltration paths.

Pagination endpoints are not

enumeration endpoints.

All decisions must reference:

Section 06 --- Auth & Sessions

(session management /

revocation)

Section 13 --- Async Processing

(correction job governance /

secret rotation)

Section 16 --- Rate Governance

(rate limit key format /

global counters)

Section 18 --- Security Audit

(audit log governance)

Section 19 --- Privacy & Compliance

(residency / DSAR / erasure)

Section 21 --- Caching

(cache key scope / version)

Section 22 --- Resilience

(revocation propagation /

circuit breaker)

Section 23 --- Performance

(autoscale / economic DoS /

cardinality)

Section 24 --- Deployment

(skew window / config skew /

correction jobs / canary /

event version skew /

pipeline security)

Section 27 --- Observability

(observability as attack surface)

1\. FORMAL THREAT MODEL

[GOVERNANCE]

Threat model documented?

(yes --- required)

Method:

STRIDE / PASTA / custom (declare)

Assets classified:

PII

Payment data

Auth tokens

Session store

Rate limit store

Cache

Event bus

Async job system

DB

Object storage

Secrets store

CI/CD pipeline

Feature flag system

Admin panel

Audit logs

Observability pipeline

Webhook delivery system

For each asset declare:

Confidentiality impact

Integrity impact

Availability impact

Financial impact

Compliance impact

Blast radius

Adversary classes:

Anonymous external

Authenticated user

Compromised account

Malicious tenant

Insider

Compromised internal service

Supply chain attacker

Threat model review cadence:

\_\_\_ months

Owner: \_\_\_

2\. EXPLOIT CHAIN INVENTORY

[GOVERNANCE + APPLICATION]

⚠ EXPLOIT CHAIN INVARIANT:

Individual controls may be

correct in isolation.

Attackers combine small

misalignments across layers.

Each cross-section seam is

a potential chain link.

Chains must be explicitly

declared and tested ---

not assumed impossible.

Declared exploit chains:

CHAIN 1 --- Config skew

disables auth:

S22 §12A: config key removed

during skew window.

Config key controlled an auth

enforcement flag.

v1 instances lose the key.

Auth check defaults to OFF

or crashes.

Auth not enforced on v1

instances during deploy window.

Attacker routes requests to

v1 instances only.

Mitigation:

Auth must never default to OFF

on missing config key.

Fail-closed always

(Section 2A).

Config schema validation

enforced on load.

Auth config = security-critical

deploy (Section 2A).

CHAIN 2 --- Rate limit key split

\+ brute-force timing:

S22 §12B: rate limit key format

changes during deploy.

Counters split across old and

new key formats.

Effective rate limit halved

per instance set.

Attacker times brute-force

attack to deploy window.

Auth endpoint partially

unprotected during transition.

Mitigation:

Rate limit key format changes

use dual-write (S22 §12B).

Counters merged, not split.

No bypass window.

Align Section 16.

CHAIN 3 --- Cache key version

mismatch + IDOR:

S19 / S22 §5: during rolling

deploy, v1 cache key lacks

tenant scope.

v2 cache key includes tenant

scope.

v1 instance serves cached

response to wrong tenant.

Cross-tenant data exposure

during deploy window.

Mitigation:

Cache key ALWAYS includes

tenant ID regardless of

version (Section 10).

Old keys purged before

traffic shifts.

Align Section 24 §5.

CHAIN 4 --- Canary + partially

migrated auth path:

S22 §8: canary receives subset

of traffic.

v2 has new auth check.

v1 is missing the check.

During canary: some requests

hit v2 (checked), some hit

v1 (unchecked).

Attacker routes only to v1

instances in canary window.

Canary metrics (p99, error rate)

do NOT detect auth regression.

Mitigation:

Canary security gate separate

from performance gate

(Section 2B).

v1 auth ≥ v2 auth during

skew window.

CHAIN 5 --- Async revocation +

event version skew:

S22 §6: revocation event

produced in v2 format.

v1 consumer cannot parse it.

Revocation event dropped.

Session remains valid after

revocation.

Attacker retains access to

revoked account.

Mitigation:

Revocation is synchronous-first

(Section 26).

Revocation event schema:

all supported versions must

be able to consume it.

CHAIN 6 --- Correction job

bypasses auth:

S22 §12C: post-deploy correction

job modifies data directly in DB.

Bypasses application-layer

auth and tenant scoping.

Correction job modifies

permissions table.

Privilege escalation via job.

Mitigation:

Correction jobs must be

tenant-scoped.

Must run under least-privilege

DB role.

Must audit every row modified.

Permissions table modification

= security-critical sign-off

required (Section 03).

CHAIN 7 --- Webhook SSRF:

Attacker registers webhook URL

pointing to internal service

or cloud metadata endpoint.

System follows URL on event.

SSRF to internal services.

Mitigation:

Webhook URL validated against

SSRF blocklist at registration

AND at delivery (Section 16).

CHAIN 8 --- Job fan-out

economic amplification:

Attacker submits single job

that fans out to N child jobs.

No fan-out cap declared.

Worker pool exhausted.

Billing inflated.

Other tenants degraded.

Mitigation:

Per-tenant job fan-out cap

(Section 22).

Cap enforced at submission.

Exploit chain test required

for each declared chain?

(yes --- always)

Chains reviewed at threat model

review cadence? (yes --- always)

Additional chains added as

new seams are discovered?

(yes --- always)

2A. SECURITY-CRITICAL DEPLOY

CLASSIFICATION

[GOVERNANCE]

⚠ SECURITY-CRITICAL DEPLOY

INVARIANT:

Not all deploys carry equal

security risk.

Config changes that affect auth,

rate limiting, encryption, or

audit logging are

security-critical.

They require additional security

review before deploy.

A config key removal that

accidentally disables auth

is a security incident,

not a misconfiguration.

Security-critical deploy when:

Deploy touches auth config

→ security review required

Deploy touches rate limit config

→ security review required

Deploy touches encryption config

→ security review required

Deploy touches audit log config

→ security review required

Deploy modifies permissions model

→ security review required

Deploy changes feature flag that

gates any security control

→ security review required

Correction job touches

permissions table

→ explicit security sign-off

required

Auth fail-closed invariant:

⚠ AUTH FAIL-CLOSED INVARIANT:

Missing config key must never

cause auth to default to ALLOW.

Auth defaults to DENY on any

missing or invalid config.

Crash is acceptable.

Silent bypass is never acceptable.

Enforced at:

Config load time

Auth middleware

Feature flag evaluation

Fail-closed applies to:

Auth enforcement

Rate limiting

Encryption

Audit logging

Tested: config key removed →

system denies, does not allow.

2B. SKEW WINDOW SECURITY

VALIDATION

[GOVERNANCE + OPERATIONAL]

⚠ SKEW WINDOW SECURITY INVARIANT:

During rolling deploy, all version

combinations run simultaneously.

Security invariants must hold

for every combination.

v1 auth must be at least as

secure as v2 auth.

A deploy that weakens auth in

v1 during the skew window

= open security regression window.

v1 auth enforcement during skew:

v1 must enforce all existing

auth checks? (yes --- always)

v2 cannot have FEWER auth

checks than v1 during skew?

(yes --- required)

v2 adds new check:

v1 does not enforce it.

Acceptable if new feature.

NOT acceptable if closes

an active vulnerability.

Active vulnerability fix:

Requires blue-green deploy,

not rolling.

Rolling = skew window =

vuln open on v1 instances

during entire deploy.

Canary security gate:

Canary auto-rollback (Section 24

§8) is based on p99, error rate,

DB CPU.

These do NOT detect:

Auth regression

IDOR exposure

Rate limit bypass

Permission boundary violation

Canary security gate required:

Explicit security test suite

runs against canary before

full rollout.

Tests:

Auth check on all permission

boundaries

IDOR: cross-tenant access

attempted and blocked

Rate limit: bypass attempted

and blocked

Feature flag: security control

still enforced

Canary blocked from full

rollout until security gate

passes? (yes --- required)

Security gate owner: \_\_\_

Security gate cadence:

Every canary deploy.

3\. TRUST BOUNDARIES &

CROSS-LAYER AUTH DESYNC

[APPLICATION + OPERATIONAL]

⚠ AUTH DESYNC INVARIANT:

Gateway auth ≠ internal trust.

An attacker who compromises any

internal service can inject

arbitrary identity headers.

Internal services must verify

identity independently.

Never trust forwarded identity.

Internal services must NOT trust:

X-User-Id

X-Role

X-Tenant

X-Forwarded-For (as auth signal)

Unless cryptographically verified

by the receiving service.

Internal identity derived

only from:

Verified JWT

mTLS service identity

Signed internal service token

Gateway strips identity headers

from external traffic?

(yes --- required)

Internal service-to-service auth:

mTLS enforced? (yes --- recommended)

Service identity validated?

(yes --- required)

Zero-trust internal network

model declared?

(yes --- recommended)

Correction job cross-layer auth:

⚠ CORRECTION JOB AUTH INVARIANT:

Post-deploy correction jobs

(Section 24 §12C) modify data

directly in DB.

They bypass application-layer

authorization paths entirely.

This is a privilege escalation

vector by design.

Must compensate with:

All operations scoped to

declared tenant only

No cross-tenant writes

Validate permissions before

modifying any record

Run under least-privilege

DB role

Audit every single row modified

Security review required

before deploy approval

permissions / roles table:

Prohibited without explicit

security sign-off.

Classified as security-critical

Algorithm rotation procedure:

⚠ ALGORITHM ROTATION INVARIANT:

Algorithm pinning protects

against confusion attacks.

But algorithms must eventually

rotate (e.g. RS256 → ES256).

Without a declared procedure:

Either permanently pinned

to old algorithm (cannot

ever upgrade) OR permanently

accepting multiple algorithms

(confusion attack window open

indefinitely).

Neither is acceptable.

Rotation procedure:

1\. Validator updated to accept

both old and new algorithm

(dual-accept window begins)

2\. New tokens issued with

new algorithm only

3\. Old tokens expire naturally

(max TTL: \_\_\_ hours)

4\. Old algorithm retired after

all old tokens expired +

\_\_\_ day buffer

5\. Validator pinned to new

algorithm only

Dual-algorithm acceptance

window: \_\_\_ days

Validator updated before

new tokens issued?

(yes --- required)

Old algorithm retirement

date: \_\_\_

Session fixation prevention?

(yes --- required)

Session ID regenerated on login?

(yes --- required)

Auth failure timing:

Normalized to prevent

timing-based enumeration.

Align Section 08.

8\. SIDE-CHANNEL PROTECTION

[APPLICATION]

⚠ TIMING SIDE-CHANNEL INVARIANT:

Any timing difference between

code paths reveals state to

attacker.

All auth-adjacent operations

must return in constant time

regardless of outcome.

Response timing normalized for:

Login --- user existence:

User found vs not found:

Identical timing required.

Hash dummy operation if

user not found.

Password reset --- email existence:

"Email found, sending reset"

vs "Email not found":

Identical timing AND

identical response body.

Separate timing channels:

DB lookup + hash dummy

to equalize.

Account lockout:

"Account locked" vs

"Wrong password":

Identical timing required.

⚠ Timing difference between

locked and wrong-password

reveals account existence

AND lockout status.

Tenant existence:

API key validation:

Identical timing regardless

of tenant existence.

Payment validity:

Identical timing for valid

vs invalid payment method.

Auth failure:

All failure reasons return

identical timing.

Uniform error response enforced?

(yes --- required)

Error messages do NOT reveal:

Role names

Internal IDs

SQL fragments

Schema structure

Tenant existence

Account lockout status

Email registration status

User existence

Latency variance audit performed?

(yes --- required)

Cadence: \_\_\_ months

13\. SSRF & INTERNAL ACCESS CONTROL

[APPLICATION]

⚠ SSRF COMPLETENESS INVARIANT:

Dangerous protocols

DNS rebinding paths

172.16.0.0/12 blocked

169.254.0.0/16 blocked

(link-local / metadata)

127.0.0.1 / ::1 blocked

Only declared external domains

permitted? (yes --- recommended)

blocklist enforced?

(yes --- required)

Protocol allowlist:

Only https:// and http://

permitted for outbound.

Blocked:

file://

gopher://

dict://

ftp://

⚠ file://, gopher://, dict://

bypass URL validation if not

explicitly blocked.

Explicitly blocked?

(yes --- required)

(yes / no)

If yes:

validated against internal

IP blocklist?

(yes --- required)

⚠ Attacker uses open redirect

to bypass initial URL

not just the original URL.

Re-validate resolved IP against

internal IP blocklist after

DNS resolution?

(yes --- required)

⚠ DNS rebinding:

URL passes initial validation.

DNS resolves to internal IP

at request time.

Must re-validate after resolution.

28\. FAILURE MODE DECLARATION

[GOVERNANCE]

Explicit response defined for:

Token replay spike:

→ revoke + blacklist

→ alert + investigate

Privilege escalation:

→ freeze affected account

→ audit trail reviewed

→ patch path declared

IDOR detected:

→ freeze endpoint

→ audit cross-tenant access

→ patch + re-test

→ purge affected cache range

→ identify poisoned keys

→ alert

(Chain 3):

→ purge old version keys

→ align Section 24 §5

→ audit cross-tenant hits

→ identify bypass vector

→ close split-counter gap

→ audit abuse window

Rate limit bypass during deploy

(Chain 2):

→ dual-write counters

→ close deploy window

→ audit auth endpoint hits

→ align Section 24 §12B

Redis exposed:

→ revoke all sessions

→ rotate all secrets

→ audit keyspace

Config skew disables auth

(Chain 1):

→ fail-closed immediately

(deny, not allow)

→ rollback config

→ audit bypass window

→ security-critical deploy

review triggered

Feature flag disables auth:

→ disable flag immediately

→ audit affected requests

→ patch + re-test

Auth skew window regression

(Chain 4):

→ pause rolling deploy

→ blue-green required for

active vuln fix

→ canary security gate

before resuming

Async revocation + event skew

(Chain 5):

→ synchronous blacklist holds

→ fix consumer version

→ verify propagation complete

Correction job auth bypass

(Chain 6):

→ stop job immediately

→ audit all modified rows

→ assess blast radius

→ security sign-off required

before re-running

Audit suppression detected:

→ alert + freeze suspicious

path

→ forensic review

Secret leak (source):

→ rotate immediately

→ audit access during

exposure window

Secret runtime exposure

(crash report / heap dump /

env var / trace span):

→ verify scrubbing

→ audit exposure window

→ rotate if confirmed leak

Supply chain compromise:

→ revoke artifact

→ block deploy

→ security incident declared

Webhook SSRF attempt (Chain 7):

→ block webhook URL

→ audit all registered

webhooks for tenant

→ tenant investigation

Webhook data exfiltration:

→ disable tenant webhooks

→ audit payload history

→ DPO notification

Job fan-out economic abuse

(Chain 8):

→ cap enforced immediately

→ freeze tenant job submission

→ billing audit

Object storage enumeration:

→ restrict list operations

→ rotate pre-signed URLs

→ audit access logs

Async / job abuse:

→ freeze tenant job submission

→ audit job queue

→ alert

Autoscale economic abuse:

→ rate limit offending

tenant or IP

→ alert + investigate

→ per-tenant cap enforced

Storage amplification abuse:

→ enforce quota immediately

→ alert

Notification / webhook

amplification:

→ rate limit enforced

→ tenant freeze if exceeded

Admin XSS detected:

→ revoke all admin sessions

→ investigate full scope

→ security incident declared

Admin impersonation without

audit trail:

→ freeze admin account

→ forensic audit

DSAR / erasure identity abuse:

→ block request

→ audit attempt

→ alert affected user

Data exfiltration via pagination:

→ cap page size immediately

→ alert on high-volume reads

→ audit access pattern

Session fixation:

→ invalidate all sessions

→ audit

SSRF metadata attempt:

→ block + alert

→ audit all outbound requests

SSRF via redirect bypass:

→ validate final destination

→ alert + block

Protocol SSRF attempt:

→ block non-http/https

→ alert

Request smuggling detected:

→ alert

→ proxy + app parser audit

Observability cardinality attack:

→ cap enforced (Section 23)

→ identify source

→ alert + block

Metrics label injection:

→ scrub label value

→ alert

→ block source

Algorithm confusion attack:

→ reject token

→ alert

→ pin algorithm validation

Algorithm rotation

misconfiguration:

→ dual-accept window enforced

→ old algorithm not retired

until all tokens expired

Each maps to:

Block / Rotate / Revoke /

Patch / Freeze / Escalate /

Alert / Audit

- Section 07 --- DB & migration tooling

- Section 30 --- Testing strategy

§27 — OBSERVABILITY

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No (always required for production)

[PURPOSE] → Define the three pillars of observability —

logs, metrics, and traces — plus alerting rules,

dashboards, SLO/SLA tracking, and on-call runbooks.

Observability is not optional. A system you cannot

observe cannot be operated safely.

All decisions must reference:

- Section 03 --- Uptime / latency / error rate NFRs

- Section 04 --- Expected traffic volumes

- Section 24 --- Deployment pipeline (deploy markers)

- Section 22 --- Resilience (circuit breaker states)

1. LOGGING STRATEGY

Log format: (structured JSON — required for production / plaintext for dev)

Standard log fields (every log line must include):

- timestamp: ISO8601 UTC

- level: debug / info / warn / error / fatal

- service: service name

- version: deployment version/commit SHA

- requestId: correlation ID (from request context)

- tenantId: (if multi-tenant)

- userId: (if authenticated — no PII beyond ID)

- message: human-readable description

- duration_ms: (for request logs)

- error: { message, code, stack } (for error logs — stack in non-prod only)

Log levels (what goes in each):

- DEBUG: detailed flow tracing (never in production default)

- INFO: business events, request start/end, state transitions

- WARN: degraded conditions, retries, approaching limits

- ERROR: failures that require attention, unexpected states

- FATAL: service unable to start or continue

Log aggregation platform: (Datadog / Grafana Loki / ELK / CloudWatch / other)

Log retention:

- Production: ___ days hot + ___ days cold archive

- Staging: ___ days

- Dev: local only

PII in logs:

- Email: (never log / hash / truncate — pick one)

- Phone: (never log / mask last 4)

- Payment data: (never log — absolute rule)

- Passwords: (never log — absolute rule)

Invariant: Stack traces MUST NOT appear in production logs accessible to non-engineers.

Invariant: PII MUST be scrubbed or masked before log aggregation.

2. METRICS STRATEGY

Metrics platform: (Prometheus + Grafana / Datadog / CloudWatch / other)

Required system metrics (auto-collected):

- CPU utilization per service

- Memory utilization per service

- HTTP request rate (req/s)

- HTTP error rate (4xx rate / 5xx rate)

- HTTP latency percentiles (p50 / p95 / p99)

- DB connection pool utilization

- DB query latency (p95)

- Queue depth per queue

- Cache hit rate / miss rate

- Active WebSocket connections (if Section 09)

Required business metrics (custom — declare all):

For each critical user journey (from Section 01):

- Funnel step completion rate

- Conversion rate

- Key action counts (signups / orders / messages sent)

SLI definitions (Service Level Indicators):

- Availability SLI: % of requests returning non-5xx over 5-minute window

- Latency SLI: % of requests completing under ___ ms

- Error rate SLI: % of requests returning 5xx

SLO definitions (Service Level Objectives):

- Availability SLO: ___% (e.g. 99.9%)

- Latency SLO: ___% of requests under ___ ms

- Error rate SLO: < ___% 5xx rate

Error budget:

- Monthly error budget = 100% - SLO %

- Error budget burn rate alert: (yes — alert at 5% burn in 1hr / no)

3. DISTRIBUTED TRACING

Tracing required: (yes — any multi-service architecture / no)

Tracing platform: (Jaeger / Zipkin / Datadog APM / AWS X-Ray / OpenTelemetry)

Trace propagation:

- Standard: W3C TraceContext / B3 (pick one)

- Propagated via: HTTP headers (traceparent / X-B3-TraceId)

- Cross-service: (yes — all internal calls traced / no)

Sampling strategy:

- Default: ___ % (common: 1-10% for high volume)

- Error traces: 100% always sampled

- Slow traces (> ___ ms): 100% always sampled

Spans to capture:

- HTTP inbound requests: yes

- DB queries: yes

- Cache operations: yes

- External API calls: yes

- Queue publish/consume: yes

- Background job execution: yes

Sensitive data in spans:

- Request URLs: allowed (no query params with PII)

- DB query text: allowed (parameterized only, no values)

- User IDs: allowed

- PII: never

4. ALERTING RULES

Alerting tiers:

- P1 (page immediately, 24/7): service down / error rate > ___% / data loss risk

- P2 (page during business hours): degraded performance / SLO breach approaching

- P3 (ticket created, no page): non-critical anomalies / capacity warnings

Required alerts (declare threshold for each):

- Service down (health check failing): P1, threshold: ___ consecutive failures

- 5xx error rate spike: P1, threshold: > ___% over ___ minutes

- P99 latency spike: P2, threshold: > ___ ms sustained ___ minutes

- DB connection pool exhaustion: P1, threshold: > ___% utilization

- Queue depth spike: P2, threshold: > ___ messages pending

- Disk space warning: P2, threshold: > ___% used

- Memory usage warning: P2, threshold: > ___% sustained

- Failed login rate spike: P2, threshold: > ___ failures/min (brute force)

- Certificate expiry warning: P2, threshold: < ___ days remaining

- Error budget burn rate: P2, threshold: burning at ___x rate

Alert routing:

- P1: PagerDuty / OpsGenie / phone call

- P2: Slack channel + email

- P3: Ticket in project tracker

Alert fatigue prevention:

- Alert deduplication window: ___ minutes

- Alert suppression during maintenance: (yes / no)

- Runbook URL attached to every alert: (yes — required / no)

5. DASHBOARDS

Required dashboards:

1. Service Health Overview: request rate / error rate / latency / saturation per service

2. SLO Dashboard: current SLO status / error budget remaining / burn rate

3. Infrastructure Dashboard: CPU / memory / disk / network per host

4. DB Dashboard: query latency / connection pool / slow query log

5. Business KPI Dashboard: signups / active users / key actions (non-engineer audience)

6. Deployment Dashboard: deploy frequency / change failure rate / MTTR

Dashboard standards:

- All dashboards as code: (yes — Grafana JSON / Terraform / no)

- Shared with whole team: (yes / no)

- Updated as part of feature delivery: (yes — required / no)

6. RUNBOOKS

Required runbook per alert:

- Alert name

- What it means (business impact)

- Immediate triage steps (numbered)

- Common causes + resolution steps

- Escalation path if unresolved in ___ minutes

- Rollback procedure if caused by deploy

Runbook location: (GitHub /docs/runbooks/ / Confluence / Notion / PagerDuty)

Runbook review cadence: (after each incident / quarterly / never)

7. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION (MANDATORY)

Before finalizing:

[ ] Alert thresholds derived from actual traffic projections in Section 04

[ ] Log retention aligns with compliance requirements from Section 20

[ ] Business metrics cover all critical journeys from Section 01

[ ] Dashboard coverage includes every component that can fail

[ ] Every P1 alert has a runbook

Flag all contradictions explicitly.

§28 — ANALYTICS & PRODUCT INSTRUMENTATION

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No (required for product decisions)

[PURPOSE] → Define the product analytics instrumentation plan,

event taxonomy, tracking architecture, A/B testing model,

and data pipeline to product intelligence.

Without analytics you are building blind — every feature

decision becomes a guess.

All decisions must reference:

- Section 01 --- Critical user journeys

- Section 19 --- Privacy & data governance (consent model)

- Section 20 --- Compliance (GDPR / CCPA analytics rules)

- Section 27 --- Observability (do not duplicate operational metrics)

1. ANALYTICS PLATFORM DECISION

Platform type:

- Third-party SaaS: (Mixpanel / Amplitude / PostHog / Heap / Segment / other)

- Self-hosted: (PostHog self-hosted / Matomo / custom ClickHouse pipeline)

- First-party only: (custom event log → data warehouse / no third-party)

If using third-party:

- Data residency: where does data land? (US / EU / choose — align Section 19)

- DPA (Data Processing Agreement) signed: (yes — required for GDPR / no)

- Customer data shared with vendor: (yes — declare what / no)

Analytics collection layer:

- Client-side (browser/app): (yes — track UI events)

- Server-side: (yes — track backend events — more reliable, no ad-blockers)

- Both: (recommended for completeness)

2. EVENT TAXONOMY

Event naming convention:

- Format: noun_verb (e.g. user_signed_up / checkout_completed / file_uploaded)

- Case: snake_case

- Tense: past tense (action completed)

Event categories (declare all events per category):

ACQUISITION:

- page_viewed { page_name, referrer, utm_source, utm_medium, utm_campaign }

- user_signed_up { method: "email"|"google"|"sso", plan }

- trial_started { plan, source }

ACTIVATION:

- onboarding_step_completed { step_name, step_number, total_steps }

- first_[key_action]_completed { ... }  ← define your "aha moment" event

ENGAGEMENT:

- [core_feature]_used { feature_name, ... entity-specific props }

- session_started { platform: "web"|"mobile" }

RETENTION:

- user_returned { days_since_last_visit }

- notification_clicked { type, source }

REVENUE:

- subscription_started { plan, billing_cycle, amount }

- subscription_upgraded { from_plan, to_plan }

- subscription_cancelled { plan, reason, days_active }

- payment_completed { amount, currency, method }

SUPPORT / RISK:

- error_encountered { error_code, page, feature }

- feature_blocked { reason: "paywall"|"permission"|"quota" }

3. IDENTITY & USER TRACKING

Anonymous → identified user stitching:

- Pre-login events tracked as anonymous: (yes / no)

- Identity merge on signup/login: (yes — alias anonymous ID to user ID / no)

User properties to track (no PII unless consented):

- Plan / tier

- Account age (days since signup)

- Role

- Tenant ID (for B2B)

- Feature flags active

Do NOT track (PII controls):

- Full name (unless explicit consent)

- Email address in event properties

- Phone number

- Payment information

Consent gating:

- Analytics fires only after consent: (yes — GDPR / no — legitimate interest)

- Consent change triggers: (clear anonymous ID / stop tracking / both)

4. FUNNEL & RETENTION ANALYSIS

Define the primary conversion funnel:

Step 1: ___ (event: ___)

Step 2: ___ (event: ___)

Step 3: ___ (event: ___)

...

Final: ___ (event: ___)

Retention analysis:

- D1 retention event: (what action = retained on day 1)

- D7 retention event: ___

- D30 retention event: ___

Cohort analysis dimensions:

- Acquisition source (utm_source)

- Signup method

- Plan at signup

- Platform (web / mobile)

5. A/B TESTING & FEATURE FLAGS

A/B testing platform: (LaunchDarkly / Statsig / GrowthBook / PostHog / custom)

Experiment contract:

- Experiment ID: string (unique, human-readable)

- Variants: control + at least one treatment

- Assignment: (client-side / server-side — server-side preferred for consistency)

- Assignment persistence: (cookie / user property / DB — must be stable per user)

- Minimum sample size: calculated before launch (statistical significance)

- Guardrail metrics: define what would kill an experiment early

Feature flag contract (not experiments — just rollouts):

- Flag evaluated at: (runtime — not build time)

- Default value: (always defined — no undefined behavior)

- Targeting: (user ID / tenant / percentage rollout / custom attribute)

- Flag removal process: (cleanup ticket created when flag reaches 100%)

Invariant: Feature flags MUST NOT gate security controls (Section 25 §2 invariant).

Invariant: Experiment assignment MUST be logged as an analytics event for analysis.

6. DATA PIPELINE TO WAREHOUSE

If data warehouse required (Full Track):

- Warehouse: (BigQuery / Snowflake / Redshift / other)

- ETL/ELT tool: (Fivetran / Airbyte / custom dbt / Segment CDP)

- Sync frequency: (real-time / hourly / daily)

- Data mart for product: (yes / no)

Events → warehouse flow:

Client/Server events → analytics platform → warehouse → BI tool

BI / dashboarding tool: (Metabase / Looker / Mode / Grafana / other)

Flag all contradictions explicitly.
