§29 — DATA LIFECYCLE MANAGEMENT

[TRACK] → Full Track

[CONDITIONAL] → No (required if any PII or regulated data exists)

[PURPOSE] → Define data retention policies, deletion workflows,

archival strategies, backup schedules, and the

complete lifecycle from data creation to destruction.

Failure to define this upfront creates GDPR/CCPA

liability, uncontrolled storage costs, and compliance

failures at audit time.

All decisions must reference:

- Section 07 --- Data model & entity classification

- Section 19 --- Privacy & data classification

- Section 20 --- Compliance & legal obligations

- Section 27 --- Observability (lifecycle event logging)

1. DATA RETENTION POLICY

For EVERY data entity classified in Section 07, declare:

- Retention period (how long is this data kept active)

- Archival period (how long is it kept in cold storage after archival)

- Deletion trigger (what causes deletion: TTL / user request / account closure / legal hold)

- Legal hold exception (can deletion be blocked: yes / no — if yes, how)

Minimum retention matrix (legal minimums — override if stricter):

| Entity Type          | Minimum Keep | Regulatory Driver   |

|---------------------|-------------|---------------------|

| Financial records    | 7 years     | Tax law             |

| Auth/access logs     | 90 days     | SOC2 / ISO27001     |

| Security event logs  | 1 year      | SOC2                |

| User PII             | Until erasure request | GDPR Art.17 |

| Payment records      | 5-7 years   | PCI DSS / Tax       |

| Communications       | ___ days    | Declare             |

Retention enforcement:

- Automated purge job: (yes — required for compliance / no — manual only)

- Purge job cadence: (daily / weekly / monthly)

- Purge audit log: (yes — who deleted what when / no)

- Hard delete vs soft delete: (declare per entity)

- Soft delete: mark deleted_at, exclude from queries, purge after retention period

- Hard delete: immediate removal (for GDPR erasure requests)

2. GDPR / CCPA DATA SUBJECT RIGHTS

Right to Erasure (GDPR Art. 17 / "Right to be Forgotten"):

- Request intake: (UI self-service / email / both)

- Verification: (re-authentication required / email confirmation)

- Processing SLA: ___ days (GDPR requires ≤ 30 days)

- Scope: which data is deleted / which is retained (legal hold / anonymized)

- Cascading deletion: (list all related entities deleted with user account)

- Third-party notification: (notify sub-processors to delete / list of processors)

- Confirmation to user: (yes — required / no)

Right of Access (DSAR — Data Subject Access Request):

- Request intake: (UI self-service / email / both)

- Response format: (JSON export / PDF / ZIP)

- Data included: (all PII fields / list specific fields)

- Processing SLA: ___ days (GDPR requires ≤ 30 days)

- Verification: (re-authentication required)

Data Portability:

- Export format: (JSON / CSV / both)

- Export contents: (user-created content / all data / configurable)

- Export delivery: (download link / email / both)

- Export link expiry: ___ hours

3. BACKUP STRATEGY

Database backups:

- Backup type: (full daily + incremental hourly / continuous WAL streaming)

- Backup frequency: (hourly / daily / both)

- Backup retention: (7 days / 30 days / 90 days — declare)

- Backup storage: (same region / cross-region / both — cross-region required for DR)

- Backup encryption: (yes — required / no)

Recovery targets:

- RPO (Recovery Point Objective): ___ hours (maximum data loss acceptable)

- RTO (Recovery Time Objective): ___ hours (maximum downtime for recovery)

Backup validation:

- Restore test cadence: (monthly / quarterly / never)

- Restore test process: (restore to staging, verify row counts / full data validation)

- Last restore test date: (tracked / not tracked)

File / object storage backups:

- Object storage versioning: (yes / no)

- Object replication: (cross-region / same-region / none)

- Deletion protection: (object lock / versioned delete / none)

4. DATA ARCHIVAL

Archival triggers (declare per entity):

- Age-based: archive records older than ___ days

- Status-based: archive when status = closed/completed/expired

- Size-based: archive when table exceeds ___ rows

Archival destination:

- Cold storage: (S3 Glacier / BigQuery / separate archive DB / compressed files)

- Archival format: (original / compressed JSON / parquet)

- Index in archive: (yes — searchable / no — retrieve by ID only)

Archive access pattern:

- Who can access archived data: (ops / legal / support / automated jobs only)

- Access requires: (ticket / approval / audit log / all)

- Retrieval SLA from archive: ___ hours

5. ANONYMIZATION & PSEUDONYMIZATION

When anonymization applies:

- Analytics data: (anonymize after ___ days)

- Deleted user records: (anonymize vs hard delete — state choice)

- Test/staging data: (anonymized copy from production / synthetic data)

Anonymization techniques per field type:

- Name: (replace with "Deleted User" / hash / null)

- Email: (replace with UUID@deleted.invalid / hash)

- Phone: (null / hash)

- IP address: (truncate last octet / null)

- User ID in logs: (keep — not PII / hash / null)

Pseudonymization (reversible, for analytics):

- Technique: (HMAC with rotating key / deterministic encryption)

- Key rotation: (yes — every ___ days / no)

6. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION (MANDATORY)

Before finalizing:

[ ] Every entity from Section 07 has a declared retention period

[ ] Retention periods meet or exceed legal minimums

[ ] GDPR erasure SLA ≤ 30 days

[ ] DSAR SLA ≤ 30 days

[ ] Backup RPO/RTO align with uptime NFRs from Section 03

[ ] Archive access is audited

[ ] Purge jobs are automated (no manual-only compliance process)

[ ] Staging environment does not use real PII

[ ] Deletion cascade list is complete (no orphaned PII after account deletion)

Flag all contradictions explicitly.

Use this section to:

→ Generate retention policy enforcement jobs (cron / worker)

→ Generate GDPR erasure workflow (cascade delete + audit log)

→ Generate DSAR export endpoint

→ Generate data export ZIP builder

→ Generate anonymization functions per field type

→ Generate backup schedule configuration

→ Generate archive pipeline

→ Generate lifecycle audit log schema

§30 — TESTING STRATEGY

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No

[PURPOSE] → Define the complete testing pyramid — unit,

integration, E2E, contract, load, and security tests —

coverage requirements, tooling, and quality gates.

Testing strategy must be defined before writing code,

not retrofitted after bugs are found in production.

All decisions must reference:

- Section 07 --- Data model (test data strategy)

- Section 08 --- API contracts (contract testing)

- Section 24 --- CI/CD pipeline (where tests run)

- Section 26 --- Developer tooling (test runner setup)

1. TESTING PYRAMID

Coverage targets:

- Unit tests:        ___% (recommended: 80%+)

- Integration tests: ___% of critical paths

- E2E tests:         cover all flows from Section 01 critical journeys

- Contract tests:    cover all external API integrations from Section 12

Testing framework (declare per layer):

- Unit: (Jest / Vitest / Mocha / pytest / other)

- Integration: (same as unit / Supertest / separate)

- E2E: (Playwright / Cypress / Selenium / Detox for mobile)

- Contract: (Pact / Dredd / schemathesis)

- Load: (k6 / Gatling / Locust / Artillery)

2. UNIT TESTING STANDARDS

What requires unit tests (must have — no exceptions):

- All business logic / domain functions

- All data transformation functions

- All validation functions

- All utility functions with branching logic

- All state management reducers / selectors

Unit test structure (AAA pattern required):

describe('functionName', () => {

it('should [expected behavior] when [condition]', () => {

// Arrange: set up inputs and mocks

// Act: call the function

// Assert: verify output

})

})

Mocking strategy:

- External dependencies: always mock (DB / HTTP / file system)

- Internal modules: mock only at layer boundaries

- Time: mock in all tests that depend on dates/timers

- Random: mock or seed for deterministic tests

Test isolation:

- Each test must be independent (no shared state between tests)

- DB state reset between integration tests: (yes — required)

- Test database: (separate DB / in-memory / Docker)

3. INTEGRATION TESTING STANDARDS

Scope: test full request-response cycle including real DB, real cache, mocked external services.

What requires integration tests:

- All API endpoints (happy path + key error paths)

- All background job handlers

- All webhook handlers

- All auth flows (login / refresh / logout / MFA)

- All DB transaction boundaries

- All queue message handlers

Test data strategy:

- Factory functions: (yes — generate test entities programmatically / no — fixtures)

- Test data isolation: (per-test tenantId / transaction rollback / truncate)

- Realistic data volume: (yes — test with N records to catch N+1 / no — minimal)

Integration test contract:

- Request shape: matches Section 08 API contract exactly

- Response shape: matches Section 08 exactly

- Error shapes: matches Section 06 §18D auth errors / Section 08 error contract

- Auth: real tokens issued by test auth service (not mocked)

4. END-TO-END TESTING STANDARDS

E2E test scope: cover all critical user journeys defined in Section 01.

For each journey, E2E test must cover:

- Happy path (complete the journey successfully)

- Auth failure path (what happens if session expires mid-journey)

- Error state (what happens if server returns error at each step)

E2E environment:

- Run against: (staging environment / local Docker stack / both)

- Test data: (seeded before run / generated by test / shared pool)

- Test account: (dedicated test accounts — never use real user accounts)

E2E performance:

- Max E2E test suite duration: ___ minutes

- Parallel execution: (yes — N workers / no)

- Flaky test policy: (quarantine immediately / 3 strikes then quarantine)

- Visual regression: (yes — screenshot comparison / no)

E2E in CI:

- Run on: (every PR / merge to main only / nightly)

- Gate production deploy: (yes — must pass / no)

5. CONTRACT TESTING

Consumer-driven contract tests for each integration from Section 12:

- Consumer (your service) defines the contract (expected request/response)

- Provider (external service) verified against the contract

- Contract broker: (Pact Broker / Specmatic / inline / none)

API schema validation:

- OpenAPI schema generated: (yes — validate in CI / no)

- Request validation: (middleware validates request body against schema / manual)

- Response validation in tests: (yes — assert exact shape / no — partial)

6. LOAD & PERFORMANCE TESTING

Load test scenarios (from Section 04 traffic estimates):

- Baseline: ___ concurrent users / ___ RPS

- Peak: ___ concurrent users / ___ RPS (from Section 04)

- Spike: ___x baseline, injected over ___ seconds

- Soak: baseline load for ___ hours (memory leak detection)

Performance thresholds (fail if exceeded):

- P95 response time: < ___ ms

- P99 response time: < ___ ms

- Error rate under load: < ___%

- Throughput degradation vs baseline: < ___%

Load test cadence:

- Before major release: (yes / no)

- After infrastructure changes: (yes / no)

- Regular schedule: (monthly / quarterly / never)

7. SECURITY TESTING

SAST (Static Application Security Testing):

- Tool: (Semgrep / CodeQL / Snyk Code / Bandit / other)

- Run: (every PR in CI)

- Gate: (block merge on high/critical / warn only)

DAST (Dynamic Application Security Testing):

- Tool: (OWASP ZAP / Burp Suite / Nuclei)

- Run: (on staging — before production deploy / quarterly)

Dependency scanning:

- Tool: (Snyk / Dependabot / npm audit)

- Frequency: (daily automated / on PR)

- Auto-patch: (yes — auto-merge patch versions / no)

Penetration testing:

- Cadence: (annually / on major releases / never)

- Scope: (full application / API only / critical flows)

- Provider: (internal / third-party / both)

8. TEST DATA MANAGEMENT

Test data sources:

- Factories: (yes — programmatic, language-native)

- Fixtures: (yes — for stable reference data / no)

- Production snapshots: (anonymized / never use raw production data)

Factory standards:

- Every entity in Section 07 has a factory

- Factories use sensible defaults (valid data out-of-the-box)

- Factories support overrides for edge case testing

- Factories are tenant-aware (inject tenantId correctly)

9. QUALITY GATES (CI BLOCKERS)

Block merge to main if ANY of these fail:

[ ] Unit test coverage < ___%

[ ] Any unit test fails

[ ] Any integration test fails

[ ] Any type error

[ ] Any lint error

[ ] SAST high/critical finding (unless suppressed with justification)

[ ] Build fails

Block production deploy if ANY of these fail:

[ ] All above merge gates

[ ] E2E tests fail

[ ] Contract tests fail

[ ] Smoke tests post-staging-deploy fail

10. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION (MANDATORY)

Before finalizing:

[ ] E2E tests cover all critical journeys from Section 01

[ ] Integration tests cover all API endpoints from Section 08

[ ] Contract tests cover all integrations from Section 12

[ ] Load test targets derived from Section 04 estimates

[ ] Test DB strategy aligned with Section 07 migration runner

[ ] Security test cadence aligned with Section 25 threat model

[ ] All test types run in CI pipeline from Section 26

[ ] Factory defined for every entity in Section 07

Flag all contradictions explicitly.

§31 — INTERNATIONALIZATION (i18n) ARCHITECTURE

[TRACK] → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Yes — skip if single-language, single-region only

[PURPOSE] → Define locale support, translation pipeline,

RTL support, date/number/currency formatting, and

pluralization rules.

i18n retrofitted after launch is extremely expensive.

Even single-language apps must get date, currency,

and timezone handling right from day one.

All decisions must reference:

- Section 01 --- Target geography & personas

- Section 03 --- Supported locales as NFR

- Section 07 --- Timezone strategy in DB

1. LOCALE & LANGUAGE SUPPORT

Languages supported at launch:

- Primary: ___ (e.g. en-US)

- Secondary: ___ (list all)

Languages planned (post-launch):

- ___

Locale detection strategy:

- Priority order: (browser preference / user setting / URL prefix / geolocation)

- URL structure: (prefix: /en/dashboard / subdomain: en.app.com / query: ?lang=en / none)

- Fallback locale: en-US (or declare)

- Right-to-left (RTL) support: (yes — Arabic/Hebrew/Farsi / no)

Translation file format:

- Format: (JSON / YAML / PO files / ICU message format)

- Namespace structure: (single file / per feature / per screen)

- Key naming: (flat: "button.save" / nested: { button: { save: "Save" } })

2. TRANSLATION PIPELINE

Translation workflow:

- Developer adds new key with English value

- CI detects missing translations for other locales

- Sent to: (professional translator / crowdsourced / machine translation / internal)

- Reviewed by: (native speaker / PM / automated)

- Merged back via: (PR / translation platform sync / automated script)

Translation platform: (Crowdin / Phrase / Lokalise / Transifex / manual / none)

Missing key behavior:

- Show English fallback: (yes / no)

- Show key name as fallback: (never in production)

- Log missing key: (yes — for discovery / no)

3. DATE, TIME & TIMEZONE

Storage: always UTC (declared in Section 07)

Display:

- User's local timezone: (detect from browser / user setting / both)

- Timezone setting persisted: (in user profile / browser only)

- Date format: locale-specific via Intl.DateTimeFormat (required — no hardcoded formats)

- Relative time (e.g. "3 hours ago"): (yes — via Intl.RelativeTimeFormat / no)

Critical timezone rules:

- Invariant: NEVER store local time in DB — UTC only

- Invariant: NEVER display UTC to end users — always convert to local

- Invariant: All date comparisons happen in UTC

- Business hours / scheduling: store as UTC + timezone name (IANA format), NEVER as offset

Date library: (date-fns / Luxon / Temporal API / Day.js — declare one)

4. NUMBER, CURRENCY & UNIT FORMATTING

Numbers:

- Decimal separator: locale-specific (1,234.56 vs 1.234,56)

- Thousand separator: locale-specific

- Use: Intl.NumberFormat (required — no manual formatting)

Currency:

- Currencies supported: list (USD / EUR / GBP / etc.)

- Currency storage: always store as minor units (cents) in integer column

- Display: Intl.NumberFormat with style: 'currency'

- Exchange rate source: (none — single currency / live API / fixed rates — declare)

Units of measurement:

- Imperial vs metric: (user preference / locale-based / single standard)

- Weight / distance / temperature: (which system per locale)

5. RTL SUPPORT

(Skip if no RTL languages)

CSS approach:

- Logical CSS properties: (yes — margin-inline-start / no — manual LTR/RTL classes)

- dir attribute on html element: (yes — required / no)

- CSS-in-JS RTL: (styled-components RTL plugin / manual / other)

Component adjustments for RTL:

- Icons that are directional (arrow-right → arrow-left in RTL): list

- Text alignment: (start-aligned — not left-aligned — required)

- Form field order: (reversed in RTL / not reversed)

- Charts / graphs: (mirrored in RTL / not mirrored)

6. PLURALIZATION & GRAMMAR RULES

Pluralization:

- Use ICU message format (required — not manual if/else in code):

"{count, plural, one {# item} other {# items}}"

- Plural categories needed: (zero / one / two / few / many / other — per language)

Gender agreement (if target languages require):

- German / French / Spanish gender: (handle via ICU select / not supported)

7. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION (MANDATORY)

Before finalizing:

[ ] All locales from Section 03 NFR are covered

[ ] DB stores all datetimes as UTC (Section 07)

[ ] No hardcoded date or currency formats in codebase

[ ] Currency stored as integer minor units

[ ] RTL support planned if any RTL locale targeted

[ ] Translation pipeline defined before first string is written

[ ] Timezone handling consistent across API / DB / UI

[ ] Pluralization uses ICU format (no manual branching)

Flag all contradictions explicitly.

§32 — EXTENSIBILITY & FUTURE-PROOFING

[TRACK] → Full Track

[CONDITIONAL] → No

[PURPOSE] → Define the architectural patterns, plugin/extension points,

API versioning strategy, deprecation lifecycle,

and evolution path that allow the system to grow

without requiring full rewrites.

Systems that cannot evolve safely accumulate technical debt

faster than features can be added.

All decisions must reference:

- Section 05 --- Current architecture style

- Section 08 --- API design (versioning)

- Section 04 --- Scale triggers

- Section 24 --- Deployment (backward compatibility)

1. API VERSIONING & BACKWARD COMPATIBILITY

API versioning strategy (declared in Section 08 — enforce here):

- Version scheme: (URL path /v1/ /v2/ / header Accept: application/vnd.api+v2 / query ?version=2)

- When a new version is created: (breaking change only / major feature change / never)

- How many versions supported simultaneously: ___

- Sunset policy: (N months notice before removing old version)

Backward compatibility rules (mandatory):

- NEVER remove a field from a response (add new, deprecate old)

- NEVER change field type (add new field with new type)

- NEVER change the meaning of an existing field value

- NEVER remove an enum value (add new, mark old deprecated)

- ALWAYS default new optional fields to null/empty (not error)

- ALWAYS accept unknown fields in requests (ignore, don't error)

Deprecation lifecycle:

1. Mark deprecated in docs + API response header: Deprecation: true

2. Log usage of deprecated endpoints/fields (to measure migration)

3. Notify active consumers via email / changelog

4. Sunset date: ___ months after deprecation announcement

5. Remove only after sunset date AND zero usage confirmed

2. PLUGIN & EXTENSION ARCHITECTURE

Extension model (declare if applicable):

- Webhook-based: (consumers register webhooks — events pushed to them)

- SDK/plugin system: (third parties write plugins that run in your runtime)

- Marketplace / app store: (installable integrations / extensions)

- None: (closed system — no extensibility for third parties)

If webhooks (align with Section 12):

- Events that can be subscribed to: (list)

- Webhook contract: immutable once published (no breaking changes)

- Webhook versioning: (yes — include version in payload / no)

- Retry behavior: (exponential backoff / N retries / dead letter)

If plugin system:

- Plugin interface contract: (declare API surface / sandbox boundary)

- Plugin isolation: (separate process / VM / WASM sandbox)

- Plugin permissions model: (declare what plugins can/cannot access)

- Plugin review process: (automated / manual / self-publish)

3. FEATURE FLAG ARCHITECTURE

(Also declared in Section 28 — align and do not contradict)

Feature flag lifecycle:

1. Create flag (default OFF, targeting no one)

2. Enable for internal team only

3. Enable for beta users / small % rollout

4. Ramp to 100%

5. Remove flag from code (cleanup)

6. Archive flag in system

Flag types:

- Release flags: (hide incomplete features — short-lived, removed at 100%)

- Ops flags: (kill switches — long-lived, never auto-removed)

- Experiment flags: (A/B tests — removed after experiment concludes)

- Permission flags: (gate features by plan/tier — long-lived)

Technical debt prevention:

- Release flags MUST have a removal ticket created at creation time

- Max age for release flags: ___ weeks before forced cleanup review

- Flag count alarm: (alert if > ___ flags active in codebase)

4. SCHEMA EVOLUTION

DB schema evolution rules (align with Section 07 §21D):

- Additive changes only in single deploy: (add columns / add tables / add indexes)

- Destructive changes require expand-contract pattern:

Phase 1: add new column, dual-write, backfill (deploy)

Phase 2: migrate readers to new column (deploy)

Phase 3: remove old column (deploy — after full migration confirmed)

- Column rename = expand-contract (never ALTER COLUMN RENAME in single deploy)

Event schema evolution (if using event sourcing or message queues):

- Event schema versioning: (include schema_version in every event)

- Consumer handles old and new versions: (yes — consumers must be forward-compatible)

- Schema registry: (Confluent Schema Registry / AWS Glue / JSON Schema in repo / none)

5. MODULARIZATION & MONOLITH EXTRACTION PATH

Current architecture: (monolith / modular monolith / microservices — from Section 05)

Extraction trigger thresholds (when to split a module into a service):

- Team size > ___ engineers working on the module

- Independent deployment needed (module deploys block other teams)

- Scaling requirement differs (module needs 10x more resources than others)

- Compliance boundary required (module handles regulated data)

Module boundary rules (apply today, even in monolith):

- Modules MUST NOT import from other modules' internal packages

- Cross-module communication via: (defined interfaces / events / shared DB — pick one)

- Shared DB access: (yes — but via repository layer only / no — separate DB per module)

- Circular dependencies: (never — enforced by linter)

Strangler fig preparation (for future extraction):

- Anti-corruption layer at module boundaries: (yes / no)

- Module has its own migration files: (yes / no)

- Module config isolated from other modules: (yes / no)

6. TECHNICAL DEBT GOVERNANCE

Tech debt tracking:

- Where tracked: (GitHub Issues / Jira / ADRs / code comments only)

- Labeling: (tech-debt label / dedicated sprint / ad hoc)

Debt repayment policy:

- % of sprint capacity reserved for tech debt: ___%

- Debt items that block new features: (must be resolved before feature / allowed with mitigation)

Architecture Decision Records (ADRs):

- Format: (MADR / RFC / custom)

- Location: (git repo /docs/adr / Confluence)

- Required for: (breaking API changes / new services / DB schema redesign / technology adoption)

- Review process: (team review / architect approval / PR only)

7. EVOLUTION ROADMAP

Declare the planned evolution path for the next 3 stages:

Stage 1 (current):

- Architecture: ___

- Scale target: ___ users

- Team size: ___

Stage 2 (triggers from Section 04):

- Architecture change: ___

- What forces the change: ___

- Migration path: ___

Stage 3 (future):

- Architecture target: ___

- What forces the change: ___

Key decisions that are REVERSIBLE (can change without major migration):

- ___

Key decisions that are IRREVERSIBLE (changing requires major migration):

- Data model decisions (hard to change)

- API contract decisions (breaking changes hurt consumers)

- Auth model decisions (session invalidation at scale is hard)

- Multi-tenancy model (retrofitting is extremely costly)

8. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION (MANDATORY)

Before finalizing:

[ ] API versioning strategy aligns with Section 08

[ ] Backward compatibility rules enforced in Section 24 CI

[ ] Feature flag lifecycle aligns with Section 28 A/B testing

[ ] Schema evolution rules align with Section 07 §21D migration runner

[ ] Module boundaries enforced by linter/tooling

[ ] Scale triggers align with Section 04 estimates

[ ] ADR process defined and team agrees

[ ] Technical debt policy communicated to team

Flag all contradictions explicitly.

W1 — SEO ARCHITECTURE

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Skip if: app is fully behind login (no public pages),

internal tool only, or mobile-only.

[PURPOSE]     → Define which pages need search engine visibility,

how metadata is structured, how crawlers are guided,

and how structured data is implemented.

SEO architecture cannot be retrofitted cheaply.

Every public page needs an SEO contract before it is built.

All decisions must reference:

- §01 screen inventory (which screens are public)

- §05 rendering strategy (SSR/SSG required for SEO)

- §08 URL structure

1. SEO SCOPE DECISION

Pages that need SEO (public, indexable):

- ___

Pages that must NOT be indexed (behind auth, private):

- ___

Primary SEO goal:

(brand awareness / lead generation / content discovery /

marketplace listings / programmatic SEO / all)

Target search intent:

(informational / transactional / navigational / local)

2. RENDERING STRATEGY FOR SEO

Confirm rendering model per page type (must align with §05 + §15):

- Marketing / landing pages:  (SSG — recommended)

- Blog / content pages:       (SSG or ISR — recommended)

- Product / listing pages:    (SSR or ISR — if dynamic content)

- User dashboard:             (CSR — no SEO needed)

- Public profile pages:       (SSR — if dynamic user content)

Invariant: Any page targeted for SEO MUST use SSR or SSG.

CSR pages are invisible to search engines.

3. METADATA ARCHITECTURE

For each public page type, define:

- Title tag format:   (e.g. "[Page Name] | [Brand]")

- Meta description:   (template: ___ — max 160 chars)

- Canonical URL:      (self-referencing canonical on all pages)

- robots meta:        (index,follow / noindex,nofollow per page type)

Dynamic pages (e.g. product pages, user profiles):

- Title generated from: (entity name / template / CMS)

- Meta description generated from: (entity description / auto-generated)

- Canonical handles pagination: (yes — rel=next/prev / no)

- Handles duplicate content: (canonical / noindex on duplicates / URL parameters blocked in robots.txt)

Hreflang (multi-language):

- Required: (yes — §31 i18n required / no — single language)

- If yes: hreflang tags on all language variants

4. STRUCTURED DATA (SCHEMA.ORG)

Schema types needed (declare per page type):

- Organization schema:      (yes — on homepage / no)

- WebSite + SearchAction:   (yes — enables sitelinks search box / no)

- Product schema:           (yes — if e-commerce / no)

- Article / BlogPosting:    (yes — if content/blog pages / no)

- FAQPage:                  (yes — if FAQ sections exist / no)

- LocalBusiness:            (yes — if physical location / no)

- Review / AggregateRating: (yes — if user reviews / no)

Implementation format: (JSON-LD — recommended / Microdata / RDFa)

5. SITEMAP & CRAWL STRATEGY

Sitemap:

- Type: (XML sitemap / sitemap index with multiple sitemaps)

- Auto-generated: (yes — on build / on publish / scheduled job)

- Submitted to: (Google Search Console / Bing Webmaster / both)

- Max URLs per sitemap: 50,000 (standard limit)

- Dynamic sitemap needed: (yes — for user/product pages / no)

robots.txt rules:

- Disallow: (list paths to block — /admin / /api / /dashboard etc.)

- Allow: (any exceptions to disallowed paths)

- Sitemap location declared in robots.txt: (yes — required)

- Crawl-delay: (set if server needs protection / not set)

Crawl budget optimization:

- Faceted navigation URLs blocked: (yes — via robots.txt or noindex / no)

- Paginated pages handled: (canonical / rel=next-prev / noindex after page 3)

- URL parameters that create duplicates: (list — block via GSC or robots.txt)

6. TECHNICAL SEO REQUIREMENTS

Core requirements (non-negotiable):

- HTTPS: yes — required (HTTP → HTTPS redirect)

- www vs non-www: (choose one — 301 redirect other to canonical)

- Trailing slash consistency: (always trailing / never trailing — enforce with redirect)

- 404 page: (custom — returns actual 404 status code)

- Soft 404s: (avoided — blank pages return 404 not 200)

- Redirect chains: (max 1 redirect — no chains)

- Page speed: (align with W2 Core Web Vitals targets)

URL structure (confirm aligns with §08 + W8):

- Clean URLs: (yes — no query params in indexable URLs)

- URL depth: (max ___ levels deep for important pages)

- Keywords in URL: (yes — descriptive slugs / no — ID-based)

- URL case: (lowercase only — enforce with redirect)

W2 — CORE WEB VITALS & PERFORMANCE BUDGET

[TRACK]       → Both

1. CORE WEB VITALS TARGETS

Set targets for each metric (Google thresholds for reference):

LCP — Largest Contentful Paint (loading):

- Target: < ___ ms  (Good: <2500ms / Needs work: 2500-4000ms)

- Measured on: (mobile / desktop / both)

INP — Interaction to Next Paint (interactivity):

- Target: < ___ ms  (Good: <200ms / Needs work: 200-500ms)

CLS — Cumulative Layout Shift (visual stability):

- Target: < ___     (Good: <0.1 / Needs work: 0.1-0.25)

FCP — First Contentful Paint:

- Target: < ___ ms  (Good: <1800ms)

TTFB — Time to First Byte:

- Target: < ___ ms  (Good: <800ms)

TTI — Time to Interactive:

- Target: < ___ ms  (Good: <3800ms)

Measurement conditions:

- Network: (simulated 3G / 4G / fast 3G — use 3G for mobile targets)

- Device: (low-end mobile / mid-range / desktop)

- Tool: (Lighthouse / WebPageTest / Chrome UX Report / all)

2. PERFORMANCE BUDGET PER PAGE TYPE

Define budget for each page category:

Landing / marketing page:

- Total JS (parsed + executed): < ___ KB gzipped

- Total CSS: < ___ KB gzipped

- Total images: < ___ KB

- Total page weight: < ___ KB

- HTTP requests: < ___

App / dashboard pages:

- Total JS bundle: < ___ KB gzipped

- Per route chunk: < ___ KB gzipped

- API response time (p95): < ___ ms (from §03)

Critical rendering path:

- Render-blocking resources: (0 — none allowed on critical path)

- Above-the-fold CSS inlined: (yes / no)

- Web fonts: max ___ font files, loaded with font-display: swap

- Modern format: (WebP / AVIF — with fallback for older browsers)

- Retina (2x) support: (yes / no)

Loading:

- Lazy loading: (yes — all below-fold images / no)

- Eager loading: (hero image + above-fold only)

- Priority hint on LCP image: (yes — fetchpriority="high")

- Image CDN: (Cloudinary / Imgix / Next.js Image / Vercel / none)

- On-the-fly resizing: (yes / no)

W5 — COOKIE CONSENT & BANNER ARCHITECTURE

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Skip if: app serves users exclusively outside EU/UK,

no analytics or tracking cookies used,

and no third-party marketing scripts.

[PURPOSE]     → Define the consent model, cookie categories,

consent storage, and the technical architecture

that gates analytics and tracking behind user consent.

This is a legal requirement under GDPR and ePrivacy.

Getting it wrong means fines, not just bad UX.

All decisions must reference:

- §19 Privacy & Data Classification

- §20 Compliance & Legal

- §28 Analytics (consent must gate analytics firing)

1. CONSENT REQUIREMENT SCOPE

Applicable regulations:

- GDPR (EU/EEA): (yes / no)

- UK GDPR: (yes / no)

- ePrivacy Directive: (yes / no)

- CCPA (California): (yes / no — CCPA is opt-out, not opt-in)

- Other: ___

Consent model:

- Opt-in (explicit consent before tracking): required for GDPR

- Opt-out (tracking by default, user can opt out): CCPA model

- Legitimate interest claim (no consent needed for some uses): (yes — declare basis / no)

Geo-targeted consent:

- Show banner to EU/UK users only: (yes — detect by IP / no — show to all)

- CCPA opt-out link for California users: (yes / no)

2. COOKIE CATEGORIES

Define all cookies and scripts per category:

STRICTLY NECESSARY (no consent required):

- Auth session cookie

- CSRF token

- Load balancer cookie

- User language preference

- Cookie consent preference itself

FUNCTIONAL (consent recommended):

- User UI preferences (theme / layout)

- Saved search filters

- Form autofill data

ANALYTICS (consent required under GDPR):

- Google Analytics / Mixpanel / Amplitude

- Heatmap tools (Hotjar / Microsoft Clarity)

- A/B testing if tied to user identity

MARKETING / TARGETING (consent required):

- Meta Pixel

- Google Ads tags

- LinkedIn Insight

- Retargeting pixels

Invariant: Strictly necessary cookies fire WITHOUT consent.

All other categories fire ONLY AFTER consent given.

3. CONSENT BANNER DESIGN

Banner type:

(simple accept/reject / granular category toggles / both — show simple first, link to granular)

Required elements (GDPR compliance):

- [ ] "Accept all" button

- [ ] "Reject all" button (as prominent as Accept — required)

- [ ] "Manage preferences" / granular control link

- [ ] Link to Privacy Policy

- [ ] Link to Cookie Policy

- [ ] Brief explanation of what is tracked and why

Banner placement: (bottom bar / center modal / bottom-left corner)

Banner timing: (on first visit — immediate / after X seconds / on scroll)

Dark pattern prohibition (GDPR enforcement):

- Reject button NOT hidden or smaller than Accept: (confirmed)

- No pre-ticked boxes: (confirmed)

- No misleading button labels: (confirmed)

- Consent withdrawal as easy as giving consent: (confirmed)

4. CONSENT STORAGE & PROPAGATION

Consent storage:

- Where stored: (cookie — cookieConsent / localStorage / both)

- Cookie name: ___

- Cookie lifetime: ___ months (max 13 months under ePrivacy)

- Stored values: (per-category boolean flags + timestamp + version)

Consent version:

- Version field in stored consent: (yes — required for re-consent on policy change)

- Re-consent trigger: (policy version change / annual / never)

Propagation to scripts:

- Method: (Google Consent Mode v2 / custom consent manager / tag manager)

- Analytics fires only after consent: (yes — gated in §28 analytics init)

- Script loader respects consent: (yes — dynamic inject / no)

Consent API (internal):

interface ConsentState {

analytics: boolean

}

W7 — WEB ACCESSIBILITY (WCAG)

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No — accessibility is a legal requirement in most

markets and a baseline quality standard everywhere.

[PURPOSE]     → Define the WCAG compliance level, automated testing

setup, manual audit process, and component-level

accessibility contracts that ensure the app is

usable by everyone including screen reader users,

keyboard-only users, and users with visual impairments.

Note: §14 UI/UX already defines accessibility at component level.

This section defines the TESTING and AUDIT architecture —

how you verify and maintain compliance over time.

All decisions must reference:

- §14 accessibility standard decision

- §30 testing strategy

- §03 compliance requirements

1. COMPLIANCE TARGET

WCAG level: (2.1 AA — recommended minimum / 2.1 AAA / 2.2 AA)

Legal requirements:

- ADA (US): (yes — applies to public accommodations / no)

- EN 301 549 (EU): (yes — applies to public sector / no)

- Section 508 (US federal): (yes / no)

- AODA (Canada): (yes / no)

- EAA 2025 (EU — applies June 2025): (yes — affects all EU digital products / no)

Invariant: WCAG 2.1 AA is the minimum for any app with a public

interface or serving users in EU, US, or Canada.

2. AUTOMATED ACCESSIBILITY TESTING

Tools:

- Linting: (eslint-plugin-jsx-a11y — catches issues at write time)

- Unit/component tests: (jest-axe / vitest-axe — catches issues in CI)

- E2E tests: (Playwright accessibility checks / axe-playwright)

- CI gate: (fail build on new accessibility violations — yes / no)

- Browser extension for dev: (axe DevTools / Accessibility Insights)

Automated test coverage:

- Every component has axe test: (yes — required / no)

- Every page has automated scan: (yes — in E2E suite / no)

- Violations fail CI: (yes — new violations block merge / warning only)

What automated tools catch (~30% of WCAG issues):

- Missing alt text

- Insufficient color contrast

- Missing form labels

- Duplicate IDs

- Invalid ARIA usage

- Missing landmark roles

3. MANUAL AUDIT PROCESS

Manual testing catches the remaining ~70% of WCAG issues.

Keyboard navigation audit:

- All interactive elements reachable via Tab: tested

- Focus order logical and visible: tested

- No keyboard traps (focus cannot escape a component): tested

- Escape closes modals and dropdowns: tested

- Enter / Space activate buttons and links: tested

Screen reader audit:

- Tool: (NVDA + Chrome / VoiceOver + Safari / JAWS + Edge)

- Cadence: (every release / quarterly / on major UI changes)

- Test all critical user journeys with screen reader

Color contrast audit:

- Tool: (Colour Contrast Analyser / browser DevTools)

- All text meets 4.5:1 ratio (normal) / 3:1 (large): tested

- All interactive element borders meet 3:1: tested

4. COMPONENT ACCESSIBILITY CONTRACTS

Every interactive component must have:

- Keyboard interaction spec (which keys do what)

- ARIA role + attributes declared

- Focus management defined (where focus goes after action)

- Screen reader announcement defined (what is announced on change)

Critical patterns (non-negotiable):

- Modal: focus trap + return focus on close + aria-modal

- Dropdown/Select: arrow key navigation + role=listbox/option

- Toast/Alert: role=alert or role=status + aria-live

- Form error: aria-invalid + aria-describedby pointing to error

- Icon-only button: aria-label required — no exceptions

- Loading state: aria-busy or aria-live announcement

- Tab panel: role=tablist/tab/tabpanel + aria-selected

5. ACCESSIBILITY STATEMENT

Public accessibility statement required: (yes — EAA/ADA / no)

If yes:

- Compliance level claimed: ___

- Known limitations listed: ___

- Contact for accessibility issues: ___

- Last audit date: ___

6. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION

[ ] WCAG level matches §14 and §03 requirements

[ ] eslint-plugin-jsx-a11y installed and configured

[ ] jest-axe / axe-playwright in test suite (§30)

[ ] CI blocks on new accessibility violations

[ ] Keyboard navigation tested on all critical paths

[ ] Screen reader tested on all critical user journeys

[ ] All icon-only buttons have aria-label

[ ] All form fields have visible, associated labels

[ ] Color contrast meets 4.5:1 minimum

[ ] Focus ring visible on all interactive elements

→ Generate jest-axe test wrapper for all components

→ Generate Playwright accessibility test for each critical journey

→ Generate ARIA-compliant modal / dialog component

→ Generate ARIA-compliant dropdown / select component

→ Generate skip-to-content link component

→ Generate color contrast utility checker

→ Generate accessibility statement page template

W8 — URL STRUCTURE & ROUTING STRATEGY

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No — every web app needs a defined URL structure.

[PURPOSE]     → Define the complete URL taxonomy, routing patterns,

deep linking rules, redirect strategy, and URL

parameter conventions.

URL structure is one of the hardest things to change

after launch. External links break. SEO equity is lost.

Get it right before the first page is built.

All decisions must reference:

- §08 API URL structure

- §15 routing model (file-based / code-defined)

- W1 SEO (URL requirements for indexable pages)

1. URL DESIGN PRINCIPLES

Case convention: (lowercase always — enforce with 301 redirect)

Word separator: (hyphen — never underscore for SEO)

Trailing slash: (always / never — enforce consistently with redirect)

URL encoding: (UTF-8 slugs / ASCII only)

Language in URL: (prefix /en/ /fr/ / no prefix — from §31)

Max URL depth for key pages:

- Marketing pages: max ___ levels (e.g. /features/analytics = 2)

- App pages: max ___ levels

- Content pages: max ___ levels

2. FULL URL TAXONOMY

Define every route category and its URL pattern:

PUBLIC / MARKETING:

/                          → Homepage

/pricing                   → Pricing page

/features/[feature-slug]   → Feature pages

/blog/[post-slug]          → Blog posts

/about                     → About page

/contact                   → Contact page

AUTH:

/login                     → Login

/signup                    → Signup

/forgot-password           → Password reset request

/reset-password/[token]    → Password reset confirm

/verify-email/[token]      → Email verification

APP (authenticated):

/dashboard                 → Main dashboard

/[entity]/                 → Entity list

/[entity]/[id]             → Entity detail

/[entity]/[id]/edit        → Entity edit

/[entity]/new              → Create new entity

/settings                  → User settings

/settings/[section]        → Settings subsection

MULTI-TENANT (if applicable):

/[tenantSlug]/dashboard    → Tenant-scoped dashboard

OR: subdomain.app.com      → Subdomain per tenant

Tenant routing model: (path prefix / subdomain / both — from §05)

ADMIN:

/admin                     → Admin panel root

/admin/[section]           → Admin subsections

ERROR PAGES:

/404                       → Not found

/500                       → Server error

/maintenance               → Maintenance mode

3. DYNAMIC ROUTE CONVENTIONS

ID in URL:

- Format: (UUID / slug / numeric ID / CUID)

- Slug generation: (from entity name — auto-slugify / manual / both)

- Slug uniqueness: (per-tenant / global / with numeric suffix if duplicate)

Optional segments:

- Declare any optional URL segments and fallback behavior

- Example: /blog/[category]/[slug] where category is optional

Catch-all routes:

- Used for: (CMS pages / documentation / custom domains)

- Pattern: /[...slug]

404 handling for dynamic routes:

- Entity not found: (return 404 page with 404 status — not 200)

- Deleted entity: (410 Gone / 301 redirect to parent / 404)

- Private entity accessed without auth: (redirect to login / 403)

4. QUERY PARAMETER CONVENTIONS

Standard query params (use consistently across all pages):

- Pagination:    ?page=1&limit=20

- Sorting:       ?sort=created_at&order=desc

- Filtering:     ?filter[status]=active

- Search:        ?q=search+term

- Tab/view:      ?tab=overview

- Modal state:   ?modal=edit-profile (shareable modal state)

URL state vs session state:

- What lives in URL (shareable / bookmarkable): filters, sort, search, page, tab

- What lives in session state only: form drafts, scroll position, UI toggles

5. REDIRECT STRATEGY

Permanent redirects (301):

- HTTP → HTTPS

- www → non-www (or reverse)

- Old URL structure → new URL structure

- Trailing slash enforcement

Temporary redirects (302):

- Auth redirect (unauthenticated → login with ?returnTo=)

- Maintenance mode redirect

Post-action redirects:

- After login: → returnTo URL or /dashboard

- After signup: → onboarding or /dashboard

- After delete: → parent list page

- After form submit: → confirmation page (POST-Redirect-GET pattern)

Redirect rules storage:

(Next.js redirects config / Nginx / Vercel redirects / CDN rules)

6. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION

[ ] All routes documented in taxonomy above

[ ] URL conventions match §15 routing model

[ ] URL structure aligns with §08 API routes

[ ] Multi-tenant URL model matches §05 decision

[ ] Auth redirect preserves returnTo URL

[ ] POST-Redirect-GET pattern on all form submissions

[ ] No 404s returning 200 status codes

[ ] Redirect rules cover all legacy URLs if migrating

[ ] Query param naming consistent across all list pages

[ ] Trailing slash enforced consistently (W1 SEO requirement)

→ Generate router configuration with all routes

→ Generate route guard middleware (auth + role checks)

→ Generate redirect rules file (framework-specific)

→ Generate 404 and 500 error pages

→ Generate URL slug generator utility

→ Generate query param state management hooks

→ Generate returnTo redirect handler for auth flow

→ Generate sitemap route list for W1

M2 — APP VERSIONING & FORCE-UPDATE

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No — every mobile app needs a versioning and

update enforcement strategy.

[PURPOSE]     → Define the version numbering scheme, force-update

mechanism, soft-update prompt, and backend

compatibility strategy to manage multiple app

versions in the wild simultaneously.

Users do not update immediately. You will always

have old versions active. Define how you handle that.

1. VERSION NUMBERING SCHEME

Format: MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH (semantic versioning)

- MAJOR: breaking change / complete redesign

- MINOR: new feature, backward compatible

- PATCH: bug fix, performance improvement

Build number: (auto-increment on every CI build — separate from version)

Version declaration per platform:

- iOS: CFBundleShortVersionString (display) + CFBundleVersion (build)

- Android: versionName (display) + versionCode (integer, always incrementing)

Single source of truth for version:

(package.json / version.json / environment variable / build config)

2. FORCE-UPDATE MECHANISM

Force-update required when:

- Security vulnerability patched

- Breaking API change deployed

- Critical bug that corrupts data

- Minimum supported OS version changed

Implementation:

- App sends version on every API request: (yes — header: X-App-Version / no)

- Backend checks version against minimum: (yes — server-side enforcement)

- Backend response when outdated:

{ "update_required": true, "min_version": "2.0.0", "store_url": "..." }

- App handles response: (block all UI / show force-update modal / redirect to store)

Force-update UI:

- Non-dismissible modal: (yes — user cannot proceed / no)

- Message: "A required update is available. Please update to continue."

- Deep link to app store: (yes — direct to update page)

- Allow background use: (no — block app / yes — warn only)

3. SOFT-UPDATE PROMPT

Soft update (recommended, not required):

- Trigger: new version available but not breaking

- UI: dismissible banner or bottom sheet

- Frequency: (once per session / once per day / once per week)

- "Remind me later" option: (yes / no)

- Track prompt dismissal: (yes — stop showing after N dismissals)

4. API BACKWARD COMPATIBILITY

Old app versions call old API behavior.

You cannot force all users to update immediately.

Therefore:

API versioning for mobile (aligns with §08 + §32):

- Version in URL: /api/v1/ /api/v2/ (cleanest for mobile)

- Maintain old versions for: ___ months after new version released

- Sunset notification: in-app message + API response header

Mobile-specific API rules:

- Never remove a field from a response (old apps will crash)

- Never change a field type (old apps will crash)

- Always add new fields as optional

- Test API changes against oldest supported app version

5. RELEASE CHANNELS

Distribution channels:

- Internal testing: (TestFlight / Firebase App Distribution / both)

- Beta testing: (TestFlight external / Google Play open testing)

- Production: (App Store / Google Play)

Phased rollout:

- iOS: (phased release — roll out to % of users over 7 days / full release)

- Android: (staged rollout — 10% → 50% → 100% / full release)

- Rollback trigger: (crash rate > ___% / ANR rate > ___% / manual)

6. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION

[ ] Version sent on every API request

[ ] Backend enforces minimum version

[ ] Force-update modal is non-dismissible

[ ] API maintains backward compatibility for old versions

[ ] Phased rollout configured with rollback trigger

[ ] OTA update strategy defined (M10)

[ ] Version aligns with §32 API versioning strategy

M3 — BACKGROUND PROCESSING & LIMITS

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Skip if: no background sync, no push-triggered

processing, no location tracking, and no background

downloads needed.

[PURPOSE]     → Define what work the app does in the background,

within strict OS-imposed time and resource limits.

iOS kills background tasks after 30 seconds.

Android restricts background work aggressively.

Apps that ignore these limits drain battery and

get removed from the background by the OS.

1. BACKGROUND WORK INVENTORY

Declare all background operations needed:

- [ ] Background data sync (upload/download data when app not in foreground)

- [ ] Silent push notification processing

- [ ] Background location updates

- [ ] Background audio playback

- [ ] Background download (large files)

- [ ] Background fetch (periodic data refresh)

- [ ] Geofencing

For each operation:

- Trigger: (push notification / timer / location event / app state change)

- Max execution time needed: ___ seconds

- Frequency: ___

- Data size: ___

2. iOS BACKGROUND MODES

iOS background modes required (declare each — must match actual usage):

- [ ] audio (background audio playback)

- [ ] location (continuous location updates)

- [ ] voip (VoIP calls)

- [ ] remote-notification (silent push processing)

- [ ] background-fetch (periodic background refresh)

- [ ] background-processing (long-running tasks via BGTaskScheduler)

BGTaskScheduler (iOS 13+):

- BGAppRefreshTask: periodic short tasks (max 30 seconds)

- BGProcessingTask: long tasks when plugged in (minutes)

- Tasks declared in Info.plist: (yes — all task identifiers listed)

- Earliest begin date: ___ (minimum interval between runs)

Invariant: You CANNOT use background modes you have not declared.

Apple audits this. Use only what you need.

3. ANDROID BACKGROUND PROCESSING

Android background work tool: (WorkManager — recommended for all deferred work)

WorkManager job types:

- OneTimeWorkRequest: single background task

- PeriodicWorkRequest: repeating task (min interval: 15 minutes)

- Chained work: sequential tasks

Constraints per job (declare):

- Network required: (yes — CONNECTED / UNMETERED / no)

- Battery not low: (yes / no)

- Device charging: (yes / no)

- Device idle: (yes / no)

Foreground Service (for user-visible ongoing work):

- Required for: (music playback / navigation / ongoing upload)

- Notification required: (yes — mandatory for foreground service)

- Service type declared: (dataSync / mediaPlayback / location)

Battery optimization exemption:

- Request "ignore battery optimization": (yes — user prompted / no)

- Justify why: (required for store approval)

4. BACKGROUND SYNC STRATEGY

Data sync when app resumes:

- On foreground: (full sync / delta sync / user-triggered only)

- Conflict resolution: (server wins / client wins / last-write-wins / manual merge)

- Failed sync queued: (yes — retry with exponential backoff / no)

Offline queue (if applicable):

- Queue store: (SQLite / AsyncStorage / MMKV / in-memory)

- Max queue size: ___ items

- Queue processing: (on reconnect / on foreground / on schedule)

M4 — BATTERY & PERFORMANCE OPTIMIZATION

[TRACK]       → Full Track

[CONDITIONAL] → Skip on Fast Track.

[PURPOSE]     → Define battery usage targets, CPU/memory budgets,

render performance standards, and the toolchain

that monitors them.

An app in the iOS battery usage list gets uninstalled.

Performance on low-end Android is a primary market.

1. PERFORMANCE TARGETS

App launch time:

- Cold start (first launch): < ___ ms  (good: <2000ms)

- Warm start (from background): < ___ ms  (good: <500ms)

- Time to interactive: < ___ ms

Frame rate:

- Target: 60 FPS (standard) / 120 FPS (ProMotion if supported)

- Dropped frame budget: < ___% frames dropped

- Jank-free scrolling: no frame drops > 16ms

Memory:

- Target memory usage (foreground): < ___ MB

- Memory warning threshold: > ___ MB triggers cleanup

- Memory leak tolerance: zero — all leaks are bugs

Battery:

- Background battery drain: < ___% per hour

- Active use drain: < ___% per hour

- Network requests per session: < ___ (batch where possible)

2. RENDER PERFORMANCE

List rendering (FlatList / RecyclerView):

- Virtual scrolling: (yes — required for lists > 50 items)

- Item recycling: (yes — reuse rendered cells)

- getItemLayout provided: (yes — avoids height measurement / no)

- keyExtractor: (yes — stable key per item)

- removeClippedSubviews: (yes — on Android / no)

Image rendering:

- Image caching library: (FastImage / SDWebImage / Glide / other)

- Resize images before display: (yes — to display size / no)

- Placeholder while loading: (blur hash / skeleton / color)

- Progressive loading for large images: (yes / no)

Animation:

- Use native driver: (yes — required for smooth animation)

- Animations on JS thread: (avoid — only for layout animations)

- Heavy animations on low-end: (reduced / disabled via accessibility setting)

3. NETWORK EFFICIENCY

Request batching:

- Batch multiple API calls: (yes / no — where applicable)

- GraphQL for batching: (yes / no — from §08)

- Avoid polling: (use WebSockets or push instead — from §09)

Data transfer optimization:

- Compress API responses: (gzip / brotli — from §08)

- Paginate large lists: (yes — from §08)

- Cache responses locally: (yes — from §21)

- Delta sync (send only changes): (yes / no)

Connection awareness:

- Detect network type (WiFi vs cellular): (yes / no)

- Reduce data usage on cellular: (yes — lower image quality / defer sync / no)

- NetInfo library used: (yes / no)

4. LOW-END DEVICE SUPPORT

Minimum device specs targeted:

- iOS: iPhone ___ (e.g. iPhone 8 — A11 chip, 2GB RAM)

- Android: ___ GB RAM, Android ___

Adaptations for low-end devices:

- Reduce animations: (yes — detect and disable / no)

- Lower image quality: (yes / no)

- Disable background effects: (yes / no)

- Reduce list prefetch distance: (yes / no)

Testing on low-end:

- Test device profile: (Android emulator with 2GB RAM / physical device)

- CI performance test on low-end profile: (yes / no)

5. PERFORMANCE MONITORING

Tools:

- iOS Instruments: (Time Profiler / Memory Graph / Energy Log)

- Android Profiler: (CPU / Memory / Network / Energy)

- RN/Flutter profiling: (Flipper / DevTools)

- Production monitoring: (Firebase Performance / Datadog / none)

Metrics to track in production:

- App start time (cold / warm)

- Screen load time per screen

- API call duration

- JS bundle parse time (React Native)

- Frame rate during key interactions

[ ] List virtualization on all long lists

[ ] Native driver used for all animations

[ ] Image caching library configured

M5 — DEVICE PERMISSION REQUEST FLOW

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No — every mobile app requests at least one

permission. Even push notifications require permission.

[PURPOSE]     → Define every device permission needed, when to

request it, how to explain it, and how to handle

denial gracefully.

iOS allows asking permission only ONCE.

If the user denies, they must go to Settings to

re-enable. Your one chance must be well-timed.

1. PERMISSION INVENTORY

Declare every permission the app needs:

| Permission           | iOS                    | Android              | When Needed       |

|----------------------|------------------------|----------------------|-------------------|

| Push notifications   | UNUserNotificationCenter| POST_NOTIFICATIONS   | ___               |

| Camera               | NSCameraUsageDesc      | CAMERA               | ___               |

| Photo library        | NSPhotoLibraryUsageDesc| READ_MEDIA_IMAGES    | ___               |

| Microphone           | NSMicrophoneUsageDesc  | RECORD_AUDIO         | ___               |

| Location (when use)  | NSLocationWhenInUse    | ACCESS_FINE_LOCATION | ___               |

| Location (always)    | NSLocationAlways       | ACCESS_BACKGROUND_LOC| ___               |

| Contacts             | NSContactsUsageDesc    | READ_CONTACTS        | ___               |

| Calendar             | NSCalendarsUsageDesc   | READ_CALENDAR        | ___               |

| Bluetooth            | NSBluetoothUsageDesc   | BLUETOOTH_CONNECT    | ___               |

| Face ID              | NSFaceIDUsageDesc      | USE_BIOMETRIC        | ___               |

2. PRE-PERMISSION RATIONALE (iOS)

iOS shows a system dialog that cannot be customized.

Show your own explanation BEFORE the system dialog to increase acceptance.

Pre-permission screen for each critical permission:

- Icon: (permission-relevant icon)

- Title: "Allow [App] to access your [permission]?"

- Body: (1–2 sentences — specific value to user, not legal text)

- Primary CTA: "Continue" → triggers system dialog

- Secondary: "Not now" → skips and can ask later

When NOT to show pre-permission:

- Do not ask at app launch (too early — context missing)

- Do not ask all at once

- Ask in context: camera permission when user taps camera button

3. PERMISSION REQUEST TIMING

For each permission, define the trigger:

- Push notifications: (after first value delivered / after onboarding / when user enables notifications in settings)

- Camera: (when user taps photo/camera button)

- Location: (when user uses location-dependent feature)

- Microphone: (when user starts recording)

Invariant: Never request a permission before the user

understands why they need it.

Invariant: Never request more than one permission at a time.

4. DENIAL HANDLING

When permission is denied:

- Show explanation of what they lose: (yes — brief message / no)

- Offer to open Settings: (yes — "Open Settings" button / no)

- Feature degrades gracefully: (yes — app still works without / no — feature unavailable)

- Retry request: (never re-request on iOS — user must go to Settings)

Denial states per permission:

- Camera denied: (show "Enable camera in Settings" prompt when camera needed)

- Location denied: (show manual location entry alternative)

- Notifications denied: (show in-app notification center as fallback)

5. PRIVACY USAGE DESCRIPTIONS

Every permission must have a usage description in Info.plist (iOS).

These appear in the system permission dialog.

Write them as user benefits, not technical descriptions.

Examples:

BAD:  "App requires camera access for functionality"

GOOD: "Take and upload profile photos directly in the app"

BAD:  "Location is used by the app"

GOOD: "Find events and meetups near your current location"

6. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION

[ ] Every permission has a usage description in Info.plist

[ ] No permissions requested at app launch

[ ] Pre-permission rationale screen for each critical permission

[ ] One permission requested at a time

[ ] Denial handled gracefully for all permissions

[ ] Settings deep link available for denied permissions

[ ] Android permission declarations in manifest

[ ] Runtime permissions requested at right moment (Android 6+)

[AGENT HINT]

→ Generate permission request hooks per permission type

→ Generate pre-permission rationale modal component

→ Generate permission status checker utility

→ Generate Settings deep link handler

→ Generate graceful degradation components for each denied permission

→ Generate Info.plist usage descriptions

→ Generate Android manifest permission declarations

M6 — BIOMETRIC AUTHENTICATION

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Skip if: no biometric login and no biometric

action confirmation needed.

[PURPOSE]     → Define Face ID / Touch ID (iOS) and fingerprint /

face recognition (Android) integration for login

and sensitive action confirmation.

Biometric auth requires secure credential storage —

this section defines the entire flow from enrollment

to token retrieval to fallback handling.

All decisions must reference:

- §06 Authentication model (token storage strategy)

- M5 Device Permission Request (Face ID permission)

1. BIOMETRIC USE CASES

Where biometric is used:

- [ ] App login (replace password entry)

- [ ] Re-authentication (unlock after timeout)

- [ ] Sensitive action confirmation (payment / delete / transfer)

- [ ] App lock (lock app after background)

2. CREDENTIAL STORAGE MODEL

What is stored in the secure enclave:

- Refresh token (encrypted, biometric-protected)

- NOT: passwords, PINs, sensitive data (never stored in plaintext)

Storage mechanism:

- iOS: Keychain with kSecAccessControlBiometryAny or BioCurrentSet

- Android: EncryptedSharedPreferences + BiometricPrompt + KeyStore

- React Native: react-native-keychain / expo-secure-store

Enrollment flow:

1. User logs in with password (first time)

2. App prompts: "Enable Face ID for faster login?"

3. User accepts → refresh token encrypted → stored in Keychain/Keystore

4. Next login → biometric prompt → decrypt token → authenticate silently

Biometric change handling (iOS: BioCurrentSet):

- If biometric changes (new fingerprint added): (invalidate stored token / require re-login)

- Reason: security — new biometric could be attacker's

3. BIOMETRIC PROMPT UI

Prompt configuration:

- Title: "Sign in to [App Name]"

- Subtitle: (optional — context specific)

- Cancel button label: "Use Password"

- Negative button (Android): "Cancel"

Fallback options (when biometric fails):

- After N failed attempts: (fall back to PIN / fall back to password)

- Device passcode fallback: (yes — automatic on iOS / yes — explicit on Android)

- Manual switch: "Use Password Instead" always visible

4. ERROR HANDLING

Handle all biometric error states:

- Not enrolled: (prompt to enable in Settings / skip biometric)

- Locked out (too many failures): (fall back to password — mandatory)

- Hardware not available: (skip biometric — use password only)

- Permission denied (Face ID): (prompt to enable in Settings — M5)

- Biometric changed: (invalidate and re-enroll)

- User cancelled: (show password login)

5. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION

[ ] Credentials stored in Keychain / Keystore only

[ ] Never store plaintext passwords

[ ] Biometric change invalidates stored credentials

[ ] Fallback to password always available

[ ] Face ID permission in M5 permission inventory

[ ] NSFaceIDUsageDescription in Info.plist

[ ] Aligns with §06 token storage strategy

[AGENT HINT]

→ Generate Keychain / Keystore credential storage service

→ Generate biometric prompt handler (iOS LAContext / Android BiometricPrompt)

→ Generate biometric enrollment flow

→ Generate biometric change detection and re-enrollment

→ Generate fallback to password flow

→ Generate app lock with biometric unlock

M7 — DEEP LINKING & UNIVERSAL LINKS

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No — every mobile app should handle deep links.

Push notifications, email links, web-to-app

transitions all require deep linking to work properly.

[PURPOSE]     → Define the deep link scheme, Universal Links (iOS)

and App Links (Android) configuration, link routing,

and deferred deep linking for new user installs.

1. LINK TYPES

Custom URL scheme (legacy, always works):

- Scheme: myapp:// (e.g. myapp://profile/123)

- Use for: internal navigation, push notification deep links

Universal Links / App Links (preferred — opens app or website):

- iOS Universal Links: https://yourapp.com/[path]

- Android App Links: https://yourapp.com/[path]

- Requires: AASA file (iOS) + assetlinks.json (Android) on your domain

- Fallback when app not installed: (web page / App Store redirect)

2. DEEP LINK ROUTE MAP

Define every deep link destination:

| Deep Link URL                        | Screen / Action                    | Auth Required |

|--------------------------------------|------------------------------------|---------------|

| myapp://dashboard                    | Main dashboard                     | Yes           |

| myapp://profile/[userId]             | User profile                       | No            |

| myapp://notification/[id]            | Specific notification              | Yes           |

| myapp://reset-password/[token]       | Password reset                     | No            |

| myapp://invite/[code]                | Accept invitation                  | No            |

| https://app.com/share/[contentId]    | Shared content page                | No            |

| [add all deep links for your app]    |                                    |               |

3. LINK HANDLING LOGIC

When app is open (foreground):

- Navigate directly to deep link destination

- Preserve current navigation stack or replace: (navigate / reset stack)

When app is in background:

- Bring to foreground + navigate to destination

- Animate transition: (yes / no)

When app is closed (cold start from link):

- App launches → check initial URL → navigate after auth check

- If auth required and not logged in: (store link → login → redirect after auth)

Link parsing:

- Parse URL scheme + path + query params

- Validate token/ID from URL before navigation

- Handle malformed links: (navigate to home / show error / ignore)

4. DEFERRED DEEP LINKING

Scenario: user clicks link → no app installed → App Store → install → link destination.

Deferred deep linking needed: (yes — important for onboarding / campaigns / no)

Implementation:

- Service: (Branch.io / Firebase Dynamic Links / AppsFlyer / custom)

- How it works: link metadata stored → matched after install by fingerprint

- Attribution tracking: (yes — link installs to campaigns / no)

5. UNIVERSAL LINKS CONFIGURATION

iOS — apple-app-site-association (AASA):

- Hosted at: https://yourapp.com/.well-known/apple-app-site-association

- Content-Type: application/json (no .json extension)

- Paths included: (list all paths that should open the app)

- Paths excluded: (list paths that should open the browser)

Android — assetlinks.json:

- Hosted at: https://yourapp.com/.well-known/assetlinks.json

- Includes: app package name + SHA-256 certificate fingerprint

6. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION

[ ] All push notification links use deep links (from M9 / §09)

[ ] AASA file hosted correctly (iOS)

[ ] assetlinks.json hosted correctly (Android)

[ ] Auth-required links redirect to login and return after auth

[ ] Malformed links handled gracefully

[ ] Deferred deep linking if marketing campaigns planned

[ ] Deep link route map covers all notification types

→ Generate assetlinks.json

→ Generate initial URL handler (cold start)

→ Generate deferred deep link setup (Branch / Firebase)

→ Generate deep link test suite

M8 — APP SIZE OPTIMIZATION

[TRACK]       → Full Track

[CONDITIONAL] → Skip on Fast Track.

[PURPOSE]     → Define app size budgets, asset optimization strategy,

and on-demand resource loading to keep install size

within limits that affect conversion and retention.

Every 6MB increase in install size = ~1% drop in

install conversion (Google study).

1. SIZE TARGETS

Install size targets:

- iOS IPA: < ___ MB (Apple limit for cellular download: 200MB)

- Android AAB: < ___ MB (Google Play limit: 150MB)

- Over-the-air update size: < ___ MB (M10)

Size budget breakdown:

- Native code / framework: ~___ MB

- Assets (images / fonts / sounds): < ___ MB

- JS bundle (React Native): < ___ MB

- Third-party SDKs: < ___ MB total

2. ASSET OPTIMIZATION

Images:

- Format: (WebP for Android / HEIF for iOS / PNG for icons)

- Resolution variants: (1x / 2x / 3x — only include what's needed)

- Remove unused assets: (yes — automated check in CI)

- Vector assets: (use SVG / XML vectors where possible — scale without size cost)

Fonts:

- Custom fonts: (list all — each font file adds 50–500KB)

- Subset fonts: (yes — include only glyphs used / no — full font)

- System fonts used where possible: (yes / no)

Audio / Video:

- Audio format: (AAC / MP3 — compressed)

- Video format: (H.264 — most compatible)

- Stream instead of bundle: (yes — load from CDN / no — bundled)

3. CODE OPTIMIZATION

JavaScript bundle (React Native):

- Enable Hermes engine: (yes — reduces bundle size + improves startup)

- Enable RAM bundles: (yes — load code on demand / no)

- Tree shaking: (yes — remove unused exports)

- Minification: (yes — enabled in production build)

- Remove dev-only code: (__DEV__ guards stripped in production)

Native code:

- Enable App Thinning (iOS): (yes — bitcode + slicing per device)

- Android App Bundle: (yes — Play delivers only needed APK splits)

- Enable ProGuard / R8 (Android): (yes — shrinks + obfuscates)

SDK audit:

- List all third-party SDKs and their size contribution

- Remove unused SDKs: (audit before each release)

4. ON-DEMAND RESOURCES

iOS On-Demand Resources (ODR):

- Assets downloaded only when needed: (yes / no)

- Use for: (level assets / tutorial content / language packs / none)

Android Dynamic Feature Modules:

- Features delivered on demand: (yes / no)

- Use for: (advanced features / regional content / none)

5. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION

[ ] App Thinning / App Bundle enabled

[ ] Unused assets removed from build

[ ] Custom fonts subsetted

[ ] Third-party SDK size audited

[ ] OTA update size aligns with M10 targets

M9 — CRASH REPORTING STRATEGY

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No — crash reporting is mandatory for any app

in production. You cannot fix what you cannot see.

[PURPOSE]     → Define crash reporting tooling, alerting thresholds,

symbolication setup, non-fatal error tracking,

and the triage process that turns crash reports

into resolved bugs.

1. CRASH REPORTING TOOL

Tool: (Firebase Crashlytics — free, recommended / Sentry / Bugsnag / Datadog)

Platforms covered: (iOS / Android / both)

Integration method: (SDK / React Native bridge / Flutter plugin)

What is captured:

- Fatal crashes: (yes — always)

- Non-fatal errors: (yes — caught exceptions / no)

- ANRs (Android Not Responding): (yes / no)

- Custom logs before crash: (yes — breadcrumbs / no)

- Custom keys per session: (yes — user ID, screen, action / no)

2. SYMBOLICATION

Without symbolication, crash stacks are unreadable memory addresses.

iOS dSYM upload:

- Automatic: (yes — via Xcode + Crashlytics plugin / no — manual)

- CI uploads dSYMs after every build: (yes — required)

- Bitcode builds: (yes — download dSYMs from App Store Connect)

Android mapping.txt upload:

- Automatic: (yes — via Gradle plugin / no — manual)

- ProGuard / R8 mapping uploaded: (yes — required if obfuscation enabled)

React Native JS stack trace:

- Source map upload: (yes — upload to Sentry / Crashlytics / required for readable RN stacks)

- Source map per release version: (yes — match to M2 version number)

3. CRASH RATE THRESHOLDS & ALERTING

Alert thresholds:

- Crash-free users rate drops below ___% → P1 alert (good target: >99.5%)

- New crash type with > ___ occurrences in 1 hour → P2 alert

- Crash rate increase > ___% vs previous version → P2 alert

- ANR rate > ___% (Android) → P2 alert

Alert routing: (PagerDuty / Slack channel / email — from §25 alert config)

4. TRIAGE PROCESS

On P1 crash alert:

1. Identify top crash by volume

2. Read symbolicated stack trace

3. Identify affected app version

4. Check if new version regression or pre-existing

5. If new regression: trigger rollback (M2) or hot fix

6. Communicate status in #incidents channel

Crash review cadence:

- Daily: review new crashes introduced in last 24h

- Weekly: review crash-free rate trend

- Per release: compare crash rate vs previous version before full rollout

5. USER IDENTIFICATION IN CRASHES

Set user ID in crash reporter: (yes — set on login / no — anonymous)

If yes:

- Set: userId only (not email, not name)

- Clear on logout: (yes — required for privacy)

- Aligns with §19 PII classification

Custom keys to attach per session:

- Current screen name

- App version (M2)

- User role / plan tier

- Last user action (breadcrumb)

6. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION

[ ] Crash reporter SDK integrated

[ ] dSYM / mapping.txt upload automated in CI

[ ] Source maps uploaded per version (React Native)

[ ] Crash-free rate alert configured

[ ] User ID set on login, cleared on logout

[ ] Triage process documented in runbook (§25)

[ ] Crash rate threshold triggers rollback in M2

M10 — OTA (OVER-THE-AIR) UPDATES

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Skip if: native app (Swift/Kotlin) — OTA only applies

to React Native, Expo, and Capacitor apps.

[PURPOSE]     → Define the OTA update strategy for JavaScript-based

mobile apps that can push JS bundle updates without

going through App Store review.

OTA enables hotfixes in minutes instead of days.

But it has limits — native code changes still

require store submission.

1. OTA SCOPE & LIMITS

Framework: (React Native / Expo / Capacitor)

OTA service: (Expo EAS Update / CodePush / Capgo / custom)

What CAN be updated via OTA:

- JavaScript / TypeScript code

- React component changes

- Business logic changes

- UI changes (non-native)

- Bug fixes in JS layer

- Asset updates (images, fonts bundled in JS)

What CANNOT be updated via OTA (requires store submission):

- Native module changes

- New permissions

- Info.plist / AndroidManifest changes

- SDK version upgrades

- App icons / launch screens

App Store rules on OTA:

- Apple: OTA updates must not change primary app purpose

- Google Play: less restrictive but same spirit

- Invariant: Do NOT use OTA to add features that would require review

2. UPDATE STRATEGY

Update channels:

- production: live users

- staging: internal testers

- development: developer builds

Update download trigger:

- On app launch: (yes — check for update silently / no)

- In background: (yes — download while app in use / no)

- On specific events: (e.g. after completing an action)

Update apply trigger:

- Immediate: (apply on next JS reload — disruptive)

- On next app launch: (recommended — apply after user closes app)

- Silent: (apply without user knowing — when app resumes from background)

User notification:

- Show "Update available" UI: (yes — for major updates / no — silent always)

- Force-apply OTA: (yes — for critical hotfixes / no — always on next launch)

3. ROLLBACK STRATEGY

Automatic rollback:

- If new OTA bundle causes crash on launch: (auto-rollback to previous bundle — yes / no)

- Crash detection window: first ___ seconds after update applied

- Rollback trigger: crash rate > ___% of update recipients

Manual rollback:

- Promote previous bundle to production: (one CLI command)

- Rollback time: < 5 minutes

4. BUNDLE SIZE & DIFFERENTIAL UPDATES

OTA update size target: < ___ MB (for fast update on mobile data)

Differential updates: (yes — only changed files downloaded / no — full bundle)

Bundle compression: (yes — gzip / brotli)

5. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION

[ ] OTA channels match deployment environments (§24)

[ ] Native changes go through store (never OTA)

[ ] Rollback tested before first production OTA

[ ] OTA bundle size within target

[ ] Crash auto-rollback configured

[ ] OTA update policy complies with App Store rules

[ ] Aligns with M2 force-update strategy

[AGENT HINT]

→ Generate Expo EAS Update config (eas.json)

→ Generate CodePush configuration

→ Generate OTA update check on app launch

→ Generate update channel management (prod/staging/dev)

→ Generate rollback trigger on crash detection

→ Generate CI OTA deployment pipeline

- Feature flags (enable/disable features remotely)

- Kill switches (disable broken features without OTA)

- Dynamic content (change strings/values without update)

- Experiment variants (serve different UI to different users)

Default values:

- All Remote Config values have local defaults: (yes — required)

- Reason: if fetch fails, app uses defaults — never undefined behavior

- Defaults match production-safe behavior

Fetch strategy:

- Fetch on every launch: (yes — but serve cached until next launch)

- Real-time updates: (yes — listener for flag changes / no — launch only)

- Connects to §26 analytics pipeline
