M12 — TABLET & LARGE SCREEN LAYOUT

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Skip if: tablet and large screen support explicitly

not required in §01.

[PURPOSE]     → Define adaptive layout strategy for tablets (iPad,

Android tablets) and large screens (foldables, iPads

in landscape).

A phone layout stretched to tablet is a bad app.

But building two separate apps is unnecessary.

Define the breakpoints and layout changes here.

1. DEVICE TARGETS

Devices to support:

- [ ] iPad (all sizes)

- [ ] iPad Pro (12.9" — very wide)

- [ ] Android tablets (7"–10")

- [ ] Android foldables (unfolded state)

- [ ] iPhone in landscape

- [ ] Android phone in landscape

2. LAYOUT BREAKPOINTS

Breakpoint definitions:

- Phone portrait:    < 600dp wide   → single column layout

- Phone landscape:  600–839dp wide  → compact two-panel or expanded single

- Tablet:           840–1199dp wide → two-column / master-detail

- Large tablet:     ≥ 1200dp wide   → three-column or wide content

Layout patterns per breakpoint:

PHONE (< 600dp):

- Navigation: bottom tab bar

- Lists: full-width single column

- Forms: full-screen

- Modals: full-screen sheet

TABLET (≥ 840dp):

- Navigation: sidebar (persistent or collapsible)

- Lists: master-detail (list left, detail right)

- Forms: centered with max-width

- Modals: centered overlay (not full-screen)

3. NAVIGATION ADAPTATION

Phone navigation: bottom tab bar

Tablet navigation: (left sidebar — always visible / collapsible drawer / split view)

Navigation transition:

- Detect screen width → swap navigation component

- Persist navigation state across orientation change

- iPad multitasking: (support split view / slide over / full screen only)

4. MASTER-DETAIL PATTERN

Screens that use master-detail on tablet:

- ___

Master-detail behavior:

- Phone: navigate to detail screen (push navigation)

- Tablet: show detail in right panel alongside list

- Empty state in detail panel: (show placeholder / first item selected automatically)

- URL state: (reflect selected item in URL / no)

5. CONTENT WIDTH & DENSITY

Max content width on large screens:

- Article / form content: max ___ dp (avoid overly wide text — max ~600dp for readability)

- Dashboard: max ___ dp or full-width grid

- Lists: (use grid layout on tablet — N columns / single column)

Touch target size:

- Phone: minimum 44x44dp (Apple) / 48x48dp (Material)

- Tablet: same minimums — larger targets preferred

Keyboard + pointer support (iPad with keyboard / Android with mouse):

- Hover states: (yes — pointer events supported / no)

- Keyboard shortcuts: (yes — cmd+N for new / no)

- Drag and drop: (yes / no)

6. CONSISTENCY VALIDATION

[ ] Breakpoints defined and used consistently

[ ] Navigation adapts correctly at tablet breakpoint

[ ] Master-detail implemented for list screens

[ ] No full-screen modals on tablet (use centered overlays)

[ ] Content max-width prevents overly wide text

[ ] iPad multitasking supported

[ ] Orientation changes handled without state loss

[ ] App Store screenshots include iPad sizes (M1)

[AGENT HINT]

→ Generate responsive layout hook (useBreakpoint)

→ Generate adaptive navigation component (tabs → sidebar)

→ Generate master-detail layout component

→ Generate responsive grid system

→ Generate orientation change handler

→ Generate iPad multitasking configuration (Info.plist)

→ Generate pointer/keyboard event handlers

LAYER 3 — APP-TYPE MODULES

3A THROUGH 3E

⚠ IMPORTANT: Run ONE module from this layer only.

These modules define what TYPE of app you are building.

They are mutually exclusive — your app is ONE type.

If your app fits two types, run the primary module fully,

then cherry-pick only the unique subsections from the secondary.

Run AFTER completing all relevant Layer 1 and Layer 2 sections.

These modules cover ONLY what is not already in Layer 1.

Each module calls out which Layer 1 sections to reference

rather than repeating content already defined there.

DO NOT CONFUSE WITH LAYER 4:

Layer 3 = WHAT TYPE of app is this? (pick one)

Layer 4 = WHAT FEATURES does this app have? (pick any combination)

MODULE SELECTION — PICK ONE:

3A → E-commerce / Marketplace  (selling products, bookings, or services)

3B → Social / Community        (users create content, follow, interact)

3C → AI-Powered App            (LLM / ML inference is a core feature)

3D → Regulated Industry        (healthcare, fintech, legal, education)

3E → Offline-First App         (app must work without internet)

3A — E-COMMERCE & MARKETPLACE

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Run only if: your app sells products, services,

bookings, or operates as a marketplace.

[PURPOSE]     → Define the complete commerce architecture —

catalog, cart, checkout, payments, orders,

shipping, returns, tax, and marketplace mechanics.

These decisions cannot be reverse-engineered from

a generic data model. Commerce has specific state

machines, legal obligations, and payment rules

that must be designed before the first endpoint.

Layer 1 sections to complete BEFORE this module:

§01 (monetization model), §06 (auth / buyer-seller roles),

§07 (DB — extend with commerce schema), §08 (API — add commerce endpoints),

§12 (integrations — PSP, shipping, tax providers),

§20 (compliance — PCI DSS), §28 (analytics — purchase funnel)

3. FEED ARCHITECTURE

Feed types:

- Home feed (content from people you follow)

- Explore / Discovery feed (content from people you don't follow)

- Profile feed (a specific user's content)

- Topic / hashtag feed

- Trending feed

Feed algorithm:

- Chronological: (simple, predictable, no ML needed)

- Algorithmic: (ranked by engagement / personalized — ML required)

- Hybrid: (chronological with algorithmic boost for high-engagement posts)

- Your choice: ___

Feed generation strategy:

- Push on write (fanout-on-write):

When user posts → immediately write to all followers' feed caches

PRO: fast read / CON: expensive for celebrities with millions of followers

- Pull on read (fanout-on-read):

When user opens feed → query followed users' recent posts

PRO: simple / CON: slow at scale

- Hybrid (recommended at scale):

Push for users with < ___ followers

Pull + merge for celebrity posts

Feed cache:

- Store: (Redis sorted set — score = timestamp / DynamoDB / Cassandra)

- TTL: ___ hours

- Max items per feed: ___ (paginate beyond this)

Feed pagination:

- Cursor-based: (yes — required for live feeds / no)

- Page size: ___ items per request

- New items indicator: "X new posts — tap to refresh"

7. UGC PIPELINE

UGC media flow (extends §10 File & Media Handling):

Processing per media type:

- Images: resize to multiple sizes, convert to WebP, strip EXIF metadata (location data!)

- Video: transcode to HLS (adaptive bitrate), generate thumbnail, strip metadata

- Audio: transcode to AAC, generate waveform visualization

Metadata stripping:

- Strip EXIF from all images before storage: (yes — required for user privacy)

- Strip GPS coordinates: (yes — always — confirmed)

1. AI PROVIDER ARCHITECTURE

- Your choice: ___

Streaming architecture:

Client → API → LLM Provider (streaming) → SSE/WS → Client

Server implementation:

- Stream from provider → proxy through your API (add auth, logging, rate limiting)

- Never expose provider API keys to client: (confirmed — invariant)

- Streaming endpoint: POST /api/ai/stream or WebSocket /ws/ai

Client implementation:

- Render tokens as they arrive: (yes — word-by-word rendering)

- Abort in-flight request: (yes — user can cancel / no)

- Reconnect on stream drop: (yes — with last_token_id cursor / no)

- Timeout: (stream timeout after ___ seconds of no tokens)

- Total: must not exceed model context window

- Sent to LLM: (all chunks / top-K relevant chunks via RAG)

6. RAG ARCHITECTURE

- Tool: (Pinecone / Weaviate / Qdrant / pgvector / Chroma / OpenSearch)

- Hosted vs self-managed: ___

- Namespace strategy: (per tenant / per document type / global)

- Dimensions: (match embedding model — e.g. 1536 for text-embedding-3-small)

Indexing pipeline:

Document → chunk → embed → store in vector DB

- Trigger: (on upload / on schedule / on demand)

- Chunking strategy: (fixed tokens / by paragraph / by section / recursive)

- Chunk size: ___ tokens / overlap: ___ tokens

- Metadata stored per chunk: (source ID, page, section, created date, tenant ID)

Retrieval strategy:

- Search type: (dense vector / sparse BM25 / hybrid — recommended)

- Top-K chunks retrieved: ___

- Reranking: (yes — cross-encoder reranker for precision / no — cosine similarity only)

- Minimum similarity threshold: ___ (filter low-relevance results)

RAG quality:

- Citation: (yes — tell LLM to cite sources, show user which chunks were used)

- Faithfulness check: (yes — verify answer is grounded in retrieved context)

- Hallucination detection: (yes — flag answers not supported by context)

Multi-tenant RAG:

- Data isolation: (each tenant's data in separate namespace / filtered by tenant_id)

- Invariant: Never mix tenants' data in the same RAG context.

7. AI OUTPUT SAFETY & GUARDRAILS

Input guardrails (before sending to LLM):

- Forbidden topics check: (yes — block requests outside app scope / no)

- PII detection in input: (yes — redact before sending to LLM / no)

- Toxic content filter: (yes — block harmful input / no)

Output guardrails (before returning to user):

- PII in output: (yes — scan and redact / no)

- Harmful content filter: (yes — toxic / violent / NSFW / no)

- Factual claim validation: (yes — for high-stakes responses / no)

- Structured output validation: (yes — validate JSON schema if applicable / no)

- Confidence threshold: (yes — show uncertainty disclaimer below threshold / no)

Guardrail tools:

- Provider's built-in: (OpenAI content policy / Anthropic safety)

- Additional: (Guardrails AI / LlamaGuard / Presidio for PII / custom)

Fallback when guardrail triggers:

- Input blocked: "I can't help with that" + log event

- Output blocked: regenerate once / show safe fallback message

- Both: log + alert + never expose raw guardrail error to user

8. AI CACHING STRATEGY

Cache types:

Exact cache:

- Cache key: hash(model + system_prompt + user_message)

- Store: Redis with TTL ___ hours

- Hit rate target: ___% (common queries, FAQs)

- When to cache: (deterministic queries / FAQ-style / template-based)

- When NOT to cache: (personalized / time-sensitive / user-specific)

Semantic cache:

- Cache key: embedding of user query

- Lookup: find cached responses where similarity > threshold ___

- Tool: (GPTCache / custom with vector DB / no)

- Risk: semantically similar but contextually different queries — set threshold carefully

Provider-side caching:

- OpenAI prompt caching: (automatic for prompts > 1024 tokens — use long stable system prompts)

- Anthropic prompt caching: (beta — explicit cache_control parameter)

Cache invalidation:

- On model version change: (flush entire cache)

- On system prompt change: (flush affected namespace)

- Manual flush: (admin endpoint for forced cache clear)

SECTION HEALTHCARE — HIPAA TECHNICAL SAFEGUARDS

1. PHI IDENTIFICATION & CLASSIFICATION

Protected Health Information (PHI) includes:

Names, dates (except year), geographic data smaller than state,

phone, fax, email, SSN, medical record numbers, health plan numbers,

account numbers, certificate numbers, device identifiers, URLs, IPs,

biometric identifiers, full-face photos, any unique identifier.

PHI inventory (list all PHI your app stores or processes):

- ___

PHI data flow map:

- Where PHI enters the system: ___

- Where PHI is stored: ___ (list all storage locations)

- Where PHI is transmitted: ___ (list all external destinations)

- Where PHI is displayed: ___ (list all surfaces where PHI is visible)

- Where PHI is deleted: ___ (retention and deletion per §29)

De-identification method (if applicable):

- Safe Harbor method: remove all 18 identifiers listed above

- Expert Determination: statistical verification of de-identification

- De-identified data is NOT PHI — confirm classification after de-id

2. HIPAA TECHNICAL SAFEGUARDS

Access controls (§164.312(a)(1)):

- Unique user identification: (yes — no shared accounts for PHI access)

- Emergency access procedure: (yes — break-glass access documented)

- Automatic logoff: (yes — after ___ minutes of inactivity — extends §06)

- Encryption and decryption: (yes — PHI encrypted at rest and in transit)

Audit controls (§164.312(b)):

- Log all PHI access: (yes — who accessed what PHI, when, from where)

- Log all PHI modifications: (yes — before and after values)

- Log all PHI disclosures: (yes — who PHI was sent to)

- Audit log tamper-proof: (yes — append-only / WORM storage / separate system)

- Audit log retention: ___ years (HIPAA minimum: 6 years)

- Audit log format: (timestamp / user_id / action / phi_record_id / ip_address)

Integrity controls (§164.312(c)(1)):

- PHI not altered in transit: (TLS 1.2+ — from §18)

- PHI not destroyed improperly: (deletion audit trail required)

- Data integrity verification: (checksums / hash validation on PHI records)

Transmission security (§164.312(e)(1)):

- All PHI transmissions encrypted: (yes — TLS 1.2+ minimum)

- Email with PHI: (encrypted email only / no email with PHI / patient portal messaging instead)

- API transmissions: (HTTPS only — no HTTP fallback for PHI endpoints)

3. BUSINESS ASSOCIATE AGREEMENTS (BAA)

A BAA is required with every vendor that touches PHI.

Vendors requiring a BAA:

- Cloud hosting (AWS / GCP / Azure): (yes — sign BAA with provider)

- Database (managed): (yes — if provider can access data)

- Email provider (SendGrid / Mailgun): (yes — if sending PHI in emails)

- Analytics (Mixpanel / Amplitude): (yes — if PHI in events — prefer no PHI in analytics)

- Error monitoring (Sentry): (yes — if PHI in error messages — scrub PHI from errors first)

- AI provider (OpenAI / Anthropic): (yes — only use HIPAA-eligible API tiers)

- Storage (S3 / GCS): (yes)

- Search (Elasticsearch / Algolia): (yes — if PHI in index)

- Support tools (Intercom / Zendesk): (yes — if PHI in support tickets)

BAA tracking:

- BAA status per vendor: (signed / pending / not required)

- BAA renewal cadence: (annual / as-needed)

- BAA gap = PHI disclosure violation = breach

SECTION FINTECH — PAYMENT & FINANCIAL COMPLIANCE

6. PCI DSS COMPLIANCE ARCHITECTURE

PCI DSS level:

- Level 1: > 6M transactions/year (annual QSA audit required)

- Level 2: 1–6M transactions/year

- Level 3: 20k–1M ecommerce transactions

- Level 4: < 20k ecommerce transactions

- Your level: ___

Cardholder Data Environment (CDE) scope:

- Reduce scope first: (use PSP-hosted fields / Stripe Elements — eliminates card data from your systems)

- If scope includes your systems: (list every system in CDE)

- SAQ type: (SAQ A — PSP hosted fields / SAQ A-EP / SAQ D — full CDE)

PCI DSS requirements (by SAQ type):

SAQ A (minimal scope — recommended):

- No card data touches your servers

- PSP is responsible for cardholder data

- Your obligation: HTTPS, access controls, annual self-assessment

SAQ D (full scope — avoid if possible):

- Network segmentation isolates CDE

- All 12 PCI DSS requirements apply

- Quarterly vulnerability scans (ASV)

- Annual penetration testing

- File integrity monitoring

- IDS/IPS in CDE

Data never stored (absolute prohibitions):

- Full card number (PAN) after authorization: (never)

- CVV / CVC: (never — even encrypted)

- PIN: (never)

- Invariant: These are PCI DSS absolute prohibitions. No exceptions.

Tokenization:

- All saved cards stored as tokens: (yes — from PSP / no cards stored locally)

- Token format: (PSP-specific — e.g. Stripe payment method ID)

7. FINANCIAL DATA SECURITY

Encryption standards for financial data:

- Data at rest: AES-256 (from §18 — confirm applies to all financial records)

- Data in transit: TLS 1.2+ (from §18 — confirm enforced on all financial endpoints)

- Key management: (AWS KMS / Azure Key Vault / HashiCorp Vault / HSM for Level 1)

- Key rotation: (annual / on compromise / automated)

- Envelope encryption: (yes — data key encrypted by master key / no)

Financial record immutability:

- Transactions are append-only: (yes — no updates, only new records)

- Ledger architecture: (double-entry bookkeeping / event sourcing / simple)

- Audit trail for every balance change: (yes — with actor, timestamp, reason)

Segregation of duties:

- No single person can: (create payment + approve payment + release funds)

- Technical controls: (role separation enforced in code / policy only)

8. KYC / AML ARCHITECTURE

KYC (Know Your Customer) required:

- Individual verification: (yes — government ID + liveness check)

- Business verification: (yes — company registration + beneficial ownership)

- KYC provider: (Stripe Identity / Onfido / Jumio / Persona)

- KYC trigger: (at signup / at first transaction / at threshold amount)

- KYC levels: (basic — email only / standard — ID / enhanced — additional docs)

AML (Anti-Money Laundering):

- Transaction monitoring: (yes — flag unusual patterns / no)

- Sanctions screening: (yes — OFAC, EU, UN sanctions lists — real-time check)

- Politically exposed persons (PEP): (yes — screen and flag / no)

- Suspicious Activity Reports (SARs): (yes — regulatory obligation / no)

- CTR (Currency Transaction Reports): (yes — for US transactions > $10k / no)

Risk scoring:

- User risk score: (low / medium / high based on KYC + transaction patterns)

- High risk users: (enhanced due diligence / restrict / off-board)

- Risk model: (rules-based / ML / third-party — Featurespace / Sardine)

9. TRANSACTION MONITORING

Fraud detection signals:

- Velocity checks: (too many transactions in short period)

- Geographic anomaly: (transaction from unusual country)

- Device fingerprint mismatch: (new device for large transaction)

- Behavioral anomaly: (unusual amount vs user history)

Fraud response:

- Low confidence fraud: (flag for review — allow transaction)

- High confidence fraud: (block transaction + alert user)

- Confirmed fraud: (freeze account + notify compliance team)

3DS (3D Secure) for card payments:

- 3DS2 required: (yes — EU Strong Customer Authentication / best practice globally)

- Frictionless flow: (for low-risk transactions)

- Challenge flow: (for high-risk transactions — user verifies with bank)

10. FINANCIAL REGULATORY REQUIREMENTS

SOX (public US companies):

- Internal controls over financial reporting: (documented)

- Segregation of duties: (technical controls in place)

- Change management controls: (all code changes logged and approved)

- Data retention: 7 years for financial records

FINRA (US broker-dealers):

- Communications archived: (yes — all client communications / no)

- Trade surveillance: (yes — review all transactions for manipulation / no)

- Books and records: (complete and accurate financial records maintained)

MiFID II (EU investment services):

- Best execution reporting

- Transaction reporting to regulators

- Record keeping: 5 years

- Client classification: (retail / professional / eligible counterparty)

FCA (UK):

- SM&CR (Senior Managers and Certification Regime): (individual accountability)

- Operational resilience: (important business services must stay within impact tolerances)

11. ENHANCED AUDIT TRAIL ARCHITECTURE

Audit trail requirements (beyond §27 Observability):

Every audit event must capture:

- who: (user_id + role + IP address + session_id)

- what: (action performed + resource type + resource_id)

- when: (timestamp — millisecond precision + timezone)

- why: (business reason if applicable — e.g. "patient consent on file")

- result: (success / failure + error code)

- before: (previous state of modified resource)

- after: (new state of modified resource)

Audit storage:

- Separate from application DB: (yes — dedicated audit store)

- Append-only: (yes — updates and deletes prohibited)

- WORM storage: (yes — Write Once Read Many — for regulatory compliance)

- Options: (AWS S3 Object Lock / Azure Immutable Blob / purpose-built audit DB)

- Retention: (HIPAA: 6 years / PCI DSS: 1 year online + 3 years archive / SOX: 7 years)

Audit trail integrity:

- Hash chaining: (yes — each event includes hash of previous event / no)

- Cryptographic signing: (yes — events signed with private key / no)

- Tamper detection: (yes — daily integrity check / no)

Access to audit logs:

- Who can read: (compliance officer / auditors / no application users)

- Who can delete: (nobody — ever)

- Export format: (CSV / JSON / SIEM-compatible)

Data residency requirements:

- PHI must stay in: (US / EU / specific country / no restriction)

- Regulated data cannot go to: ___

- Cloud region locked: (yes — deploy only in compliant regions)

Data localization for multi-region:

- EU customers' data in EU region: (yes)

- US customers' data in US region: (yes)

- Sub-processor list: (yes — maintained / no)

- Annual review: (yes / no)

- Maintain list of all vendors with: name / data accessed / certification / DPA status / last reviewed

- Critical vendors: (annually reassessed)

- Non-critical vendors: (every 2 years)

Vendor offboarding:

- Data deletion certification required: (yes — vendor must confirm data deleted)

14. INCIDENT RESPONSE FOR REGULATED DATA

Breach notification timelines (regulatory):

- HIPAA: (covered entity notifies HHS + affected individuals within 60 days / media if > 500 in state)

- PCI DSS: (notify card brands within 24 hours of suspected breach)

- GDPR: (notify supervisory authority within 72 hours — from §19/§20)

- State breach laws: (notify affected residents — timeline varies by state)

Breach response playbook:

1. Detect & contain: (isolate affected systems within ___ hours)

2. Assess: (what data was exposed? how many affected?)

3. Legal: (engage legal counsel within ___ hours)

4. Notify regulator: (within regulatory timeline above)

5. Notify affected individuals: (with clear explanation and remediation)

6. Remediate: (patch vulnerability / rotate credentials / review controls)

7. Post-mortem: (root cause analysis + control improvements)

Forensic readiness:

- Preserve logs before system changes: (yes — snapshot logs immediately on incident)

- Evidence chain of custody: (yes — documented / no)

- Forensic investigation capability: (internal / third-party IR firm on retainer)

15. EMPLOYEE ACCESS CONTROLS

Access principles:

- Least privilege: (every employee has minimum access to do their job)

- Need-to-know: (regulated data access requires documented business need)

- Separation of duties: (no single person has end-to-end control of regulated process)

Access provisioning:

- Access requests: (ticket-based + manager approval)

- Production access: (requires compliance team approval)

- Privileged access (admin / DBA / root): (require additional justification + time-limited)

Access reviews:

- Quarterly access review: (yes — review all privileged access / no)

- Automated de-provisioning on offboarding: (yes — within ___ hours)

Background checks:

- Required for: (all employees / employees with regulated data access only)

- Check types: (criminal / financial for fintech / reference)

- Cadence: (at hire / periodic re-check every ___ years)

Security training:

- Annual security awareness training: (yes — mandatory)

- HIPAA training: (yes — for all staff accessing PHI — HIPAA requirement)

- Phishing simulation: (yes — quarterly / no)

3E — OFFLINE-FIRST APPLICATION

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Run only if: your app must work fully or partially

without internet connectivity.

[PURPOSE]     → Define the local-first architecture, sync engine,

conflict resolution strategy, offline queue, and

UX patterns for disconnected operation.

Offline-first is an architectural decision, not a

feature toggle. Every data access pattern, every

write operation, and every UI state must be designed

for the offline case from the start.

Adding offline to an online-first app is a full rewrite.

Layer 1 sections to complete BEFORE this module:

§09 Real-time (sync reconnect), §13 Async (offline queue),

§15 Frontend state (optimistic UI), §17 Data integrity (conflict model),

§21 Caching (local data), §22 Resilience (reconnect handling),

M3 Background sync, W4 Service worker offline

1. OFFLINE-FIRST ARCHITECTURE DECISION

Offline philosophy:

- Local-first: (local DB is primary source of truth — syncs to server when online)

- Cache-first: (online is primary — cache is fallback for reads only)

- Hybrid: (certain data types local-first, others cache-first)

- Your choice: ___

What works offline:

- [ ] View all previously loaded data

- [ ] Create new records

- [ ] Edit existing records

- [ ] Delete records

- [ ] Search (local search only)

- [ ] File attachments

- [ ] Forms and drafts

What requires connectivity (explicitly online-only):

- [ ] Payment processing

- [ ] Real-time collaboration

- [ ] Sending emails / notifications

- [ ] Fetching new data from other users

- [ ] AI features

Data availability scope:

- All user data available offline: (yes / no — which data is excluded)

- Data freshness acceptable when offline: (stale-but-available / must show age of data)

- Initial sync on first login: (yes — full dataset / partial — last N days / lazy on demand)

- Max offline data size: ___ MB / GB

2. LOCAL DATABASE SELECTION

Platform options:

MOBILE (React Native):

- WatermelonDB: (high performance, lazy loading, sync-ready — recommended for large datasets)

- Realm: (MongoDB-based, reactive, good sync story via Atlas Device Sync)

- SQLite via expo-sqlite: (standard, simple, manual sync)

- MMKV: (key-value only — not for relational data)

MOBILE (Flutter):

- Drift (SQLite): (type-safe, reactive, good for complex queries)

- Isar: (fast NoSQL, good for offline-first)

- ObjectBox: (reactive, relationship support)

WEB:

- IndexedDB (raw): (built-in, complex API)

- Dexie.js: (IndexedDB wrapper — much simpler)

- RxDB: (reactive, multi-platform, sync support)

- PouchDB + CouchDB: (mature, built-in sync, CRDT-like)

CROSS-PLATFORM:

- PowerSync: (Postgres to SQLite sync — production-ready)

- ElectricSQL: (Postgres to SQLite, CRDT-based sync)

- Replicache: (write-ahead log sync, conflict-free)

- Zero (Rocicorp): (real-time sync layer, local-first)

Your choice: ___

Reason: ___

3. SYNC ENGINE ARCHITECTURE

Sync model:

- Pull-only: (client pulls from server — simpler, no collaboration)

- Push-pull: (client pushes local changes + pulls remote changes)

- Bidirectional real-time: (changes sync immediately — requires CRDT or OT)

- Your model: ___

Sync trigger:

- On reconnect: (yes — always / no)

- Periodic background sync: (yes — every ___ minutes / no)

- On foreground: (yes — sync when app comes to foreground / no)

- Manual user trigger: (yes — pull to refresh / no)

Sync protocol:

- Full sync: (download everything — only for small datasets)

- Delta sync: (download only changes since last sync — required at scale)

- Cursor-based: (server maintains cursor per client — client sends cursor, gets changes since)

- Event log: (server appends all changes to log — client replays from last position)

Sync state per entity:

local_only   → created locally, not yet synced

synced       → matches server

modified     → local change pending sync

conflict     → local and remote both changed

deleted      → soft-deleted, pending server confirmation

4. CONFLICT RESOLUTION STRATEGY

Conflict occurs when:

- Client edits record while offline

- Server (or another client) also edits same record

- Client reconnects — two divergent versions exist

Conflict resolution strategies:

Last-Write-Wins (LWW):

- Compare timestamps — most recent write wins

- Simple, lossy — data can be silently overwritten

- Best for: non-critical data, user preferences, counters

- Invariant: Clocks on client are not reliable — use server timestamp.

Server-Wins:

- Server version always authoritative on conflict

- Client changes discarded

- Best for: financial data, regulated data, shared state

Client-Wins:

- Client version always wins

- Server version discarded

- Best for: personal drafts, private notes, offline-created content

Merge (CRDT — Conflict-free Replicated Data Type):

- Both versions merged automatically without data loss

- Best for: collaborative text, counters, sets, maps

- Types: (G-Counter / PN-Counter / LWW-Element-Set / RGA for text)

- Libraries: (Automerge / Yjs / custom)

Manual Resolution:

- Present both versions to user — user picks

- Best for: high-value content where automatic resolution is too risky

- UI: show diff, highlight conflicts, offer merge or choose

Your conflict resolution per data type:

| Data Type            | Strategy    | Reason                 |

|----------------------|-------------|------------------------|

| User profile         | LWW         | Low stakes, personal   |

| Documents / notes    | CRDT / merge| Collaborative          |

| Financial records    | Server-wins | Regulatory requirement |

| Tasks / todos        | LWW         | Last edit wins         |

| [your types]         | ___         | ___                    |

5. OPTIMISTIC UI ARCHITECTURE

Optimistic update: show result immediately in UI before server confirms

Apply optimistic update:

1. User performs action (create / update / delete)

2. Write to local DB immediately

3. Show result in UI immediately

4. Queue sync operation

5. When sync succeeds: mark local record as synced

6. When sync fails: revert local change + show error

Rollback on failure:

- Revert all UI changes from failed operation

- Show error: "Couldn't save — changes reverted. Try again."

- Preserve failed change for retry: (yes — retry queue / no — discard)

Pending state indicators:

- Show when a record has unsynced local changes: (yes — icon/label / no)

- Show when sync is in progress: (yes — spinner / no)

- Show count of pending changes: (yes — in settings / sync indicator / no)

Operations that must NOT be optimistic:

- Payment processing (always server-authoritative)

- Permission checks (never trust client)

- Regulatory actions (audit trail required)

6. NETWORK STATE MACHINE

States:

ONLINE       → full connectivity, sync active

OFFLINE      → no connectivity, local-only mode

RECONNECTING → connectivity restored, sync in progress

PARTIAL      → connectivity but sync failing (server error, auth issue)

DEGRADED     → online but slow (high latency, timeouts)

Transitions:

ONLINE → OFFLINE: (network event / request timeout)

OFFLINE → RECONNECTING: (network restored event)

RECONNECTING → ONLINE: (sync complete)

RECONNECTING → PARTIAL: (sync failing)

PARTIAL → ONLINE: (issue resolved)

ONLINE → DEGRADED: (latency > ___ ms)

Network detection:

- Platform events: (navigator.onLine / NetInfo for React Native)

- Active probe: (ping server every ___ seconds when status uncertain)

- Do not rely solely on navigator.onLine — it can be wrong

Actions per state:

- ONLINE: sync queue, stream real-time, full feature set

- OFFLINE: local only, queue writes, hide online-only features

- RECONNECTING: show sync progress, disable conflict-prone actions

- PARTIAL: show warning, block writes until resolved

- DEGRADED: show performance warning, reduce polling frequency

7. OFFLINE QUEUE MANAGEMENT

Queue storage:

- Persistent queue: (yes — survives app restart — store in local DB / SQLite / IndexedDB)

- Queue structure: (FIFO — first in first out / priority queue)

Queue item structure:

{

id: unique_id,

operation: 'create' | 'update' | 'delete',

entity: entity_type,

payload: serialized_change,

created_at: timestamp,

attempts: 0,

status: 'pending' | 'in_flight' | 'failed',

priority: 1-5

}

Queue processing:

- Process on reconnect: (yes — immediately)

- Process order: (FIFO / by priority / by entity dependency)

- Dependency ordering: (yes — create parent before child / no)

Retry strategy:

- Max attempts: ___

- Backoff: (exponential — 1s, 2s, 4s, 8s... / fixed / no backoff)

- Failed after max attempts: (dead letter queue / notify user / discard)

- Dead letter queue: (yes — user can review and retry / no)

Queue size limits:

- Max items in queue: ___

- Max total size: ___ MB

- When limit reached: (block new offline writes / FIFO eviction / notify user)

8. DATA PARTITIONING FOR OFFLINE

Not all data needs to be available offline.

Define explicitly what is and is not offline-available.

Offline-available (stored locally):

| Data Type         | Reason                    | Local TTL  |

|-------------------|---------------------------|------------|

| User profile      | Core to app function      | Indefinite |

| Recent records    | Most common access        | 30 days    |

| Drafts            | Created offline           | Indefinite |

| [your data types] | ___                       | ___        |

Online-only (never stored locally):

| Data Type         | Reason                    |

|-------------------|---------------------------|

| Other users' data | Privacy — only user's own |

| Payment data      | PCI compliance            |

| Audit logs        | Integrity requirement     |

| [your data types] | ___                       |

Partial offline (cached but read-only):

| Data Type         | Cached for    | Writable offline |

|-------------------|---------------|------------------|

| Reference data    | 7 days        | No               |

| Templates         | 7 days        | No               |

Data freshness policy:

- Show data age when offline: (yes — "Last synced: 2 hours ago" / no)

- Stale data threshold: (data older than ___ hours shown with warning)

9. OFFLINE SECURITY MODEL

Local database encryption:

- Encrypted at rest: (yes — SQLCipher for SQLite / Realm encryption / IndexedDB via Dexie with encryption)

- Encryption key: (derived from user's PIN/biometric — do NOT store key in plaintext)

- Key derivation: (PBKDF2 / Argon2 — from user credential + device-unique salt)

Auth token offline validity:

- Token valid offline for: ___ hours (user stays logged in without server verification)

- Token revocation offline: (cannot verify — accept risk of short validity window)

- Biometric re-auth when offline: (yes — verify biometric before decrypting local DB / no)

Data access when offline:

- Can user access their data after session expires offline: (yes — with biometric / no — must be online to re-auth)

- Sensitive data hidden offline: (yes — require online auth for PII / no)

Device loss:

- Remote wipe: (yes — mark device as wiped server-side; on next sync, wipe local DB / no)

- Data accessible without app: (no — encrypted local DB requires app + credential)

10. DELTA SYNC & BANDWIDTH OPTIMIZATION

Delta sync (send only changes):

- Track last sync timestamp per entity type

- Server returns only changes since that timestamp

- Client applies changes to local DB

Sync payload optimization:

- Compress sync payloads: (yes — gzip / no)

- Send only changed fields: (yes — field-level delta / no — full record)

- Batch changes: (yes — group multiple changes in one request / no — one request per change)

- Sync batch size: max ___ changes per request

Network awareness:

- WiFi vs cellular sync: (full sync on WiFi / metadata-only on cellular)

- Low data mode: (detect user preference / respect OS data saver mode)

- Defer large attachments: (sync attachments separately from data / sync on WiFi only)

Sync frequency:

- Background sync interval: ___ minutes (on mobile — respects M3 background limits)

- Foreground sync: (immediate on change / debounced ___ seconds / on user action)

- Maximum sync frequency: (prevent sync storms — minimum ___ seconds between syncs)

11. OFFLINE TESTING STRATEGY

Test scenarios required:

Connectivity scenarios:

- [ ] Start offline → use app → go online → verify sync

- [ ] Go offline mid-operation → complete operation → go online → verify

- [ ] Flapping connection (on/off rapidly) → verify no data corruption

- [ ] Slow connection (high latency) → verify timeout handling

- [ ] Partial sync failure → verify partial results handled correctly

Conflict scenarios:

- [ ] Same record edited on two devices while offline → verify conflict resolution

- [ ] Delete on one device while edit on another → verify expected behavior

- [ ] Create record offline with same ID as server record → verify handling

Queue scenarios:

- [ ] Queue fills to limit → verify limit behavior

- [ ] App restart with items in queue → verify queue survives restart

- [ ] Queue item fails max retries → verify dead letter behavior

Testing tools:

- Network throttling: (Chrome DevTools / Android emulator network profiles / iOS Network Link Conditioner)

- Offline simulation: (Chrome offline mode / airplane mode)

- Automated: (Playwright offline mode / custom network mock)

- Load test offline queue: (simulate N items in queue, measure sync time)

12. OFFLINE UX PATTERNS

Status indicators:

- Offline banner: (yes — persistent when offline / dismissible)

- Sync progress: (yes — progress bar during reconnect sync / no)

- Last synced timestamp: (yes — shown in settings / no)

- Pending changes count: (yes — "3 changes pending sync" / no)

Optimistic update feedback:

- Unsynced indicator on records: (subtle icon — not alarming / no)

- Tooltip on hover/tap: "This change will sync when you're online"

- Success confirmation: delayed until sync confirms (or immediate + correct if needed)

Conflict UI (if manual resolution):

- Show both versions side by side

- Highlight conflicting fields

- "Keep mine" / "Keep theirs" / "Merge" actions

- Timestamp and device context for each version

Offline-only features blocked gracefully:

- Online-only actions show: (tooltip "Requires internet connection" / disabled state / hidden)

- Error if attempted: (specific message — not generic "something went wrong")

Data age warning:

- Show when cached data may be stale: (yes — "Last updated X hours ago" / no)

- Critical data (financial, medical): (always show last sync time)

§33 — REPORTING & ANALYTICS ARCHITECTURE

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No — every SaaS app needs a reporting layer.

[PURPOSE]     → Define how users view, build, schedule, and export

reports from their own data. This section covers

the report architecture, data access model, builder

delivery.

understand usage). This section covers user-facing

1. REPORT SCOPE & TYPES

Report types your app needs:

- [ ] Summary / KPI dashboard (key numbers at a glance)

- [ ] Time-series report (metric over time — line/bar chart)

- [ ] Tabular report (rows and columns — sortable, filterable)

- [ ] Funnel report (conversion steps — where users drop off)

- [ ] Cohort report (how groups behave over time)

- [ ] Retention report (how many users return after N days)

- [ ] Revenue / financial report (MRR, ARR, churn, LTV)

- [ ] Custom report (user-defined dimensions and metrics)

- [ ] Audit / activity report (who did what — compliance)

Who creates reports:

- Platform-defined only: (reports built by you, users just view)

- User-built: (users create their own reports from available data)

- Both: (platform templates + user customization)

Data freshness:

- Real-time: (live queries — expensive but current)

- Near real-time: (5–15 min lag — materialized views / streaming)

- Daily batch: (reports run overnight — cheapest)

- Your choice per report type: ___

2. DATA ARCHITECTURE FOR REPORTING

Query model:

- Query live OLTP DB: (yes — acceptable for small data / no — creates lock contention)

- Read replica: (yes — route report queries to replica / no)

- Separate analytics DB / data warehouse: (yes — recommended at scale)

- Data warehouse: (BigQuery / Redshift / Snowflake / ClickHouse / DuckDB)

Data pipeline (if separate analytics DB):

- ETL / ELT tool: (Airbyte / Fivetran / dbt / custom)

- Sync frequency: (real-time CDC / hourly / nightly)

- Transformation layer: (dbt models / raw SQL views / no transformation)

Pre-aggregation (for fast report loading):

- Materialized views: (yes — pre-compute common aggregations / no)

- Summary tables: (yes — daily/weekly/monthly rollups stored / no)

- Cache report results: (yes — Redis / CDN — TTL ___ minutes / no)

- Rebuild trigger: (on schedule / on data change / on demand)

Multi-tenant data isolation (critical):

- Every report query scoped to tenant: (yes — tenant_id in every WHERE clause)

- Row-level security in DB: (yes — enforced at DB layer / application layer only)

- Invariant: A user must never see another tenant's data in a report. Enforce at DB level, not just application level.

§34 — MESSAGING & COMMUNICATION ARCHITECTURE

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Skip if: no in-app messaging between users or

between users and support/team.

[PURPOSE]     → Define the complete in-app messaging architecture —

direct messages, group conversations, message states,

real-time delivery, encryption, moderation, and

optional video/voice calling.

This section covers user-to-user communication inside

your app. It does NOT cover transactional emails,

push notifications, or SMS — those are in §12 and §09.

Layer 1 references: §09 Real-time (WebSocket transport),

§10 File/Media (message attachments), §06 Auth (message permissions),

§19 Privacy (message data classification),

§16 Rate limiting (message send limits)

1. MESSAGING SCOPE

Messaging types needed:

- [ ] Direct message (1-to-1 between users)

- [ ] Group conversation (multiple participants)

- [ ] Channel / topic-based (like Slack channels)

- [ ] Threaded replies (reply to a specific message)

- [ ] Support chat (user to support agent)

- [ ] AI chat (user to AI assistant — see §3C)

- [ ] Broadcast (admin to all users — one-way)

Who can message whom:

- Any user can message any other user: (yes / no — only connections/followers)

- Must follow before messaging: (yes — from 3B social graph / no)

- Message requests (unknown senders go to requests folder): (yes / no)

- Business accounts can message users: (yes / no)

Message persistence:

- Messages stored permanently: (yes / no)

- Retention policy: ___ days (then auto-deleted / archived)

- Ephemeral messages (disappear after reading): (yes — optional per message / no)

2. CONVERSATION & INBOX MODEL

Inbox structure:

- All conversations in one inbox: (yes / no)

- Separate tabs: (primary / requests / archived / spam)

- Unread count per conversation: (yes)

- Global unread badge (tab / app icon): (yes)

Conversation model:

Conversation {

id, type (direct/group/channel),

participants: [userId],

created_by, created_at,

last_message_at,   // for sorting inbox

last_message_preview,

unread_count per participant,

is_muted per participant,

is_archived per participant

}

Conversation creation:

- DM: find or create (one DM conversation per pair of users)

- Group: user selects participants, sets name + optional avatar

- Max participants per group: ___

- Max active conversations per user: ___ (soft limit)

Inbox sorting:

- Default: most recent message first

- Pinned conversations: (yes — pinned stay at top / no)

- Muted conversations: (moved to bottom / separate tab / hidden)

3. MESSAGE MODEL & STATES

Message structure:

Message {

id, conversation_id, sender_id,

type: 'text' | 'image' | 'file' | 'audio' | 'video' | 'system',

content: encrypted_text,

attachments: [{ url, type, size, name }],

reply_to_message_id,   // for threaded replies

reactions: [{ emoji, user_ids }],

is_edited, edited_at,

is_deleted, deleted_at,

status: 'sending' | 'sent' | 'delivered' | 'read' | 'failed',

created_at

}

Message delivery states:

- sending: queued locally, not yet confirmed by server

- sent: server received and stored

- delivered: recipient device received

- read: recipient opened conversation

- failed: could not deliver after retries

Read receipts:

- Show read receipts: (yes — double tick / eye icon / no)

- Per-user opt-out of read receipts: (yes / no)

- Read receipt granularity: (per message / per conversation / no)

- Group read receipts: (show who has read / count only / no)

Typing indicator:

- Show "User is typing...": (yes / no)

- Typing event sent: (on keypress — debounced ___ ms)

- Typing timeout: (stop showing after ___ seconds of no keypress)

- Group typing: ("User A and User B are typing" / "2 people are typing")

4. REAL-TIME DELIVERY

Transport (from §09 Real-Time Architecture):

- WebSocket: (yes — required for typing indicators + instant delivery)

- Connection per user: (one persistent WebSocket connection handles all conversations)

- Reconnect strategy: (exponential backoff — from §22 resilience)

Message delivery flow:

1. Sender types → sends via WebSocket or POST /messages

2. Server validates + stores message

3. Server pushes to all online recipients via WebSocket

4. Server queues push notification for offline recipients (§09)

5. Recipients acknowledge receipt → status updated to "delivered"

6. Recipient opens conversation → status updated to "read"

Online presence:

- Track online/offline status: (yes / no)

- Last seen timestamp: (yes — show to contacts / no)

- Last seen privacy: (everyone / contacts only / nobody)

- Appear offline option: (yes / no)

Multi-device:

- Messages sync across devices: (yes — user logged in on phone + desktop both receive)

- Unread count synced: (yes — marking read on one device clears on all)

5. MESSAGE ACTIONS

Actions per message:

- React (emoji): (yes — which emojis: ___ / no)

- Reply (threaded): (yes / no)

- Forward to another conversation: (yes / no)

- Copy text: (yes)

- Edit: (yes — within ___ minutes / no)

- Edited label shown: (yes — "(edited)" / no)

- Edit history visible: (yes / no)

- Delete for me: (removes from your view only)

- Delete for everyone: (yes — within ___ minutes / no)

- Shown as: "This message was deleted"

- Report message: (yes — from §3B moderation / no)

- Pin message: (yes — pinned messages visible at top / no)

- Star / bookmark: (yes — saved messages folder / no)

7. MESSAGE SEARCH

Search scope:

- Search within conversation: (yes / no)

- Search across all conversations: (yes / no)

- Search attachments / filenames: (yes / no)

Search implementation:

- Full-text search: (PostgreSQL FTS / Elasticsearch / Typesense — from §11)

- Encrypted messages: (search index on decrypted content server-side / client-side search only if E2EE)

- Search results show: (message snippet + conversation name + sender + date)

- Jump to message: (yes — scroll to and highlight message in conversation)

Search limitations with E2EE:

- Invariant: Server-side full-text search is impossible if messages are end-to-end encrypted. Choose: searchability OR E2EE — not both without client-side search.

8. ENCRYPTION MODEL

Encryption levels (choose one):

Encryption at rest + in transit only (server can read):

- Messages encrypted in DB: (AES-256 — from §18)

- TLS in transit: (yes — from §18)

- Server has access to plaintext: YES

- Search works: YES

- Compliance subpoenas can produce message content: YES

- Use when: most B2B apps, support chat, moderated platforms

End-to-end encryption (E2EE — server cannot read):

- Protocol: (Signal Protocol / MLS / custom)

- Key management: (each user has key pair — private key never leaves device)

- Key exchange: (X3DH — Extended Triple Diffie-Hellman)

- Forward secrecy: (yes — Double Ratchet algorithm)

- Group E2EE: (yes — Sender Keys / MLS — more complex)

- Server stores: ciphertext only — cannot decrypt

- Search: client-side only (limited)

- Key backup: (yes — encrypted backup to server / no — lost device = lost messages)

- Use when: healthcare, legal, high-privacy consumer apps

Your choice: ___

Reason: ___

9. VIDEO & VOICE CALLING

(Skip if no video/voice calling needed)

- [ ] 1-to-1 voice call

- [ ] 1-to-1 video call

- [ ] Group voice call (max ___ participants)

- [ ] Group video call (max ___ participants)

- [ ] Screen sharing

Transport: WebRTC (peer-to-peer where possible / server-mediated SFU)

Infrastructure:

- STUN/TURN servers: (required for NAT traversal — Twilio TURN / Coturn self-hosted)

- SFU (Selective Forwarding Unit): (required for group calls > 4 participants)

- Managed service: (Twilio / Daily.co / Agora / Livekit / 100ms / self-hosted)

- Fallback when P2P fails: (relay via TURN server)

Call features:

- Mute audio: yes

- Disable video: yes

- Screen share: (yes / no)

- Background blur: (yes / no)

- Recording: (yes — stored in §10 / no)

- Call invite via message: (yes — send call link in conversation)

Call states:

calling → ringing → connected → ended

↓

declined / missed / no answer

Missed call notification:

- Push notification: (yes — from §09)

- Missed call in conversation: (yes — "Missed call — tap to call back")

10. MODERATION & SAFETY

Message moderation:

- Automated content scan before delivery: (yes — toxic / CSAM / spam / no)

- Delay delivery for scan: (yes — small latency / no — scan async after delivery)

- User can report a message: (yes — from §3B trust & safety / no)

- Admin can read messages: (yes — for moderation / no — only if not E2EE)

Spam & abuse in messaging:

- Limit messages to unknown users: (yes — message request required / no)

- Rate limit messages per conversation: (yes — from §16 / no)

- Blocked user cannot send messages: (yes)

- Existing conversation hidden: (yes / no — archived)

- Blocked user not informed they are blocked: (confirmed — silent block)

§35 — NOTIFICATIONS & ALERTS SYSTEM

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No — every app needs a notification system.

[PURPOSE]     → Define the notification architecture — types,

templates, channels, delivery, user preferences,

alert rules, escalation, and digest.

§09 defines the real-time WebSocket transport.

§12 defines the email and SMS providers.

This section defines the notification SYSTEM on

top of those — the rules, templates, routing,

and preference management that make notifications

useful rather than annoying.

Layer 1 references: §09 Real-time (WebSocket delivery),

§12 Integrations (email/SMS/push providers),

§13 Async (notification job queue),

§28 Analytics (notification engagement tracking)

1. NOTIFICATION TAXONOMY

Notification categories:

- Transactional: (triggered by user action — order confirmed, password reset, receipt)

- Alerting: (threshold crossed — low balance, error rate spike, SLA breach)

- Social: (someone interacted with you — from §3B — new follower, comment, mention)

- System: (platform announcements — maintenance, new feature, policy change)

- Digest: (batched summary — weekly report, daily activity summary)

For each notification type in your app, declare:

- Category: ___

- Trigger event: ___

- Recipient: (the acting user / the affected user / admins / all users)

- Default channels: (in-app / email / push / SMS / Slack)

- User can opt out: (yes / no — transactional cannot be opted out)

- Priority: (P1 urgent / P2 important / P3 informational)

2. NOTIFICATION TEMPLATES

Template system:

- Templates stored in: (DB — editable without deploy / code / CMS)

- Template engine: (Handlebars / Liquid / Mjml for email / custom)

- Variables per template: (declared schema — e.g. {{user.name}}, {{order.id}})

- Preview before send: (yes — admin can preview rendered template / no)

- Version history: (yes — rollback to previous template / no)

Per-channel templates (each notification needs one per channel):

- In-app: (title — max 60 chars / body — max 120 chars / icon / action URL)

- Email: (subject / HTML body with responsive layout / plain text fallback)

- Push: (title / body / icon / deep link — from M7)

- SMS: (plain text — max 160 chars / no HTML)

- Slack: (Block Kit message with action buttons)

Localization:

- Templates localized per language: (yes — from §31 i18n / no — English only)

- Fallback language: (English)

3. NOTIFICATION CHANNELS & ROUTING

Channel priority order (for same notification):

1. In-app (always — if user is online)

2. Push (if user is on mobile and not viewing app)

3. Email (if user has not acknowledged in ___ minutes)

4. SMS (P1 only — urgent / never for informational)

Channel selection logic:

- User online (WebSocket connected): → in-app only (do not also push)

- User offline > ___ minutes: → push + email

- User has push disabled: → email fallback

- SMS: (only for P1 / user has verified phone / user opted in)

Third-party channel integrations:

- Slack: (yes — user connects Slack workspace / no)

- Microsoft Teams: (yes / no)

- Webhook: (yes — from §36 Webhooks / no)

- PagerDuty: (yes — for P1 system alerts / no)

4. USER NOTIFICATION PREFERENCES

Preference granularity:

- Per notification type + per channel: (yes — full granularity / no)

- Example: user can turn off "new comment" via email but keep in-app

Preference defaults:

- All notifications on by default: (yes — opt-out model / no — opt-in model)

- Transactional always on: (yes — cannot be disabled)

Quiet hours (Do Not Disturb):

- User sets quiet hours: (yes — e.g. 10pm–8am / no)

- Timezone respected: (yes — user's local timezone / UTC)

- During quiet hours: (queue and deliver after / suppress and discard)

- Emergency override: (P1 alerts bypass quiet hours / no exceptions)

Notification frequency controls:

- Maximum notifications per day per category: ___

- Batching: (group multiple low-priority notifications into one)

- Batching window: ___ minutes

Unsubscribe:

- One-click unsubscribe in email footer: (yes — required by CAN-SPAM / GDPR)

- Unsubscribe manages preference in DB: (yes — survives re-login)

- Global unsubscribe (all non-transactional): (yes)

5. ALERT RULES ENGINE

(For apps where users define their own alert conditions)

(Skip if your app only has system-defined notifications)

User-defined alert types:

- [ ] Metric threshold (e.g. "alert me when revenue drops below $X")

- [ ] Event-based (e.g. "alert me when a new user signs up")

- [ ] Anomaly detection (e.g. "alert me when usage is unusually high")

- [ ] Scheduled check (e.g. "alert me every Monday with last week's stats")

Alert rule model:

AlertRule {

id, user_id, name,

trigger_type: 'threshold' | 'event' | 'anomaly' | 'schedule',

condition: { metric, operator, value },  // e.g. revenue < 1000

evaluation_frequency: '5min' | '1hour' | 'daily',

channels: [channel],

is_active,

last_triggered_at,

cooldown_minutes   // prevent alert spam

}

Alert evaluation:

- Run rules on schedule: (yes — from §13 job scheduler)

- Evaluation frequency options: (real-time / every 5 min / hourly / daily)

- Alert cooldown: (do not re-alert for same condition within ___ minutes)

- Alert recovery notification: (yes — "condition resolved" / no)

Alert history:

- Log every alert fired: (yes — with condition snapshot at fire time)

- User can view alert history: (yes / no)

- Alert mute: (yes — snooze for ___ hours / no)

6. ESCALATION POLICY

(For system/ops alerts — not user notifications)

(Aligns with §27 Observability alerting)

Escalation levels:

- Level 1: notify primary on-call via push + Slack

- Level 2: if not acknowledged in ___ minutes → notify secondary on-call

- Level 3: if not acknowledged in ___ minutes → notify team lead via SMS + call

Escalation tool: (PagerDuty / OpsGenie / VictorOps / custom rotation)

On-call rotation:

- Rotation schedule: (weekly / daily / follow-the-sun)

- Override: (manual override for holidays / out-of-office)

Acknowledgement:

- Alert must be acknowledged within ___ minutes

- Acknowledge via: (Slack button / PagerDuty / in-app)

- Auto-resolve if condition clears: (yes / no)

Post-incident:

- Notification sent when alert resolves: (yes / no)

- Incident linked to alert: (yes — from §27 incident management / no)

7. DIGEST & BATCH DELIVERY

Digest types:

- Daily activity summary: (yes / no)

- Weekly report email: (yes / no)

- Batched social notifications: (X new likes / followers in last hour)

- Missed notifications while offline: (delivered as digest on next login)

Digest generation:

- Trigger: (scheduled cron — daily at ___ / weekly on ___ / on login after offline period)

- Content: (top N notifications from category / full list / count summary)

- Personalized: (yes — order by relevance / no — chronological)

- Empty digest suppressed: (yes — do not send if nothing to report / no)

Digest email format:

- Sections per notification category

- Preview of top items per section

- "View all" link to in-app notification center

- Unsubscribe from digest (not from all notifications)

8. IN-APP NOTIFICATION CENTER

Notification center UI:

- Bell icon with unread badge: (yes)

- Dropdown panel: (yes — last N notifications)

- Full notification page: (yes — paginated history / no)

- Filter by category: (yes / no)

- Mark all as read: (yes)

- Delete individual notification: (yes / no)

Notification history retention:

- In-app: keep for ___ days

- After expiry: (delete / archive / compress)

Real-time updates:

- New notification appears in center without page refresh: (yes — WebSocket push / no)

- Badge count updates in real-time: (yes / no)

CONSISTENCY VALIDATION

[ ] All notification types declared with trigger + recipient + channels

[ ] Transactional notifications cannot be opted out

[ ] One-click unsubscribe in all marketing/digest emails (CAN-SPAM)

[ ] Quiet hours respected for non-urgent notifications

[ ] P1 alerts bypass quiet hours

[ ] Channel routing avoids duplicate delivery (in-app if online → no push)

[ ] Alert cooldown prevents notification spam

[ ] Digest suppressed when empty

[ ] In-app notification center updates in real-time

[ ] Templates versioned and previewable

§36 — BILLING & SUBSCRIPTION MANAGEMENT

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → Skip if: completely free app with no paid plans.

[PURPOSE]     → Define the subscription plan model, upgrade/downgrade

flows, billing portal, invoicing, dunning, trial

management, and usage-based billing.

This section covers SaaS subscription billing.

Physical product subscriptions are in §3A.

This is the section that makes or loses you revenue —

bad dunning alone can cost 10–20% of MRR.

Layer 1 references: §01 Monetization model,

§06 Auth (plan-based feature access),

§12 Integrations (Stripe / payment provider),

§19 Privacy (billing data = PII),

§20 Compliance (PCI DSS, VAT, revenue recognition)

1. PLAN ARCHITECTURE

Billing model (from §01 — confirm here):

- [ ] Flat-rate subscription (same price regardless of usage)

- [ ] Per-seat (price × number of users)

- [ ] Usage-based / metered (pay for what you use)

- [ ] Hybrid (base fee + usage overage)

- [ ] Tiered (price per unit decreases at higher volumes)

Plan tiers (define all):

| Plan      | Price/mo | Price/yr | Seats | Key limits     |

|-----------|----------|----------|-------|----------------|

| Free      | $0       | $0       | ___   | ___            |

| Starter   | $___     | $___     | ___   | ___            |

| Pro       | $___     | $___     | ___   | ___            |

| Enterprise| Custom   | Custom   | ___   | ___            |

Annual discount: ___% (typically 15–20%)

Currency: ___ (from §3A multi-currency if applicable)

Feature gates per plan:

- Map every feature to the minimum plan required

- Stored as: (feature flags per plan / plan object with feature list / per-feature plan check)

- Enforcement: (middleware checks plan on every request / client-side only — insecure)

- Invariant: Never enforce plan limits on the client only. Always validate server-side.

2. TRIAL MANAGEMENT

Trial type:

- Free trial (no card required): (yes — lower conversion but lower friction)

- Credit card trial (card required upfront): (yes — higher conversion, fewer tire-kickers)

- Freemium (free tier forever — limited features): (yes — from §01)

- Your choice: ___

Trial configuration:

- Duration: ___ days

- Plan during trial: (full Pro / limited trial tier / specific feature set)

- Trial extension: (yes — admin can extend / no)

- One trial per account: (yes — enforce by email / no)

Trial expiry flow:

- T-7 days: email "Your trial ends in 7 days"

- T-3 days: email "Your trial ends in 3 days"

- T-1 day: email "Your trial ends tomorrow"

- T-0 (expiry):

- Credit card on file: → auto-convert to paid plan

- No card on file: → downgrade to free / block access

- User notification: in-app banner + email

Post-trial behavior:

- Data preserved on expiry: (yes — all data kept / partial — kept N days then deleted)

- Grace period: ___ days to add payment before data deletion warning

3. PLAN CHANGES (UPGRADE / DOWNGRADE)

Upgrade (moving to higher plan):

- Effective: (immediately)

- Proration: (yes — credit remaining days on current plan / no — charge full new price)

- Feature access: (immediate on upgrade)

- Receipt: (send upgrade confirmation email with new amount)

Downgrade (moving to lower plan):

- Effective: (at end of current billing period — not immediate)

- Proration: (credit issued for unused days / no refund)

- Feature access on downgrade: (removed at effective date / immediate)

- Data handling: (if new plan has lower limits — warn user before downgrade takes effect)

- Warning: "You have X items that exceed the Free plan limit of Y. These will become read-only."

Seat changes (per-seat plans):

- Add seat: (immediate charge — prorated for remaining period)

- Remove seat: (effective at next billing date / immediate with credit)

- Seat assignment: (admin assigns seats to specific users / any user on plan)

- Seat overage: (hard block — cannot add user without adding seat / soft limit with warning)

4. BILLING PORTAL & PAYMENT MANAGEMENT

Self-serve billing portal:

- Use Stripe Billing Portal: (yes — fastest / no — custom UI)

- Accessible from: (settings → billing)

Portal features:

- [ ] View current plan + next billing date + amount

- [ ] Upgrade / downgrade plan

- [ ] Add / remove seats

- [ ] Update payment method

- [ ] Download invoices (PDF)

- [ ] View billing history

- [ ] Cancel subscription

- [ ] Apply coupon / promo code

Payment methods supported:

- [ ] Credit / debit card (via Stripe — never store raw card data)

- [ ] ACH bank transfer (US B2B — lower fees)

- [ ] SEPA direct debit (EU)

- [ ] Wire transfer (enterprise — manual)

- [ ] Invoice (net 30/60 — enterprise)

Multiple payment methods:

- Save multiple cards: (yes — user selects default / no — one at a time)

- Fallback card: (yes — if primary fails, try backup / no)

5. INVOICING

Invoice generation:

- Auto-generated by: (Stripe / custom / both)

- VAT/GST displayed: (yes — per §3A tax architecture / no)

- Tax ID on invoice: (yes / no)

- Emailed automatically on payment: (yes / no)

- PO number: (yes — customer provides PO / no)

Revenue recognition (if applicable):

- Deferred revenue tracked: (yes / no)

6. DUNNING (FAILED PAYMENT RECOVERY)

Dunning is the process of recovering failed subscription payments.

It is one of the highest-ROI investments in subscription billing.

Retry schedule:

- Day 0: payment fails → immediate retry (sometimes transient)

- Day 3: retry

- Day 7: retry

- Day 14: retry + escalate to SMS if available

- Day 21: final retry

- Day 28: subscription cancelled / access removed

Customer communication per retry:

- Day 0: email "Payment failed — please update your card"

- Day 7: email "Action required — your account will be suspended"

- Day 21: email "Final notice — subscription cancels in 7 days"

- In-app: banner on every page after first failure

Smart retries (Stripe Radar / Intelligent Retries):

- Retry when card issuer signals higher success probability: (yes / no)

- Use Stripe's smart retry timing: (yes — recommended / no — fixed schedule)

Account access during dunning:

- Grace period: ___ days of full access after first failure

- After grace period: (read-only / restricted features / full access until cancelled)

- Never show confusing "payment failed" state to user mid-session: (confirm)

Card updater:

- Automatic card update (Stripe Account Updater): (yes — updates expired cards automatically / no)

- Reduces involuntary churn significantly

7. USAGE-BASED BILLING

(Skip if flat-rate only)

| Metric          | Unit    | Free limit | Paid limit | Overage price |

|-----------------|---------|------------|------------|---------------|

| API calls       | per call| 1,000/mo   | 100,000/mo | $0.001/call   |

| Storage         | GB      | 1 GB       | 100 GB     | $0.10/GB      |

| [your metrics]  | ___     | ___        | ___        | ___           |

Usage tracking:

- Count usage events: (in DB / Redis counters / Stripe Meters)

- Granularity: (per request / per day / per month)

- Usage stored: (per user / per workspace / per API key)

Overage handling:

- Hard limit: (block usage when limit reached — user must upgrade)

- Soft limit: (allow overage — charge at end of period)

- Warning threshold: (alert user at 80% of limit)

- Overage notification: (email + in-app when approaching limit)

Usage reporting to user:

- Usage dashboard: (current period usage vs limit — progress bar)

- Historical usage graph: (last 3 / 6 / 12 months)

- Usage by team member: (yes — who is using what / no)

8. CANCELLATION FLOW

Cancellation UX:

- Self-serve cancellation: (yes — required / no — contact support only — friction, bad UX)

- Cancellation location: (settings → billing → cancel)

- Effective date: (end of current billing period — user keeps access until then)

Cancellation save flow (reduce churn):

Step 1: Ask reason (too expensive / missing feature / not using / competitor)

Step 2: Based on reason:

- Too expensive → offer discount or pause

- Missing feature → show roadmap item / offer workaround

- Not using → offer pause subscription

- Competitor → offer case study or demo

Step 3: If user still cancels → confirm cancellation

Pause subscription (alternative to cancel):

- Pause available: (yes — user pays nothing for ___ months max / no)

- Data preserved during pause: (yes)

- Resume: (user-initiated / auto-resume after pause period)

Post-cancellation:

- Confirmation email: (yes — with data export offer and resubscribe link)

- Data export offered: (yes — at cancellation / no)

- Win-back email: (yes — at ___ days post-cancel / no)

- Data deletion: (after ___ days post-cancel per §29)

CONSISTENCY VALIDATION

[ ] Plan feature gates enforced server-side (never client-only)

[ ] Trial expiry emails scheduled at T-7, T-3, T-1, T-0

[ ] Downgrade warns user about data/limit impact before effective

[ ] Dunning retry schedule defined with customer comms per step

[ ] Smart retries enabled (Stripe Intelligent Retries)

[ ] Invoice includes tax breakdown and complies with §3A tax model

[ ] Usage limits tracked server-side with warning at 80%

[ ] Cancellation is self-serve (legal requirement in some markets)

[ ] Data retention post-cancellation aligns with §29

[ ] PCI scope maintained — no raw card data (aligns with §3D if applicable)

§37 — ADMIN PANEL & INTERNAL TOOLS

[TRACK]       → Both

[CONDITIONAL] → No — every SaaS app needs an admin panel.

[PURPOSE]     → Define the internal admin interface that lets your

team manage users, debug issues, configure the

platform, and support customers without needing

direct database access.

Admin panels are the most under-architected part

of most SaaS apps. Built badly, they become a

security liability. Built well, they make your

ops team 10x faster.

Layer 1 references: §06 Auth (admin roles),

§18 Security (admin access controls),

§25 Security Hardening (admin threat model),

§27 Observability (system health in admin),

§28 Analytics (product metrics in admin)

1. ADMIN ARCHITECTURE

Admin access model:

- Separate subdomain: (admin.yourapp.com — recommended / /admin path)

- Separate deployment: (yes — isolated admin app / no — same app, role-gated routes)

- IP allowlist: (yes — only company IPs / no)

- MFA required for admin: (yes — always — no exceptions)

- Session timeout: ___ minutes (shorter than user session)

Admin roles:

- Super Admin: (full access — everything)

- Support Agent: (read user data, impersonate, no config changes)

- Billing Admin: (billing and subscription management only)

- Operations: (system health, feature flags, announcements)

- Read Only: (view everything, change nothing)

Admin audit log:

- Every admin action logged: (yes — required — who did what to whom when)

- Log stored separately from app logs: (yes — append-only)

- Aligns with §27 Observability and §3D audit trail

2. USER MANAGEMENT

User search:

- Search by: (email / name / user ID / company / IP address)

- Filter by: (plan / signup date / last active / country / status)

- Results show: (email / name / plan / created / last active / status)

User profile view:

- Account details (email, name, plan, signup date)

- Login history (last N logins with IP + device)

- Subscription and billing history

- Usage stats (from §36 usage metering)

- Activity log (key actions in the app)

- Support ticket history

- Notes (internal notes by support team — never visible to user)

User actions available to admin:

- [ ] Edit user details (name, email)

- [ ] Reset password (send reset email)

- [ ] Force logout (invalidate all sessions)

- [ ] Verify email manually

- [ ] Change plan / apply discount

- [ ] Extend trial

- [ ] Add / remove feature flags

- [ ] Suspend account (temporary — user sees maintenance message)

- [ ] Ban account (permanent — data preserved for legal)

- [ ] Delete account (GDPR request — full data deletion per §29)

- [ ] Merge duplicate accounts

- [ ] Export user data (GDPR subject access request)

Bulk actions:

- Select multiple users → apply action: (yes / no)

- Bulk actions available: (export / change plan / send email / suspend)

- Bulk action confirmation required: (yes — "are you sure?" for destructive actions)

- Bulk action limit: max ___ users per operation

3. IMPERSONATION (LOGIN AS USER)

Impersonation allows support to see exactly what a user sees.

Impersonation model:

- Admin clicks "Login as user" → gets session scoped to that user

- Impersonated session is READ-ONLY: (yes — cannot make changes on user's behalf / no)

- Impersonated session duration: max ___ minutes (auto-expire)

- Visible indicator: (yes — banner "You are viewing as [user@email.com]" — cannot be hidden)

- Exit impersonation: (clear button — returns to admin session)

Security requirements:

- Every impersonation logged: (yes — admin_id + user_id + timestamp + duration)

- User is NOT notified they were impersonated: (confirm — silent / yes — notify)

- Impersonation requires reason: (yes — dropdown: debugging / support / QA / no)

- Roles that can impersonate: (Super Admin / Support Agent / no others)

What admin CANNOT do while impersonating:

- Cannot change user's password

- Cannot make payments on user's behalf

- Cannot delete user's data

- Cannot see user's payment details

Maintenance mode:

- Status page: (statuspage.io / custom — from §27)

[ ] Admin roles enforce least privilege

§38 — WEBHOOKS & EVENT STREAMING

[TRACK]       → Full Track

[CONDITIONAL] → Skip on Fast Track unless customers explicitly

need to integrate your app with their own systems.

[PURPOSE]     → Define the outbound webhook system that lets

customers receive real-time events from your app

in their own infrastructure — plus the internal

event catalog and streaming architecture.

§13 covers internal async messaging between your

own services. This section covers the external

event delivery system your customers use.

Layer 1 references: §13 Async/Messaging (internal events),

§08 API (event schema conventions),

§18 Security (webhook signature verification),

§27 Observability (webhook delivery monitoring)

1. EVENT CATALOG

Define every event your system emits:

Event naming convention: (resource.action — e.g. user.created / order.paid / subscription.cancelled)

Core event categories and examples:

| Category      | Events                                              |

|---------------|-----------------------------------------------------|

| User          | user.created / user.updated / user.deleted          |

| Auth          | user.login / user.logout / user.password_reset      |

| Subscription  | subscription.created / subscription.upgraded / subscription.cancelled / subscription.payment_failed |

| [your domain] | [list all events for your app]                      |

For each event, declare:

- Event name: ___

- Trigger: (what action causes this event)

- Payload fields: (what data is in the event body)

- Frequency: (per user action / system-generated / scheduled)

- Sensitive data included: (yes — PII — list fields / no)

Event schema standard:

{

id: "evt_unique_id",

type: "user.created",

created_at: "ISO8601 timestamp",

api_version: "2024-01-01",

data: {

object: { ... resource fields ... }

},

metadata: { ... optional context ... }

}

Event versioning:

- API version in every event: (yes — customers can pin to version)

- Breaking change policy: (new api_version, old version maintained for ___ months)

- Invariant: Never silently change the schema of an existing event. Always version.

2. WEBHOOK ENDPOINT MANAGEMENT

Customer webhook registration:

- Via UI: (settings → webhooks → add endpoint)

- Via API: (POST /webhooks — for programmatic setup)

- Fields per endpoint: (URL / event types to subscribe / description / active status)

- Max endpoints per account: ___

- HTTPS required: (yes — reject HTTP webhook URLs — invariant)

Event type subscription:

- Subscribe to all events: (yes — wildcard / no — must specify each type)

- Subscribe per event category: (yes — e.g. all subscription.* events)

- Subscribe per individual event: (yes)

Webhook secret:

- Auto-generated secret per endpoint: (yes — shown once at creation)

- Used to sign payloads: (yes — HMAC-SHA256 signature)

- Secret rotation: (yes — customer can rotate / generates new secret)

3. WEBHOOK DELIVERY ARCHITECTURE

Delivery model:

- At-least-once delivery: (yes — required — events may be delivered more than once)

- Exactly-once: (not guaranteed — customers must handle idempotency by event ID)

- Invariant: Customers must use event.id for idempotency. Document this clearly.

Delivery flow:

1. Internal event fires (from §13 event bus)

2. Webhook dispatcher queries: which endpoints subscribed to this event type?

3. For each endpoint: create delivery job in queue

4. Worker sends HTTP POST to endpoint URL

5. Log attempt with: timestamp / status code / response body (first 1024 chars) / latency

Timeout:

- Request timeout: ___ seconds (good: 10–30 seconds)

- Customer endpoint must respond quickly: (document: respond 2xx immediately, process async)

Success:

- 2xx response = delivered

- Anything else = failure → retry

Retry strategy:

- Retry on: (non-2xx / timeout / connection error)

- Retry schedule: (immediate / 1min / 5min / 30min / 2hr / 8hr / 24hr)

- Max retries: ___ (after which: mark as failed, stop retrying)

- Total retry window: ___ hours / days

4. WEBHOOK SECURITY

Payload signing:

- Algorithm: HMAC-SHA256

- Signed value: raw request body (not parsed — byte-exact)

- Signature header: Webhook-Signature or X-Signature-256

- Timestamp included in signature: (yes — prevents replay attacks)

- Signature format: "t=timestamp,v1=signature"

Customer verification (document for customers):

1. Extract timestamp from signature header

2. Reject if timestamp is > 5 minutes old (replay protection)

3. Compute HMAC: HMAC-SHA256(secret, "{timestamp}.{body}")

4. Compare with provided signature (constant-time comparison)

IP allowlist (optional for customer):

- Publish your webhook sender IPs: (yes — customers can restrict to your IPs / no)

- IP range stable: (yes — publish static IPs / no — do not promise)

What never goes in webhook payload:

- Full card numbers or CVV

- Passwords or auth tokens

- Full PII unless explicitly required (use IDs + fetch via API)

5. WEBHOOK LOGS & DEBUGGING

Delivery log per webhook attempt:

- Event ID + type

- Endpoint URL

- HTTP status code received

- Response body (truncated to ___ chars)

- Latency (ms)

- Timestamp

- Attempt number (1st, 2nd retry, etc.)

- Status: (delivered / failed / pending retry)

Customer-visible log:

- Customers can view delivery history in UI: (yes — last ___ days)

- Filter by: (event type / status / date range)

- See full request and response per attempt: (yes / no)

Webhook testing tool:

- Send test event: (yes — trigger test payload to endpoint without real event / no)

- Test from UI: (yes — "Send test" button per event type)

- CLI / API test endpoint: (yes — POST /webhooks/{id}/test / no)

- Test events clearly marked: (yes — test: true in payload)

Replay:

- Resend failed event: (yes — manual replay from logs / no)

- Replay window: ___ days (after which event is expired)

- Bulk replay: (yes — replay all failed events in a time range / no)

6. WEBHOOK MONITORING & RELIABILITY

Endpoint health tracking:

- Track success rate per endpoint

- Auto-disable endpoint after ___ consecutive failures: (yes — prevents wasted retries)

- Notify customer when endpoint disabled: (yes — email / no)

- Customer must manually re-enable: (yes — after fixing their endpoint)

Platform-side alerts (from §27):

- Webhook queue depth > ___ → alert

- Delivery failure rate > ___% → alert

- Average delivery latency > ___ ms → alert

SLA:

- Delivery attempt within ___ seconds of event (p95)

- No SLA on customer endpoint response time

CONSISTENCY VALIDATION

[ ] All events in catalog have stable schema + api_version

[ ] HTTPS required on all webhook endpoints

[ ] HMAC-SHA256 signature on every delivery

[ ] Timestamp in signature prevents replay attacks

[ ] At-least-once delivery documented for customers

[ ] Event ID used for idempotency (documented)

[ ] Retry schedule defined with max attempt limit

[ ] Failed endpoint auto-disabled after N failures

[ ] Customer can view delivery logs in UI

[ ] Test event tool available

[ ] No sensitive card or auth data in payloads

[ ] Event versioning policy defined

→ Generate webhook endpoint registration (CRUD API + UI)

→ Generate webhook dispatcher (query subscribers → queue jobs)

→ Generate HMAC-SHA256 payload signer

→ Generate signature verification code sample (for docs)
